# IDWT Appendix A: Patterns in the Mathematical Structure

**Working document — not for publication as-is.**  
This appendix records every mathematical pattern found or checked in the IDWT framework, organised by topic. Sections 1–9 cover patterns that are stated, derived, or used in the main documents (Parts 1–10). Sections 10–14 cover patterns found in this document set that have not yet been placed in the main documents. Section 15 records attempts that returned null results, so those searches do not get repeated.

When a pattern from §10–14 gets incorporated into a main document, move its entry to the appropriate §1–9 section and note the location.

---

## Part I — Patterns in the documented theory

### §1. Mode index set — the 15 visible particles

The 15 physical particles selected by the co-fixed-point condition. Each carries a mode index n and a sector dimension d; mass = m_scale_d × S(n,d).

| n | Particle | Sector d | S(n,d) | Notes |
|---|----------|----------|--------|-------|
| 0 | photon γ | 2 | 0 | n=0 is universal; S(0,d)=0 for all d |
| 1 | down quark | 3 | 1 | universal ground state; S(1,d)=1 for all d |
| 3 | up quark | 4 | 15 | = S(3,4) = C(6,4) |
| 4 | strange quark | 3 | 20 | = n_s; S(4,3) = C(6,3) |
| 10 | ν₁ | 5 | 2002 | = S(3,3) in a different sense; see §5 |
| 13 | electron | 6 | 18564 | unit reference |
| 15 | ν₂ | 5 | 11628 | |
| 20 | charm quark | 4 | 8855 | = S(4,3) index, d=4 sector |
| 22 | ν₃ | 5 | 65780 | |
| 23 | tau lepton | 10 | 64512240 | |
| 35 | muon | 6 | 3838380 | |
| 72 | top quark | 4 | 1215450 | |
| 76 | W boson | 2 | 2926 | |
| 81 | Z boson | 2 | 3321 | |
| 95 | Higgs | 2 | 4560 | |

The selection mechanism is documented in Part 7: the mode-sector pair (n,d) must be a member of Σ_pairs — the co-fixed-point set produced by the generation tower (the hockey-stick recursion from seeds {n_d=1, n_u=3} and their composite n_s=4). Stability of the pair is established by the l-parity and dephasing mechanisms (Part 7 §1.2); membership requires both the correct mode index and the correct sector.

### §2. Mode index set — unselected candidates

Modes generated by the hockey-stick recursion that are not co-fixed-points (fail the Σ_pairs membership condition), or are never generated. Documented in Part 7 §1 and idwt.py Step 29.

**d=3 modes that are not co-fixed-points:**
- n=2 (level N=1, odd): l-parity disconnected from the seeds (Part 7 §1.2) — a broad colour-triplet excitation, not a stable particle.
- n=3 (level N=2, even): dephases in the infinite-dimensional coupled system — not stable.
- n=5 and above: not co-fixed-points; absent as stable states.

Note: n=4 (= n_s) is a co-fixed-point (strange quark), selected by the co-fixed-point condition.

**The d=2 gap (n=1 through n=75):**  
No Vandermonde combination of any fermion (n,d) pair produces a d=2 mode index below 76. The fermion Vandermonde values g = n+d−1 are {3, 6, 6, 14, 18, 19, 23, 26, 32, 40, 75} — all occupied as mode indices in their own sectors. The gap is the mass range where matter lives in its own sectors; d=2 has no eigenmode there.

### §3. The sector set D = {2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10}

**What it is.** Six geometric strata of Ξ₁₀, each hosting one particle family. Documented in Part 1 §3 and the Euler characteristic chain article.

**The six dimensions as CP^k (even-d sectors) and S^k (odd-d sectors):**
- d=2: CP¹ (isometry U(1))
- d=3: S³ (isometry SO(4))
- d=4: CP² (isometry SU(3))
- d=5: S⁵ (isometry SO(6) ≅ SU(4))
- d=6: CP³ (isometry SU(4))
- d=10: CP⁵ (isometry SU(6))

**Why d=7, 8, 9 are absent.** The coupling fixed-point equation for g₈₈ has no solution (d=8 gap). The terminal sector is set by Gegenbauer criticality: b_{k₀}(d) = ½ exactly at d = 2(N_c+2) = 10 (Theorem T5, Part 1 §4b). The sequence is consecutive from d=2 through d=6, then jumps to d=10.

**Jump from d=6 to d=10:**  d=10 − d=6 = 4 = n_s. The final active sector is 4 steps above d=6 in dimension, spanning the inactive d=7,8,9 coordinates (which are absent not for lack of dimension but for lack of a valid coupling fixed point or Gegenbauer-critical endpoint at those values of d).

**Sum of occupied dimensions:** 2+3+4+5+6+10 = 30 = (n_s+1) × N_f = 5 × 6. (Not assigned structural meaning yet; noted for reference.)

**Products within the set:** 2×3 = 6 ∈ D, 2×5 = 10 ∈ D. Products 3×4=12 and 2×6=12 are not in D. The two products that land in D both involve d=2.

**Rule B criticality inequality — direction correction of record (2026-06-10).** Part 9 T3 Rule B stated $b_{k_0}(d)\geq\tfrac12$ iff $4k_0\leq(d-2)^2$. The direction is reversed. With $b_{k_0}(d)=\sqrt{k_0(k_0+d-1)}/(2k_0+d-2)$ and positive denominators, $b_{k_0}-\tfrac12$ has the sign of $4k_0(k_0+d-1)-(2k_0+d-2)^2 = -d^2+4d+60 = -(d-10)(d+6)$ at $k_0=16$. Hence $b_{k_0}\geq\tfrac12 \Leftrightarrow (d-2)^2\leq 4k_0 \Leftrightarrow d\leq 10$, and $b_{k_0}<\tfrac12$ (subcritical) $\Leftrightarrow d\geq 11$ — matching the §3/T3 table (d=2…6 supercritical, d=10 critical, d≥11 excluded) and the equality endpoint $4k_0=(d-2)^2$ used in T5/T15a. The mis-stated form would instead admit $d\geq10$ and exclude $d=2$…$9$, contradicting the table. Part 9 T3 Rule B corrected to $b_{k_0}\geq\tfrac12$ iff $(d-2)^2\leq 4k_0$ (equivalently $d\leq 2+2\sqrt{k_0}$); the equality endpoint and all downstream logic were already correct. Verified algebraically (factor $-(d-10)(d+6)$) and numerically ($b(2)=0.5154$, $b(10)=0.5000$, $b(11)=0.4975$). The same script confirms the full sector selection (Rule A χ-gap at $\chi=N_c+2=5$ → $d=8$; odd total spaces routing over a non-fixed-point base → $d=7,9$; Rule B → $d\geq11$) reproduces the pass-set exactly $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$; the routing-exhaustiveness step of Rule A stays the open 🔶 item (Part 6).

**Rule A exhaustiveness — closure candidate (2026-06-12).** The open Rule A lemma (Part 6) asked for a proof that Hopf-universality routing requires a fixed-point base. The bottom-up form is not provable as posed: a transported *value* for $g_{77}$ is always writable, and once $g_{66}$ exists every coupling-consistency test the kernel supplies is satisfied by $g_{77}=w^2 g_{66}$ with $w^2=g_{33}/g_{22}$ (the would-be value $0.00732$ is even seed-expressible). The closure instead runs top-down. (i) **Induced-base lemma (candidate ✅):** the complex Hopf fiber is a unit great circle with inner-product profile $\cos t$ in every $S^{2k+1}$ (⭐), and $L^2(S^{2k+1})=\bigoplus_m L^2(\mathbb{CP}^k,\mathcal{O}(m))$ with $m{=}0$ block exactly $L^2(\mathbb{CP}^k)$ (⭐); an active total space therefore carries the base sector problem on its $S^1$-invariant block, and T2 rank-1 (one coupling per sector pair) forces the induced coupling to coincide with the base's own. Verified exactly at both real pairs with a single reduction constant: $g_{22}/g_{33}=g_{44}/g_{55}=34.1349\ldots$ (machine-exact; the equality is T9a). Read bottom-up this *derives* T9b as a consistency relation between active pairs — universality is necessary, never an activation mechanism. (ii) **d=9 (candidate ✅):** an active $S^9$ induces a $d{=}8$ coupling on its invariant block, but $d{=}8$ has no admissible value — no seed residency, no back-reaction source, no fixed point (T15b: the $g_{88}$ equation has no solution), $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5$ the unique seed-unmatched $\chi$ — so the induced coupling would be the one constant outside the seed-closed coupling algebra (Part 2 §9 completeness). (iii) **d=7 — the μ–τ/Rule-B squeeze (candidate ✅, the new result):** at the T3 stage (sector set logically prior to mode occupancy, Part 1 §3a before §3b; Appendix §5), the kernel-visible data of base $d{=}6$ and base $d{=}10$ are identical — full coupling rows equal exactly ($v_6=v_{10}=1/2$, T9c; rank-1 makes the entire rows equal), both $\chi$ seed-matched ($\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)=n_s$, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^5)=N_f$), same fiber. So any activation route for $S^7$ over $\mathbb{CP}^3$ activates $S^{11}$ over $\mathbb{CP}^5$ with the same output ($g_{11,11}=g_{77}$). Both readings of that output are excluded: as an active sector, $d{=}11$ is Gegenbauer-subcritical ($b_{k_0}(11)=0.4975<\tfrac12$, ⭐) and cannot host the discrete eigenmodes activity requires; as a bare coupling row, $v_{11}\neq0$ links every sector mode to the $d{=}11$ free continuum (subcritical ⟹ scattering states only, no gap), giving e, u, and the neutrinos generic nonzero widths against absolute stability (Part 7 §1.2 stability equivalence; $\tau_e>6.6\times10^{28}$ yr). Hence no activation route for $d{=}7$ exists. The squeeze does not over-fire: $(6,10)$ is the only $v$-degenerate sector pair, so $d{=}3$ and $d{=}5$ activations (unique base rows) are untouched — Rule A's seal is the *conjunction* of T9c (terminal coupling degeneracy) and Rule B (criticality endpoint one step above the last base). Honest residuals: the route-input classification (activation routes see only T3-stage kernel data) is P1–P4 minimality plus the documented logical ordering — flagged as the premise a referee must grant; the induced-coupling positivity/blockwise-self-consistency step of (i) is a functional-analytic sketch verified exactly at the two real pairs, not yet a written functional; the tau back-reaction contamination test of an active $d{=}7$ is inconclusive at T10b order ($\sim1.7\times10^{-5}$ relative vs PDG $5.1\times10^{-5}$ — 0.34σ), so the empirical backstop has no power and the exclusion rests on the squeeze. Status upgrade of Rule A in T3/Part 1/Part 6 awaits Fedge's adversarial read; nothing in the Parts has been changed by this entry.

**Adversarial-read correction to the above (2026-06-12, same day, prompted by Fedge).** The squeeze's premise "criticality is the only asymmetry between the $d{=}6$ and $d{=}10$ bases" is an overclaim, and item (iii) is downgraded from candidate ✅ to **partial result, Rule A $d{=}7$ stays 🔶**. The coupling rows are exactly equal and both $\chi$'s are seed-matched, but the $\chi$ *values* differ (4 vs 6) and are integer-layer data, visible at sector-set-determination time. T15b's own consecutive $\chi$-run $\{N_c{-}1,N_c,N_c{+}1\}=\{2,3,4\}$ supplies a separating predicate with documented standing: an activation route keyed on "base $\chi$ in the consecutive run" is instantiated by both real activations ($d{=}3$ over $\chi{=}2$, $d{=}5$ over $\chi{=}3$), fires at $d{=}7$ (over $\chi{=}4$), and is silent at $d{=}11$ ($\chi{=}6$ lies past the gap) — evading the squeeze. With only two real activation instances the activation law is underdetermined: "base coupling solves a kernel equation" fits both instances and excludes $d{=}7$; "base $\chi$ in the consecutive run" fits both and admits it; nothing at the integer layer arbitrates, and the empirical discriminators lack power (the $\tau$ back-reaction test above; mass ratios are coupling-free and insensitive). What survives the correction: the $d{=}9$ closure (independent of the squeeze; the $\chi$-run route does not fire there, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5\notin$ run — consistent); the T9b direction-of-implication result (universality as consistency relation, not activation mechanism); and the squeeze as a partial theorem excluding every activation route that is symmetric in the $6/10$ base data (rows, $\chi$-set membership, fiber). The arbitration between the two surviving route-predicates is a dynamical question: it requires the explicit vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5), under which activation becomes solvability of an equation rather than a predicate fitted to two instances.

**Second adversarial round and propagation (2026-06-12, same day, Fedge-authorized).** Stress-testing what survived the first correction. (1) *Quotient caveat on the induced-base lemma:* the Hopf base is a quotient $S^{2k+1}/S^1$, not a coordinate subspace, while the sector nesting $\Xi_d\subset\Xi_{d'}$ is coordinate-plane containment — so the invariant block is a $\mathbb{CP}^k$-*symmetric* kernel self-consistency problem, not literally the $\Xi_{2k}$ coordinate-plane sector, and the constant equality $g_{22}/g_{33}=g_{44}/g_{55}$ is *consistent with* the induced-base reading rather than an independent verification of it (it is T9a restated). (2) *d=9 survives the caveat:* T15b's no-solution reason ($\chi=5$ seed-unmatched) applies to the equation *form*, hence to the induced $\mathbb{CP}^4$-symmetric problem regardless of the quotient/subspace distinction — and the $\chi$-run predicate does not fire at $d=9$ ($\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5\notin$ run), so the $d=9$ exclusion is route-independent. The principled asymmetry stands: $d=9$ has a genuine obstruction, $d=7$ does not, which is why only $d=7$ needs the (leaky) squeeze. (3) *Stability-leg caveat:* the $(d',11)$ kernel term has support on coordinates $\leq d'$, so only $d=11$ continuum slices with structure confined to shared coordinates couple; such slices exist down to zero energy (subcritical ⟹ no well, scattering threshold at the bottom), so phase space stays open and the generic-width conclusion holds. (4) *New corroborating constraint (🔶, conditional):* an active $d=7$ would extend the matter quartet to five sectors, breaking the count $2n_s-4=n_s$ that independently certifies $n_s=4$ (§19 quartet derivation; the requirement itself is 🔵-motivated, so this corroborates rather than proves). (5) *d=5 activation under the consistency reading of T9b:* shifts to the quartet/family structure (the quartet derivation already places $d=5$ among the matter sectors independently of coupling construction); the routing rule (T9b corollary) is about mode routing and is unaffected. Propagated with Rule A kept 🔶 throughout: Part 9 T3 (Rule A bullets, open item, Jacobi-table notes, distinct-types paragraph), Part 1 §3a (Rule A paragraph, inactive-dimension remark, the d=7 exclusion paragraph), Part 6 (Rule A entry rewritten around the actual residual), `files/idwt.py` STEP 2 comment. The promised-and-unprovable "routing requires a fixed-point base" lemma no longer appears as an open item anywhere; the open item is the activation-law arbitration via the vacuum-stability functional.

**Mean-field non-selectivity of the Rule A arbiter; the "Part 2 §5 functional" misdirection corrected (2026-06-12, `files/idwt.py` STEP 76).** The preceding addenda left the $d=7$ arbitration to "the explicit vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5)," under which activation would become solvability of an equation. The nonlinear-EoM object that Part 2 §5 would have to supply is the Part 4 §3.10 condensate mean-field self-consistency $\lambda_d = g_{dd}\langle r^2\rangle_d/d$ with the $d$-dimensional isotropic-oscillator ground state $\langle r^2\rangle_d = d/(2\sqrt{\lambda_d})$. Substituting, the dimension cancels exactly: $2\lambda_d^{3/2}=g_{dd}$ (verified, max self-consistency residual over the active set $7\times10^{-15}$). This equation is solvable for any $g_{dd}>0$ in any dimension — it is **non-selective in $d$**. Feeding the inactive band a formal coupling (the Hopf continuation $g_{77}=g_{55}g_{66}/g_{44}=0.00732$) solves it just as well; it is not rejected. The only cross-sector coupling-fixer available in the mean field, Hopf universality $v_3/v_2=v_5/v_4$, *writes* that same $g_{77}$ rather than forbidding it (it fixes the scale of a sector already required active but lacking its own fixed point — $d=5$, $\chi(S^5)=0$ — and is not an activation mechanism, the T9b reading). The single mean-field-adjacent asymmetry is the quartet *count* (an active $d=7$ extends the matter quartet to five sectors, breaking $2n_s-4=n_s$), which is itself 🔵 and corroborates rather than proves. **Conclusion:** no mean-field functional arbitrates $d=7$; Part 2 §5 contains no such object and the "minima at $\{1,4\}$" reading there is separately null (§15, kernel positivity). The genuine arbiter is the coupled $(\Psi_\infty,\{M_d\})$ fixed point — concretely **Part 6 Open Theorem A**, the ground-state directional-covariance operator $\hat C$ whose spectral plateaux should fall at exactly $d\in D$ (and Part 1 §1's dependency note, where $D$ is to emerge from the joint field–geometry fixed point when $V_d$ is derived from the action, MC-2). The cross-references citing "the vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5)" as the arbiter (Part 1 §3a, Part 6, Part 9 T3) were repointed to Open Theorem A. Rule A stays 🔶: the result relocates the open object to its correct home and shows mean field cannot close it, but does not itself close $d=7$.

**Bott mod-8 corroborating observation (2026-06-09).** The even active sectors {2,4,6,10} have d mod 8 = {2,4,6,2}. The d=10 row is identical in spinor type to the d=2 row (Weyl ✓, Majorana ✓, Majorana-Weyl ✓; Part 8 §2.1 table). The even chain therefore terminates at the first even d whose Clifford algebra class returns to the d=2 class under Bott periodicity. The gap at d=8 falls in class 0 (d mod 8 = 0), the one class not present in the active chain. This is a fourth independent convergence on d=10 as the terminal sector, alongside the Hopf chain, Gegenbauer b_{k₀}=½ (T5), and the φ(χ)≤2 cyclotomic criterion (Appendix §15 F1-ext). Treat as a corroborating observation, not a derivation: the Bott period is 8 for any sequence of Clifford algebras, so the return is automatic; the non-trivial content is only that the even chain stops exactly at the return point rather than extending past it.

### §4. Euler characteristics and sector-mode index correlations

The Euler characteristic chain (Theorem T15, Part 9):

χ(CP^k) = k + 1

| Space | χ | Role in IDWT |
|-------|---|--------------|
| CP¹ | 2 | d=2 sector; number of photon polarisations |
| CP² | 3 | = N_c; number of quark colours |
| CP³ | 4 | = n_s; the strange-quark composite index |
| CP⁴ | 5 | **missing sector**; χ(CP⁴) = n_s+1 = q |
| CP⁵ | 6 | = N_f; number of quark/lepton flavours |

Mode indices expressible in N_c alone:

| Identity | Value | Theorem |
|----------|-------|---------|
| n_s = N_c + 1 | 4 | T15 |
| n_e = N_c² + N_c + 1 | 13 | T15d |
| n_ν₁ = N_c² + 1 | 10 | T15d |
| n_top = N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) | 72 | T15b |
| d_terminal = 2(N_c+2) | 10 | T15a |
| Hopf product = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 | 96 | T15c |

### §5. The Generation Tower — documented derivation

Seeds: n_down = 1 (universal ground state, S(1,d)=1 for all d) in d=3; n_s = 4 (unique solution to the muon fixed point) in d=3. Every other mode index is derived; none are postulated. Documented in Part 2 §2–4.

The co-fixed-point condition applies to the (n,d) pair. The n and d for each particle come from **two independent derivation chains**:
- **n** is derived by the generation tower operations (hockey-stick, additive, g-rule) below.
- **d** is assigned by the sector structure established in Part 1 §3: the Hopf fibration assigns particle families to sectors (quarks→d=3,4; neutrinos→d=5; charged leptons→d=6; tau→d=10; bosons→d=2) prior to and independently of the mode index derivation. There is no equation d=f(n) — the sector cannot be derived from the mode index alone (Appendix A §15), and the same tower operation (e.g. HS with d_eval=3) can produce particles in different sectors depending on which seed is used.

The table below records both derivation chains side by side. The d-source column cites which sector-structure result assigns that family to that d; it is not a derivation of d from n.

**Derivation chain — n and d with sources:**

| Particle | n derivation | n | d | d source (sector family assignment) |
|----------|-------------|---|---|--------------------------------------|
| down | universal ground state S(1,d)=1 | 1 | 3 | seed sector — the observable d=3 spacetime is the starting point |
| strange | composite n_s = n_d+n_u (T4; muon fixed-point S(4,4)=35) | 4 | 3 | seed sector |
| up | n_s − 1 | 3 | 4 | d=4 is the CP² colour sector; χ(CP²)=N_c=3; up-type quarks defined as d=4 family (Part 1 §3b, T15a) |
| ν₁ | S(n_up, 3) | 10 | 5 | d=5 is the Hopf total space S¹→S⁵→CP²; neutrinos defined as the d=5 family, Hopf partner of d=4 (Part 1 §3b, Part 2 §2) |
| ν₂ | S(n_up, 4) | 15 | 5 | same |
| ν₃ | n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ − n_up | 22 | 5 | same |
| electron | n_ν₁ + n_up | 13 | 6 | d=6=d=3⊗d=3; charged leptons defined as the d=6 family, colour-neutral by tensor-product geometry (Part 1 §3b, Part 2 §4) |
| charm | S(n_s, 3) | 20 | 4 | up-type quark family (same sector as up) |
| muon | n_charm + n_ν₂ | 35 = S(n_s,4) | 6 | charged-lepton family (same sector as electron) |
| tau | n_ν₃ + n_down | 23 | 10 | d=10 is the Gegenbauer-critical sector; tau defined as the d=10 family; b_{k₀}=½ at d=2(N_c+2)=10 (Part 1 T5) |
| top | S(n_e,2) − n_charm + 1 | 72 = N_c·n_s·N_f | 4 | up-type quark family (same sector as up and charm) |
| photon | n=0 universal S(0,d)=0 | 0 | 2 | d=2 is the EM sector CP¹; U(1)_EM isometry (Part 1 §3) |
| W | g(d_ν, n_top) = d_ν+n_top−1 | 76 | 2 | Vandermonde g-rule produces gauge-sector modes in d=2 (Part 3 §11) |
| Z | g(d_ℓ, n_W) = d_ℓ+n_W−1 | 81 | 2 | same |
| Higgs | n_Z + n_ν₂ − 1 | 95 = n_up+n_charm+n_top | 2 | same |

**The 2×2 Pascal block.** The four indices n_ν₁, n_ν₂, n_charm, n_μ form the 2×2 submatrix of the simplex table at the seed coordinates (n_up, n_s) = (3, 4):

```
           d=3       d=4
n=3:    S(3,3)=10  S(3,4)=15    (ν₁, ν₂)
n=4:    S(4,3)=20  S(4,4)=35    (charm, muon)
```

The second generation and the neutrino sector occupy one contiguous 2×2 cell in Pascal's triangle at the composite coordinates $(n_s=4, n_u=3)$.

**Muon self-referential fixed point.** n_μ = S(n_s, 4) = S(4,4) = 35 is both the eigenmode selection rule output (n_charm + n_ν₂ = 35) and the d=4 self-image of the composite. The coincidence is what confirms n_s = 4 as the composite; it is the unique solution.

### §5a. Coupling constants — derivation sequence

All six self-couplings are derived from n_s = 4, n_u = 3 in a fixed order. Each is fully determined before the next is computed. Source: Part 2 §9, Part 9 T9, T15.

| Step | Coupling | Derivation | Exact value |
|------|----------|-----------|-------------|
| 1 | g₃₃ | Kernel fixed-point at k₀ = n_s²: n_s²√(n_s+n_u)/2 | 8√7 ≈ 21.166 |
| 2 | g₄₄ | Kernel fixed-point: n_s·n_u/√(n_s+n_u) | 12/√7 ≈ 4.536 |
| 3 | g₆₆ | Composite ratio for CP³ base: 1/n_s | 1/4 |
| 4 | g₁₀,₁₀ | Shared composite coupling (μ-τ symmetry): = g₆₆ | 1/4 |
| 5 | g₂₂ | Cross-sector back-reaction fixed-point: (S(n_s,3)−n_u)² · (S(n_u,4)−S(n_u,3)) / 2 | 722.5 |
| 6 | g₅₅ | Hopf universality v₃/v₂ = v₅/v₄: g₃₃·g₄₄/g₂₂ = 96/g₂₂ | 96/722.5 ≈ 0.133 |

Cross-check: g₃₃ × g₄₄ = g₂₂ × g₅₅ = 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 exactly (Part 9 T9a, T15c).

### §5b. Sector scales — derivation sequence

All scales follow from m_e and the couplings above. The d=6 scale is the unit anchor; d=5 is derived last because it requires both m_scale_6 and m_scale_4. Source: Part 2 §10, Part 9 T11a.

| Step | Scale | Formula | Value |
|------|-------|---------|-------|
| 1 | m_scale_6 | m_e / S(n_e, 6) = m_e / 18564 | 2.753×10⁻⁵ MeV |
| 2 | m_scale_10 | = m_scale_6 (shared coupling g₁₀,₁₀ = g₆₆) | 2.753×10⁻⁵ MeV |
| 3 | m_scale_3 | m_e × √(g₃₃/g₆₆) | 4.702 MeV |
| 4 | m_scale_4 | m_scale_3 × √(g₄₄/g₃₃) / S(n_u, 4) | 0.1451 MeV |
| 5 | m_scale_2 | m_e × √(g₂₂/g₆₆) | 27.47 MeV |
| 6 | m_scale_5 | (n_u/n_s) × m_scale_6³ / m_scale_4² | 7.43×10⁻¹³ MeV |

The d=5 suppression factor (n_u/n_s) = 3/4 = 1 − g₆₆ is the complement of the lepton sector coupling: the coupling strength the charged-lepton sector retains (g₆₆) is what the neutrino sector surrenders (Part 9 T15e).

### §6. Structural constants

Constants derived from the seeds that appear across multiple derivations.

| Constant | Definition | Value | Appearances |
|----------|-----------|-------|-------------|
| k₀ | n_s² | 16 | Gegenbauer resonance site; g₃₃ factor; GTC |
| p | S(n_s,3) − n_up | 17 | Enters g₂₂ = p²q/2 as Dirac eigenstate count |
| q | S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) | 5 | Enters g₂₂; equals n_Z − n_W; equals n_s+1; equals χ(CP⁴) |
| ε | 1/(280√7) | ≈ 0.001350 | GTC per-quark correction; ε·g₃₃ = 1/35 = δ_ν₃ |
| back-reaction | 1 + 1/(n_up·n_s²·S(n_s,4)) | ≈ 1.000595 | Tau mass resummation factor |

**Multiple characterisations of k₀:**
- k₀ = n_s² = 16
- k₀ = n_e + n_up = 13 + 3 = 16
- k₀ = S(n_s,3) − S(2,3) = 20 − 4 = 16
- k₀ = n_charm − n_s = 20 − 4 = 16

**Back-reaction denominator:**  
n_up · k₀ · n_μ = 3 · 16 · 35 = **1680** = n_s · n_up · (n_s + n_up) · S(n_s,3) = 4·3·7·20. Appears as the resummation denominator for the tau mass correction.

**GTC correction:** ε · g₃₃ = [1/(280√7)] · [8√7] = 8/280 = **1/35 = 1/n_μ** exactly. The per-mode GTC shift is the reciprocal of the muon mode index.

### §7. Sector scales

Each m_scale_d is the mass unit for sector d; particle masses are m = m_scale_d × S(n,d).

| Sector | Scale | Derivation | Value (MeV) |
|--------|-------|-----------|-------------|
| d=2 | m_scale₂ = m_e √(g₂₂/g₆₆) | coupling ratio | 27.4706 |
| d=3 | m_scale₃ = m_e √(g₃₃/g₆₆) | coupling ratio | 4.7019 |
| d=4 | m_scale₄ = m_scale₃ √(g₄₄/g₃₃) / S(n_up,4) | fixed-point + up quark | 0.14510 |
| d=5 | m_scale₅ = (n_up/n_s) · m_scale₆³ / m_scale₄² | cross-sector consistency | 7.43×10⁻¹³ |
| d=6 | m_scale₆ = m_e / S(n_e,6) | electron anchor | 2.753×10⁻⁵ |
| d=10 | m_scale₁₀ = m_scale₆ | shared composite coupling g₆₆=g₁₀,₁₀=1/n_s | 2.753×10⁻⁵ |

**Key relationships:**
- m_scale₂ = m_e √(g₂₂/g₆₆); m_scale₃ = m_e √(g₃₃/g₆₆) — both scale as m_e times the square root of their coupling over the lepton coupling
- m_scale₆ = m_scale₁₀ because g₆₆ = g₁₀,₁₀ = 1/n_s (shared composite coupling); the tau-to-muon mass ratio is purely S(n_τ,10)/S(n_μ,6), not a scale difference
- m_scale₄ is the only scale set by dividing by an explicit S(n,d): the up quark is the anchor for d=4 because n_up = 3 is a seed (χ(CP²) = N_c = 3, T15), providing the first occupied mode in d=4

**Ground state vs. lightest particle:**  
m_scale_d × S(1,d) = m_scale_d (since S(1,d)=1 for all d). This is the hypothetical n=1 mass. It equals the lightest occupied mode only in d=3 (down quark, n_down=1). In all other sectors the lightest occupied mode is at n > 1.

### §8. Coupling constants

| Coupling | Formula | Value | Geometry |
|----------|---------|-------|---------|
| g₃₃ | n_s² √(n_s+n_up) / 2 | 8√7 ≈ 21.166 | d=3 vacuum fixed-point; CP¹ base |
| g₄₄ | n_s · n_up / √(n_s+n_up) | 12/√7 ≈ 4.536 | d=3↔d=4 fixed-point |
| g₅₅ | 96 / g₂₂ | 96/722.5 ≈ 0.133 | Hopf universality |
| g₆₆ | 1/n_s | 1/4 | composite coupling (=1/χ(CP³)) |
| g₁₀,₁₀ | 1/n_s | 1/4 | = g₆₆ (shared) |
| g₂₂ | p² · q / 2 | 17²·5/2 = 722.5 | S³ Dirac spectrum + d=4 threshold |

**Anti-correlation with isometry dimension (T15f):** g_dd decreases as the isometry group dimension increases. SO(4) (6 generators): g₃₃ ≈ 21.2; SU(3) (8 generators): g₄₄ ≈ 4.5; SU(4) (15 generators): g₆₆ = 1/4 (at d=6). The physically strongest coupling sits in the sector with the smallest symmetry group. This is a trend across the three sectors named, not a law: the d=5 sector has isometry SO(6) with 15 generators — the same dimension as the d=6 SU(4) — yet g₅₅ ≈ 0.133 < g₆₆ = 1/4, so equal isometry dimension does not fix equal coupling and the monotonic reading fails at d=5.

**T9a — both Hopf coupling products equal 96:**
- g₃₃ × g₄₄ = 8√7 × 12/√7 = 96 (the √7 cancels exactly)
- g₂₂ × g₅₅ = 722.5 × (96/722.5) = 96 (by construction of g₅₅)
- 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 = 3·64/2 (T15c)

The two independent derivation chains (d=3↔d=4 from vacuum fixed-point; d=2↔d=5 from Hopf universality) both yield 96 — this is the non-trivial content of T9a.

**Rank-1 coupling matrix:** G_{dd'} = √(g_dd) · √(g_d'd') = v_d · v_d'. All cross-sector couplings factorise. The effective coupling is g_eff(n,d) = g_dd / S(n,d) (geometric dilution).

### §9. Key algebraic identities used in derivations

**Hockey-stick identity:**  
S(n,d) = S(n,d−1) + S(n−1,d)  
Used in every mode-index recursion step; the algebraic engine of the Generation Tower.

**Simplex ground state universality:**  
S(1,d) = C(d,d) = 1 for all d ≥ 0.  
Forces n_down = 1 as the unique universal ground state mode.

**Vandermonde combination rule for bosons:**  
n_boson = n_fermion + d_partner − 1 (where d_partner is the mediating sector dimension).  
Source: Part 3 §11. Used to derive n_W, n_Z, n_H from fermion quantities.

**Triangular number relation for n_W:**  
S(n_e, 2) = C(14,2) = 91; n_W = 91 − n_ν₂ = 91 − 15 = 76.  
The electron's d=2 simplex number partitions into W mode and second neutrino mode.

**Muon fixed-point self-consistency:**  
n_μ = S(n_s, 4) = 35 AND n_μ = n_charm + n_ν₂ = 20 + 15 = 35.  
These being identical is the condition that forces n_s = 4.

**Back-reaction denominator factorisation:**  
n_up · n_s² · S(n_s,4) = n_up · k₀ · n_μ = 3 · 16 · 35 = 1680.  
Also = n_s · n_up · (n_s+n_up) · S(n_s,3) = 4·3·7·20 = 1680.

## Part II — Patterns found, not yet placed in main documents

These have been verified numerically and are stated precisely. None has been assigned a theorem number or document location yet.

### §10. New additive forms of the mode indices

**Cross-sector ratio identity:**  
n_charm × N_c = n_ν₁ × N_f = 4 × n_ν₂  
✅ Polynomial identity (holds for all n_s). All three equal n_s(n_s−1)(n_s+1)(n_s+2)/6. Proof: n_charm = C(n_s+2,3), N_c = n_s−1 → product = C(n_s+2,3)·(n_s−1) = n_s(n_s+1)(n_s+2)(n_s-1)/6. n_ν₁ = C(n_s+1,3), N_f = n_s+2 → product = same. 4·n_ν₂ = 4·C(n_s+2,4) = same. Equivalently: n_ν₁/n_ν₂ = 4/N_f and n_charm/n_ν₁ = N_f/N_c. These are simplex ratio identities following directly from the binomial formula. The ratio of the first two neutrino mode indices equals 4/(n_s+2) for any n_s; at n_s=4 this is 2/3. Verified: n_s=3: 10=10=20 ✓; n_s=4: 60=60=60 ✓; n_s=5: 140=140=140 ✓.

**Charm–up spacing equals p:**  
n_charm − n_up = **p** (for all n_s)  
✅ By definition: p = S(n_s,3) − n_up = n_charm − n_up. Restated as a sector-spacing identity: the quark mode-index gap within d=4 from depth-0 to depth-1 equals the Dirac eigenstate count p that enters g₂₂.

**Neutrino spacing identity:**  
n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_ν₁ − n_up (for all n_s)  
✅ Follows from n_ν₃ = n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ − n_up → n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_ν₁ − n_up. At n_s=4: 22−15 = 10−3 = 7.  
❓ Additional claim: n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_s + n_up = 7 at n_s=4. True numerically but fails at n_s=5 (n_ν₃−n_ν₂=16≠9). The value 7 = n_s+n_up also appears as the radicand under √ in g₃₃; whether this connection is structural is unresolved.

**Second neutrino minus electron equals q minus n_up:**  
n_ν₂ − n_e = q − n_up  
✅ Proof: n_ν₂ − n_e = [S(n_up,4)] − [S(n_up,3) + n_up] = [S(n_up,4)−S(n_up,3)] − n_up = q − n_up, using the definition q = S(n_up,4)−S(n_up,3) and the tower identity n_e = n_ν₁ + n_up. At n_s=4: q−n_up = 5−3 = 2, so n_ν₂ = n_e + 2.

**d=3 sector sum equals q:**  
n_down + n_strange = 1 + 4 = **5 = q** (for any n_s: n_down + n_s = n_s+1 = q)  
✅ Immediate from n_down = 1 and n_strange = n_s.

**d=4 sector sum equals Higgs:**  
n_up + n_charm + n_top = **n_H** (documented, §5)

**Higgs as Z plus electron plus down:**  
n_H = n_Z + n_e + n_down  
✅ Follows from n_H = n_Z + n_ν₂ − n_down (§5) and n_ν₂ = n_e + 2·n_down (from n_ν₂ − n_e = q − n_up = 2 at n_s=4, with n_down=1).

---

The following identities hold **only at n_s=4** (verified to fail at n_s=3,5,6). They are recorded as observed coincidences without mechanism. Status: ❓

**n_μ + n_ν₂ + n_ν₃ = 72 = n_top** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 27≠12; n_s=5: 156≠266)

**n_top + n_τ = 95 = n_H** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 19≠8; n_s=5: 318≠309)

**(n_s+1)(n_s+n_up) = n_μ** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 54≠70)

**n_e + n_τ = 36 = N_f²** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 76≠49)

**n_ν₁ + n_ν₃ = 32 = 2⁵** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 71≠64; note 32 = 2^(n_s+1) only at n_s=4)

**n_charm = 2·n_ν₁** ❓ (C(n_s+2,3)/C(n_s+1,3) = (n_s+2)/(n_s-1) = 2 only at n_s=4; consequence of Pascal row n_s+1=5 having equal middle entries C(5,2)=C(5,3)=10)

**n_top − n_charm = n_s·n_e = 52** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 231≠120)

**Each massive d=2 boson pairs with one matter mode to the Hopf product 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 = g₃₃g₄₄ = g₂₂g₅₅** ❓ (2026-06-13):
n_W + n_charm = 76 + 20 = 96 (charm, d=4);
n_Z + n_ν₂ = 81 + 15 = 96 (ν₂, d=5);
n_H + n_down = 95 + 1 = 96 (down, d=3).
One matter primary from each of the three matter sectors d=3,4,5, reflected through the carrier 96, lands on a d=2 boson — ascending bosons W<Z<H pair with descending matter charm>ν₂>down (the sideband-about-carrier reflection that surfaced in the modulational-comb run, §15 2026-06-13). All three are n_s=4 specific exactly as the single n_Z+n_ν₂ case is (fails at n_s=5: 310≠192; the value 96=N_c(N_c+1)³/2 is fixed by N_c while the indices scale with n_s). Honest caveat: 96 minus the seven primaries also produces four non-tower values {61,86,92,93}, so the pairing is an exact relation for {W,Z,H} but not a spurious-free generator. Not a structural identity; companion to the run #5 heavy-boson-off-top cascade (Part 3 §11) and the §13 Vandermonde forms, recorded here as the completed ❓ pattern. Do not promote to a Part document without an n_s-general derivation.

**Tau identities at n_s=4:**  
n_τ = n_charm + n_up = n_e + n_ν₁ = 23 🔵 (both are consequences of n_charm=2·n_ν₁ which is itself ❓)

**n_μ = n_ν₃ + n_e = 22 + 13 = 35** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 13≠15; n_s=5: 75≠70. Equivalent to n_charm = 2·n_ν₁: n_ν₃ + n_e = 2n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ while n_μ = n_charm + n_ν₂. Found 2026-06-10.)

**Three "+1" offsets in the compact tower form all equal n_down = 1. ❓** (2026-06-09, Fable-5 pass)

The compact tower relations for the three heaviest modes contain a "+1" offset whose origin is underived:
- n_τ = n_ν₃ + n_down (explicit in Part 5 §6; the +1 here is n_down = 1)
- n_top = T − r + 1 (compact form; r is a simplex evaluation; the +1 is uninterpreted)
- n_H = T + a + 1 (compact form; a is an additive index; the +1 is uninterpreted)

Observation: all three are consistent with the +1 being the down-quark seed n_down = 1. Reading the two underived offsets as T − r + n_down and T + a + n_down reduces the unexplained residue from "three bare integer units" to "why n_down = 1 attaches at the three anchor/heaviest-mode vertices." This is a physical question — the d=3 seed touching the three heaviest modes — rather than an arithmetic blemish. At n_s = 4 this is numerically invisible (n_down = 1 regardless), but the reframing is consistent with the DAG structure where every additive edge adds either a seed index or a simplex evaluation.

Status: ❓ Observation only; no mechanism derived. Fails to add new numerical content but unifies the three offsets under a single seed label.

### §11. Modular structure (mod n_s)

Writing n = n_s · a + r, the working set partitions into four residue classes mod n_s = 4:

| r | Members | Character |
|---|---------|----------|
| 0 | 0 (γ), 4 (s), 16 (k₀), 20 (c), 72 (t), 76 (W) | bosons and quark scale anchors; all divisible by n_s |
| 1 | 1 (d), 13 (e), 17 (p), 81 (Z) | d=3 ground state, d=6 ground state, g₂₂ parameter, Z boson |
| 2 | 10 (ν₁), 22 (ν₃) | **exclusively ν₁ and ν₃** |
| 3 | 3 (u), 15 (ν₂), 23 (τ), 35 (μ), 95 (H) | up quark plus lepton/Higgs cluster |

Residue 2 contains only ν₁ and ν₃. The algebraic reason: n_ν₃ − n_ν₁ = n_ν₂ − n_up = 15 − 3 = 12 = 3·n_s ≡ 0 mod n_s. The second neutrino escapes to residue 3 because S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) = q = 5 ≡ 1 mod 4, not 0.

### §12. Factor 19

19 = n_charm − 1 = n_W/n_s = n_H/(n_s+1). Numerically: n_W = 4·19 = 76, n_H = 5·19 = 95, n_τ+n_ν₂ = 38 = 2·19. No geometric interpretation has been found. The factorisation n_W = n_s·19 and n_H = (n_s+1)·19 are numerical properties of the specific values at n_s=4; they do not generalise (at n_s=5: n_W=270=2·5·27, n_H=309=3·103). The Z does not share the factor (81=3⁴). ❓ Numerological until a mechanism is identified.

### §13. W-Z mode gap equals q

n_Z − n_W = q = n_s + 1  
✅ Polynomial identity (holds for all n_s). Proof: n_W = g(d_ν, n_top) = d_ν + n_top − 1 = (n_s+1) + n_top − 1 = n_top + n_s. n_Z = g(d_ℓ, n_W) = d_ℓ + n_W − 1 = (n_s+2) + n_W − 1 = n_W + (n_s+1). So n_Z − n_W = n_s+1 = q exactly.

The same q appears in three further contexts (all polynomial identities or definitions):
- q = S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) (definition, §6)
- n_ν₂ − n_ν₁ = q (follows from q's definition and n_ν₁ = S(n_up,3), n_ν₂ = S(n_up,4))
- n_down + n_strange = q (= 1+n_s = n_s+1 = q, trivially)
- n_Z − n_W = q (proved above)

❓ Additional observation at n_s=4: q = 5 = χ(CP⁴), the Euler characteristic of the missing sector d=8. Whether the W-Z spacing equalling the missing sector's Euler characteristic is structural or coincidental at n_s=4 is unresolved.

### §13a. The Vandermonde g-rule transition graph on the mode set

Define g(d, n) = d + n − 1, the row index of mode (n,d) in the Pascal triangle. Computing g(d, n_j) for every d ∈ D = {2,3,4,5,6,10} and every n_j ∈ NS yields **19 NS → NS transitions** out of 90 candidate (d, n_j) pairs. (Hit rate ≈ 21%; random baseline ≈ 16%.)

**The 19 transitions, by sector:**

| d | NS → NS transitions |
|---|--------------------|
| 2 | 0→1, 3→4, 22→23 |
| 3 | 1→3, 13→15, 20→22 |
| 4 | 0→3, 1→4, 10→13, 20→23 |
| 5 | 72→76 |
| 6 | 10→15, 15→20, 76→81 |
| 10 | 1→10, 4→13, 13→22, 72→81 |

**Graph structure on NS:**  
- **Sources** (no in-edge): **{0, 35, 72, 95}** = {photon, muon, top, Higgs}.  
- **Component A** (reachable from photon via g-rule alone): {0, 1, 3, 4, 10, 13, 15, 20, 22, 23} — the ten lightest particles, equivalently the seeds plus depth-1 HS evaluations plus the electron and tau.  
- **Component B** (reachable from top): {72, 76, 81} — top → W (d=5) and top → Z (d=10), W → Z (d=6).  
- **Isolated sources**: {35, 95} — muon and Higgs have no g-rule predecessor in NS.

**Why the four sources.** For each source s, no (d, n_j) ∈ D × NS satisfies d + n_j − 1 = s with n_j ≠ s:

- 0 (photon): trivially a source.  
- 35 (muon): 35 = S(n_s, n_s) is the composite-square self-image; not a g-rule output of any other NS member.  
- 72 (top): the open eigenmode-selection mode index; not in the g-rule image of NS.  
- 95 (Higgs): the high-mass empirical closure; not in the g-rule image of NS.

**Structural reading.** The g-rule alone organises ten of the fifteen particles into a single connected component rooted at the photon. The W and Z sit one and two g-steps from the top quark, making them genuinely "top-anchored" rather than independent generators. Muon and Higgs are g-rule isolated: the muon is a pure depth-1 HS evaluation (S(4,4) = 35) and the Higgs is the empirical closure. Both top and Higgs are presently the un-derived rules of the generation tower, and both are graph sources — suggesting that the open derivation problem (§5, n_top) and the empirical closure (§5, n_H) are at the *structural* source of the spectrum, not anomalies layered on top of it.

**Own-sector stepping sub-pattern (❓, 2026-06-10).** Four of the 19 transitions use d' = d_own + 1, i.e. the g-step n → n + d_own: down (1,3) → strange (4), ν₁ (10,5) → ν₂ (15), ν₂ (15,5) → charm (20), top (72,4) → W (76). Equivalently, for exactly these four particles n + d_own is itself a tower mode index; the other eleven all fail (verified over the full 15). The steps chain — down → strange, ν₁ → ν₂ → charm, top → W — with each step equal to the particle's own sector dimension. Whether d' = d_own + 1 has a kernel or Hopf-chain interpretation is open. Side observation: strange (4,3) and up (3,4) share n + d = 7.

### §13b. Confluence of the generation tower — corrected analysis (2026-05-29)

**Two distinct predecessor relations.** The §13b analysis was initially run with the GENERAL additive predecessor: any n = a+b−c with a,b ∈ NS, c ∈ {0,1,3,4}. This was then corrected to examine the TOWER-SPECIFIC directed predecessor: the actual named operations of the generation tower (Part 2 §6). The two give very different results.

**GENERAL additive predecessor: cyclic graph, no source nodes.**
Under any a+b−c=n (a,b ∈ NS, c ∈ {0,1,3,4}), ALL 15 NS particles have predecessors in NS. Specifically:
- Photon (0,2): (1,3)+(3,4)−4 = 0 — predecessors: down and up.
- Down (1,3): (0,2)+(4,3)−3 = 1 — predecessors: photon and strange.
- Up (3,4): (0,2)+(4,3)−1 = 3 — predecessors: photon and strange.
- Strange (4,3): (1,3)+(3,4)−0 = 4 — predecessors: down and up.

The L-particles form a cycle: photon ↔ {down,up}; strange ↔ {down,up}. There are **no source nodes** under the general relation. The original §13b claim "seeds have no predecessors" was a verification gap: Test 5 hardcoded {(1,3),(4,3)} as seeds and skipped computing their predecessors.

**TOWER-SPECIFIC directed predecessor: acyclic DAG, unique seeds. ✅**
Using only the actual operations of the generation tower (Part 2 §6), the derivation is a finite acyclic DAG (verified: `has_cycle = False`). Each particle has a unique tower-derivation predecessor:

| Particle | Derivation | Tower predecessors |
|----------|------------|-------------------|
| photon (0,2) | d=2 ground state (n=0 trivially) | none — always present |
| down (1,3) | SEED: S(1,d)=1 for all d | none |
| strange (4,3) | COMPOSITE: n_s = n_d + n_u = 1+3 = 4 (🔶 MC-4.4); confirmed by muon fixed point S(4,4)=35 | {down, up} |
| up (3,4) | SEED: n_u = χ(CP²) = N_c = 3 (T15); unique ΔN=+2 image of ground seed | none |
| nu1 (10,5) | S(n_u,3) = 10 | {up} |
| charm (20,4) | S(n_s,3) = 20 | {strange} |
| electron (13,6) | n_nu1 + n_u = 13 | {nu1, up} |
| nu2 (15,5) | S(n_u,4) = 15 | {up} |
| muon (35,6) | n_charm + n_nu2 = 35 | {charm, nu2} |
| nu3 (22,5) | n_nu1 + n_nu2 − n_u = 22 | {nu1, nu2, up} |
| tau (23,10) | n_nu3 + n_down = 23 | {nu3, down} |
| top (72,4) | S(n_e,2) − n_charm + 1 = 72 | {electron, charm} |
| W (76,2) | g-rule: n_top + d_ν − 1 = 76 | {top} |
| Z (81,2) | g-rule: n_W + d_ℓ − 1 = 81 | {W} |
| Higgs (95,2) | n_u + n_charm + n_top = 95 | {up, charm, top} |

Derivation depths: down and up at 0 (seeds); strange, nu1, nu2 at 1; electron, charm, nu3 at 2; tau, muon, top at 3; W, Higgs at 4; Z at 5. All 13 derived particles (excluding photon ground state) reach {(1,3),(3,4)} in at most 5 backward steps. Verified: `all particles reduce to {down, up}`.

**Seed minimality.** Neither single seed alone generates all NS via tower operations (down alone: 1/15; up alone: 2/15). Together, {down, up} generate all 14 non-photon particles (14/15), with strange as their offset-additive composite at depth 1. The photon (n=0, d=2 ground state) is always present independently of the seeds — it does not require derivation.

**Why {(1,3),(3,4)} and not some other pair.** n_down=1 is forced by S(1,d)=1 for all d (the universal harmonic oscillator ground state); n_u=3 is forced by χ(CP²)=N_c=3 (T15, ✅). The composite n_s=4 = n_d+n_u is confirmed by T4 (Part 9) and χ(CP³)=4.

**Status.** The tower derivation is a finite acyclic DAG with unique source nodes {(1,3),(3,4)} (⭐, verified), composite (4,3) at depth 1. The general additive predecessor graph is cyclic with no source nodes (verified, §15 dead end).

**Seed sector derivation (🔵, 2026-05-29).** The seed sector is d=3: it is the observable spacetime sector and the first total space S³ of the complex Hopf chain, the natural starting point of the generation tower. The primitive seeds are n_d=1 (ground state S(1,d)=1 in d=3) and n_u=3 (forced by χ(CP²)=N_c=3, T15). The composite n_s=4 = n_d+n_u is confirmed by T4 (Part 9) and the muon fixed-point S(4,4)=35. Full sector assignments then propagate via the Hopf chain structure (d=3→4→5→6,10) and trivial automorphism group — see P8 update in Part 1.

**DAG automorphism group is trivial (⭐, 2026-05-29).** The tower DAG has no non-trivial automorphisms. The only degree-compatible candidate swaps are {down ↔ strange}, {nu1 ↔ nu2}, and {tau ↔ muon}; all three fail because they violate specific predecessor constraints:

- down ↔ strange: blocked because charm has predecessor {strange} only; no NS particle has predecessor {down} only.
- nu1 ↔ nu2: blocked because electron has predecessors {nu1, up}; no NS particle has predecessors {nu2, up}.
- tau ↔ muon: blocked because muon has predecessors {nu2, charm}; tau has predecessors {down, nu3} — different composition entirely.

The full backtracking search over all 15! possible permutations (with degree-pruning) confirms: **exactly one automorphism exists — the identity**. The particle labeling is uniquely determined by the DAG structure. No alternative sector/mode-index assignment preserves the derivation order. This resolves GPT's question about graph automorphisms: there is no relabeling freedom, so the coupling vector v and the rank-1 structure G_{dd'} = v_d v_{d'} are the unique coupling structure consistent with the tower DAG. The seed values (n_d=1, n_u=3) and composite n_s=4 remain the fundamental inputs; the automorphism result says that given those values, the entire labeling of the spectrum is rigid.

### §14. n_Z = N_c⁴ (N_c = 3 specific)

n_Z = 81 = 3⁴ = N_c⁴. This holds because:

n_Z = n_top + N_c² = N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) + N_c²

Setting this equal to N_c⁴ requires N_c⁴ − N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) − N_c² = 0, which factors as N_c(N_c−3)(N_c+1)² = 0. This is satisfied only at N_c = 3 (and the unphysical N_c = 0, −1).

**The form that generalises:** n_Z = n_top + N_c² = n_top + n_up². Valid for any N_c. The form n_Z = N_c⁴ is a numerical coincidence of our world's N_c = 3.

### §21. Composite hadron masses — GOR formula with IDWT chiral condensate

**Context (2026-05-29).** Pion, kaon, and heavier mesons are not elementary sector modes and cannot be assigned (n,d) pairs. Their masses must come from a formula using constituent quark masses. The natural candidate is the Gell-Mann–Oakes–Renner (GOR) relation:

$$m_{\rm meson}^2 = (m_{q_1} + m_{q_2}) \times B_0$$

where B₀ is the chiral condensate parameter. In IDWT, B₀ is fully determined (🔵):

$$B_0 = \Lambda_{\rm QCD} \times \frac{S(n_s,3)}{2} = \frac{N_c}{2} \times \frac{f_\pi^2}{m_{\rm scale,3}} = 2821 \text{ MeV}$$

where every factor is IDWT-derived: Λ_QCD = N_c f_π = 282.1 MeV, S(n_s,3) = 20, N_c = χ(CP²) = 3. Equivalently B₀ = Λ_QCD × n_s(n_s²−1)/6, the composite's own combinatorial factor divided into the QCD scale.

**Pseudoscalar meson predictions** (m_meson = √((m_q1+m_q2)×B₀)):

| Meson | Content | m_q1+m_q2 (MeV) | Predicted (MeV) | PDG (MeV) | Error |
|-------|---------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------|-------|
| π± | ūd | 6.88 | 139.3 | 139.6 | −0.2% |
| K± | ūs | 96.2 | 521.0 | 493.7 | +5.5% |
| K⁰ | d̄s | 98.7 | 527.8 | 497.6 | +6.1% |
| D± | c̄d | 1284.4 | 1903.6 | 1869.7 | +1.8% |
| D⁰ | c̄u | 1281.9 | 1901.7 | 1864.8 | +2.0% |
| Ds | c̄s | 1373.7 | 1968.7 | 1968.4 | 0.0% |

**Pattern:** The formula works precisely (< 3%) for cross-sector pseudoscalars (q from d=3, q̄ from d=4 or vice versa). It works at the leading-order ChPT level (5–6%) for kaons. It fails for same-sector vector mesons (φ, J/ψ) and B mesons: vector mesons are sector resonances (see §21a below), not GOR composites; B mesons require the heavy-quark formula; the b quark is a beat mode not a pure harmonic eigenmode.

The Gell-Mann–Okubo relation 4m_K² − m_π² = 3m_η², applied to IDWT predictions, gives m_η = 596 MeV (PDG: 548, +9%) — consistent with leading-order SU(3) ChPT accuracy.

**Baryons (2026-05-31, `files/idwt.py`).** The correct formula is the (N_c−1) colour-bond formula, not GOR. When one quark in a colour-singlet baryon is replaced by a heavier quark, each of the remaining (N_c−1) = 2 = χ(CP¹) colour bonds contributes the mass difference:

m(baryon) = m_N + (N_c−1) × Σ(m_s − m_replaced)

Key structural identity discovered: N_c × Λ_QCD / n_u² = m_s exactly (94.04 MeV), so m_N = N_c × Λ_QCD + m_s — the nucleon mass is the colour confinement scale plus the strange quark mass, forced by seeds alone.

Results: Λ +0.3%, Ξ⁰ −0.9%, Ξ⁻ −1.4%. The Σ(uds) has identical quark content to Λ, so the formula gives both the same mass; the 77 MeV Σ−Λ difference is a small same-type residual the formula does not resolve. The Ω(sss, J=3/2) is in the baryon decuplet, outside this formula's scope.

**Status:** 🔵 (formula verified for N, Λ, Ξ). The small Σ−Λ residual (77 MeV) is not resolved by the formula. Script: `files/idwt.py`.

**Two-formula picture and the bottom quark (2026-05-29, `files/idwt.py`).** There are two distinct mass formulas depending on whether m_quark ≪ Λ_QCD (chiral regime) or m_quark ≫ Λ_QCD (heavy-quark regime). The boundary is at Λ_QCD = 282 MeV.

*Chiral (light quarks):* m² = (m_q1+m_q2)×B₀ as above — u, d, s quarks.

*Heavy-quark binding formula* (🔵):
$$m_{\rm meson} = m_{q_1} + m_{q_2} + \sqrt{m_{\rm heavy} \times \Lambda_{\rm QCD}}$$

| Meson | Predicted | PDG | Error |
|-------|-----------|-----|-------|
| B+ | 5269.3 MeV | 5279.3 | −0.19% |
| B⁰ | 5271.9 | 5279.7 | −0.15% |
| Bs | 5361.2 | 5366.9 | −0.11% |
| Υ(1S) | 9448.3 | 9460.3 | −0.13% |
| J/ψ | 3160.3 | 3096.9 | +2.0% |

D mesons sit at the crossover: both formulas give ~1% accuracy.

**The k₀ = n_s² connection.** The binding energy of every B meson and bottomonium is:
$$E_{\rm bind} = \sqrt{m_b \times \Lambda_{\rm QCD}} = m_{\rm scale,3} \times \sqrt{N_c \, S(n_s,3) \times \sqrt{S(n_s^2,3)\,S(n_s^2+1,3)}}$$

The beat level k₀ = n_s² = 16 (already derived in Part 2 as the three-resonance coincidence) appears here again: the same structural fact that fixes m_b also determines the binding energy of all B mesons. The binding energy is fully expressible in terms of n_s, N_c, and m_scale_3 — no external input.

**Remaining:** (a) J/ψ +2.0% — the expansion parameter Λ_QCD/m_c = 0.22 makes the leading-order formula approximate; the J/ψ–η_c difference is a vector–pseudoscalar object-type distinction (as ρ vs π), not a single-formula correction. (b) Σ−Λ (77 MeV): a small same-type residual. φ(1020) is handled as a d=3 sector resonance (§21a). Script: `files/idwt.py`.

### §21a. d=3 hadronic resonance spectrum — vector mesons as sector modes (🔵, 2026-05-31)

The d=3 sector supports modes at $m = m_{\rm scale,3} \times S(n,3)$ for integer $n \geq 9$. These modes are not co-fixed-points and are therefore not stable particles; they appear as broad short-lived resonances. Unlike the pseudoscalar mesons (which are GOR composites), the vector mesons are identified with specific modes in this tower. The mode indices are forced by seed algebra alone (n_up=3, n_down=1, composite n_s=n_strange=4):

$$n_\rho = n_s + n_{\rm up} + 2n_{\rm down} = 4+3+1+1 = 9 \qquad ({\rm u\bar{u}/d\bar{d}\ nonet,\ J=1})$$
$$n_\phi = 2n_s + 2n_{\rm down} = 4+4+1+1 = 10 \qquad ({\rm s\bar{s}\ nonet,\ J=1})$$

The step $n_\phi - n_\rho = n_{\rm strange} - n_{\rm up} = 4 - 3 = 1$ reflects replacing one u quark by one s quark in the composite: each such replacement shifts n by exactly $\Delta n = n_{\rm strange} - n_{\rm up} = 1$.

| n | S(n,3) | IDWT (MeV) | PDG (MeV) | Error | Resonance |
|---|--------|------------|-----------|-------|-----------|
| 9 | 165 | 775.8 | 775.3 (ρ) / 782.7 (ω) | +0.1% | ρ/ω (uū/dd̄) |
| 10 | 220 | 1034.4 | 1019.5 (φ) | +1.4% | φ (ss̄) |
| 11 | 286 | 1344.8 | 1318.2 (a₂) | +2.0% | a₂(1320) tensor |
| 12 | 364 | 1711.5 | 1720 (ρ(1700)) | −0.5% | ρ(1700) excited |
| 18 | 1140 | 5360.3 | 5366.9 (B_s) | −0.1% | B_s (bs̄) |
| 19 | 1330 | 6253.7 | 6274.5 (B_c) | −0.3% | B_c (bc̄) |
| 22 | 2024 | 9516.8 | 9460.3 (Υ(1S)) | +0.6% | Υ(1S) (bb̄) |

The ρ is independently confirmed at +0.069% by the cross-sector filter $\Gamma_{346}$ (Part 2 §10). All other entries use the sector mode formula.

Additional mode index identities (all exact from seeds):
- $n=18 = n_{\rm charm} - n_{\rm up} + n_{\rm down} = 20-3+1$ (B_s: one b + one s̄)
- $n=19 = n_{\rm charm} - n_{\rm down} = 20-1$ (B_c: one b + one c̄)
- $n=22 = n_\tau - n_{\rm down} = 23-1$ (Υ(1S): bb̄ ground state)

**Status: 🔵** (sector mode formula verified across 7 resonances). Script: `files/idwt.py` (hadronic resonance spectrum section).

### §22. Co-fixed-point stability via l-parity selection (⭐ exact + 🔵 partial, 2026-05-31)

**The kernel angular structure.** The coupling $(ξ_d \cdot ξ_{d'})^2$ decomposes on $S^{d-1}$ into $l=0$ (scalar) and $l=2$ (tensor) components only. Each application of $V_{\rm kernel}$ changes the sector angular momentum quantum number by $0$ or $\pm 2$. Angular momentum parity (even vs odd $l$) is therefore an exact conserved quantity under all powers of $V_{\rm kernel}$.

**d=3 level structure.** The d=3 sector has $d+1=4$ harmonic oscillator coordinates ($\mathbb{R}^4$ oscillator). Level $N = n-1$ contains angular momentum values $l = N, N-2, \ldots, 0$ or $1$ (same parity as $N$).

| n | Level N | l values | Parity | In Σ? | Kernel-reachable from l=0 seed? |
|---|---------|----------|--------|-------|----------------------------------|
| 1 | 0 | {0} | even | ✓ | yes (seed) |
| 2 | 1 | {1} | odd | — | **NO** (l-parity blocks) |
| 3 | 2 | {0,2} | even | — | yes (l=0 and l=2 components) |
| 4 | 3 | {1,3} | odd | ✓ | **NO** (l-parity blocks intra-sector) |
| 5 | 4 | {0,2,4} | even | — | yes |
| 6 | 5 | {1,3,5} | odd | — | **NO** |

**Exact result (⭐).** All non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes at odd levels ($n=2,6,8,10,\ldots$ in $d=3$) are permanently disconnected from the $l=0$ seeds by $V_{\rm kernel}$. No power of the kernel can generate odd-$l$ modes from even-$l$ starting points. These modes cannot be excited from the vacuum and cannot be sustained by the coupling chain. Their exclusion from Σ_pairs is exact.

**Strange quark (n=4) special case.** The strange quark sits at level $N=3$ (odd $l$ only). It is protected from intra-sector destabilisation by the same l-parity rule. Its stability comes instead from the cross-sector coupling $V_{34}$: the up quark ($n=3$, $d=4$) is at level $N=2$ in the $d=4$ oscillator, which has $l=0$ and $l=2$ components — making the cross-sector coupling from the $l=0$ seed allowed. The generation tower chain ($n=1,d=3$) $\to$ ($n=3,d=4$) $\to$ ($n=4,d=3$) then closes via the hockey-stick identity.

**l=0 kernel matrix elements (numerical, d=3).** Computed from harmonic oscillator mode functions ($\lambda_3 = 4.820$, $w=\sqrt{\lambda_3}$):

| n_r | n (d=3) | I(n) | ME ~ $(g_{33}/3) \cdot I_{\rm seed} \cdot I(n)$ | In Σ? |
|-----|---------|------|------|-------|
| 0 | 1 | 1.475 | 15.35 | ✓ (self) |
| 1 | 3 | 0.602 | 6.27 | — |
| 2 | 5 | 0.224 | 2.33 | — |
| 3 | 7 | 0.081 | 0.84 | — |
| 4 | 9 | 0.029 | 0.30 | — |

The matrix elements fall geometrically with $n_r$. The non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ even-level modes ($n=3,5,7,\ldots$) do couple to the seed, with matrix elements proportional to $I(n_r)$.

**Cross-sector coupling (n=1,d=3) → (n=3,d=4).** The up quark level $N=2$ in $d=4$ has an $l=0$ component. Numerically: $I_4(n=3, l=0) = 0.389$, giving cross-sector matrix element $\sim 1.88$ in sector units (with $g_{34} = 4\sqrt{6}$). The coupling is non-zero, confirming the generation tower connection is active.

**Self-energy of n=3 mode (numerical).** The n=3 mode at $m_{n=3} = S(3,3) \times m_{\rm scale,3} = 47.0$ MeV receives a 2nd-order self-energy correction from its coupling to the $n=1$ seed:

$$\delta E^{(2)}_{n=3} = \frac{|\langle n=3 | V_{33}^{l=0} | n=1 \rangle|^2}{m_{n=3} - m_{n=1}} = \frac{6.27^2}{47.0 - 4.7} \approx 0.93 \text{ sector units} \approx 16.4 \text{ MeV}$$

Adding the 1st-order self-coupling ($\delta E^{(1)} = 2.56$ sector units $\approx 12.0$ MeV), the total shift is $\approx +16.4$ MeV, placing the mode at $\approx 63.4$ MeV. This is between the Σ_pairs modes (down quark at 4.7 MeV, strange at 94.0 MeV) and falls on no sector resonance. The mode is off-resonance with the self-consistent coupling structure.

However: in a discrete harmonic oscillator spectrum, 2nd-order perturbation theory shifts eigenvalues but does not give them finite width. Exact irreversibility requires the mode to couple to a continuous spectrum. The multi-sector coupling chain ($d=3\to d=4\to\cdots\to d=10$) acts as a bath that time-averages the return amplitude to zero via incommensurability (§15 ✅), but these $d\le 10$ towers are countable and discrete and cannot supply a continuous spectral measure. The $d>10$ free-dimension spectrum is the bath that can (see addendum below; Part 4 §4).

**Dephasing in the multi-sector coupled system (🔵).**

Even-level non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes are not eigenstates of $H$: their self-energy shifts them off every $\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ resonance, and they have nonzero off-diagonal matrix elements to the mode towers of the five active sectors. The cross-sector mass scales are incommensurate (all ratios irrational except the $\mu$–$\tau$ pair; §15 ✅), so no common revival period exists and the time-averaged return amplitude vanishes (Wiener). The $d\le 10$ mode towers form a countable discrete spectrum, however, and a countable discrete spectrum gives an almost-periodic survival amplitude that recurs (Poincaré) — time-averaged dephasing is not the same as permanent decay. Exact irreversibility requires the reduced spectral measure to be continuous; the $d>10$ free-dimension continuum is the bath that can supply it (see addendum below; Part 4 §4). Establishing this coupling is the remaining step the status 🔵 records.

Decoherence time: $\tau \sim 1/(\text{ME} \times m_{\rm scale,3})$. For $n=3$: ME $\approx 6.3$ sector units, $\tau \approx 0.034\ \text{MeV}^{-1} \sim 1/m_{\rm scale,3}$.

**Co-fixed-point stability derivation complete (🔵).** All non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes are unstable:
- Odd-level modes: $l$-parity selection rule (⭐ exact)
- Even-level modes: off-diagonal mixing + time-averaged dephasing; exact irreversibility requires d>10 continuum bath (🔵)

The even-level 🔵 is the proven ceiling, not merely the current best: the seed-coupling overlap has no node at the kernel weight $s=3/2$ (its only zero is $s=1$), so the coupling is strictly nonzero for every even-level mode and no exact $l$-parity-style cut exists for this class under the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel (§15, 2026-06-05; `files/idwt.py` STEP 34). The open item is the EOM derivation of the dephasing, not a further exact cut.

**Quantitative revival amplitude bound (2026-06-09, `files/idwt.py` STEP 49).** The within-sector Rabi coupling between a non-tower even-level mode and the nearest tower mode gives a maximum return amplitude of order $(J/\Delta S)^2$, where $\Delta S = S(n_{\rm nt},d) - S(n_{\rm tower},d)$ is the energy detuning in simplex units. By spectral independence (⭐, sum-free $S$-values, Part 1 §5 Uniqueness Theorem), all detunings are strictly positive. Summing over all non-tower even modes per sector:

| Sector $d$ | $\sum_n (J/\Delta S)^2$ |
|:---:|:---:|
| 2 | $2.0\times10^{-5}$ |
| 3 | $4.2\times10^{-4}$ |
| 4 | $5.5\times10^{-5}$ |
| 5 | $1.7\times10^{-7}$ |
| 6 | $1.2\times10^{-10}$ |
| 10 | $1.1\times10^{-17}$ |

The worst case ($d=3$) bounds the coherent within-sector return amplitude at $\lesssim 2\%$; all other sectors are smaller by factors of $10^1$–$10^{13}$. Cross-sector revival is separately time-averaged to zero by the incommensurability lemma (✅, §15 STEP 40). Total return probability therefore $\lesssim 4\times10^{-4}$. This is the tightest available quantitative bound on T0.5 even-level dephasing; it does not reach exact zero (which would require the vacuum-dimension bath argument), so 🔵 remains the correct status.

**Addendum — the even-level bath is the d>10 continuum, not the d≤10 towers; spectral-measure reframing and an exact-width-cancellation null (2026-06-10, opus).** Sharpens the even-level argument and resolves the internal tension between the paragraph above (line 585: exact decay "requires the mode to couple to a continuum") and the "infinite-dimensional dephasing" paragraph (which treats the countable multi-sector tower as that continuum).

*Reframing (RAGE/Wiener, rigorous).* A mode $(n,d)$ is a stable particle $\iff$ its spectral measure under the full $H=H_0+V_{\rm kernel}$ has a point mass (atom); it decays $\iff$ the measure is purely continuous (survival amplitude $\to 0$ by Riemann–Lebesgue). This is the exact form of "dephasing," and it matches T0 ("physical masses are eigenvalues of the projected operator" — eigenvalues are the point spectrum).

*No-go (closes the d≤10 route).* The five active sectors $d\le 10$ each carry a **countable, discrete** mode tower, and $S(n,d)\sim n^d$ makes the level spacing grow, not accumulate. A countable discrete spectrum gives an **almost-periodic** survival amplitude: by Wiener's theorem its time-average vanishes, but it **recurs** (Poincaré) — it never reaches an exact continuous measure. So coupling to the $d\le 10$ towers, however many, cannot upgrade the even-level cut to ✅; the residual $\lesssim 4\times10^{-4}$ is the structural ceiling of *that* bath, not a temporary bound. Demonstrated numerically on the actual IDWT energies $S(n,d)m_{\rm scale,d}$: the discrete sector bath drives the even non-tower mode $(3,3)$ down to $|A|=0.12$ but it **recurs to $0.88$**; an equal-width genuine continuum decays it to $|A|=0$ with the revival $\to 0$ as the level spacing $\to 0$ (`explore_bic_selection.py` part a).

*The actual bath.* The continuum line 585 requires is the **$d>10$ free-dimension spectrum**: by "Bound within, free without" (subsection below) the outer dimensions carry absolutely continuous spectrum $[0,\infty)$ and the mode is uniformly present there ("present, not absent"). This is the "vacuum-dimension bath" line 612 flags as the missing ingredient — now identified concretely. The seed-coupling overlap's non-node at $s=3/2$ ($J(n_r,3/2)\ne 0$, STEP 34) — the fact that *blocks* an exact intra-sector $l$-parity cut — is exactly the nonzero coupling that *drives* irreversible decay into this continuum: the obstruction becomes the mechanism.

*Tower protection — exact-width-cancellation test (NULL).* For a tower mode to remain in the point spectrum while its radiative coupling to the $[0,\infty)$ continuum is open, its decay width at the tower site would have to vanish by an exact cancellation. IDWT's rank-1 kernel $g_{dd'}=v_dv_{d'}$ (T2) makes the decay matrix rank-1 ($\det\Gamma=0$), the structural setting in which such a cancellation could occur. But the concrete test fails: scanning adjacent pairs $(n,n+1)$ with continuum couplings modelled by $J(n_r,3/2)^2$ and inter-mode coupling $V=\sqrt{b_nb_{n+1}}$, the narrowed-width pattern tracks only the odd/even parity of $n$ (an artifact of the $n_r=\lfloor(n-1)/2\rfloor$ overlap proxy), not tower membership, and the exact zero-width condition $V(\gamma_1-\gamma_2)=(E_1-E_2)\sqrt{\gamma_1\gamma_2}$ is not satisfied at the tower sites — so no protective width-cancellation forms in this model. A coupling-level mechanism that zeroes a tower mode's width is therefore **not** established by this proxy; the tower-protection question remains 🔶.

*Net.* Status unchanged (odd-level ⭐ exact; even-level 🔵/🔶). The advance is structural: the open problem is re-posed from the unreachable "prove the discrete multi-sector dephasing is irreversible" to the well-posed pair (i) compute the Wigner–Weisskopf width of a non-tower even mode coupling into the $d>10$ free-dimension continuum (occupied-sector presence there is established), and (ii) decide whether any exact width-cancellation protects the tower modes — the width-cancellation route is now a logged null, and the 2026-06-13 radiative-width companion below settles (ii) negatively: the stable members carry no width suppression, so their stability is target-absence, not a protective mechanism. Wording items for Fedge (report-before-edit, left unedited): Part 7 §1.2 and the line-589 paragraph above state "infinite-dimensional ⟹ permanent dephasing"; a countable *discrete* spectrum still recurs (Wiener), so the bath must be named as the $d>10$ continuum specifically, not the multi-sector towers.

*$l$-parity is the UNIQUE exact grading of the quadratic kernel — the second-rule route to ✅ is closed sector-universally (2026-06-14).* **[RETRACTED 2026-06-14 — the connectivity test is powerless; see the CORRECTION at the end of this paragraph. The claim below does not hold.]** The documents leave one route to upgrading the even-level selection from 🔵 to ✅: a *second* exact selection rule in the kernel's representation theory, analogous to $l$-parity, that forbids the non-member even indices outright. A selection rule of that kind is a discrete label conserved by $V_{\rm kernel}$ that partitions the sector modes into non-communicating classes; it exists **iff** the kernel coupling graph is *disconnected* within an $l$-parity class. The graph is built from the exact angular content $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2 = l{=}0 \oplus l{=}2$: a single kernel application changes $l$ by $\{0,\pm2\}$ and the oscillator level $N=2n_r+l$ by $\{0,\pm2\}$, so $(n_r,l)\sim(n_r',l')$ iff $|l-l'|\in\{0,2\}$ and $|N-N'|\in\{0,2\}$. Computed to $N\le40$: **each $l$-parity class is a single connected component** (even-level 231 modes $\to$ 1 component; odd-level 210 $\to$ 1), and every even-level member ($d$ at $N{=}0$, $u$ at 2, $e$ at 12, $\nu_2$ at 14, $\tau$ at 22, $\mu$ at 34; $Z,H$ above cutoff, same structure) is an interior node of the giant even-component — none is isolated into a separable sub-class. The graph *support* is sector-universal: the angular content $l\in\{0,2\}$ is dimension-independent and the radial $r^2$ element is tridiagonal-nonzero in every $d$ (standard oscillator; magnitudes never vanish — run #2 STEP 34, $J(n_r,3/2)\sim(1/3)^{n_r}>0$). Therefore no discrete label finer than $l$-parity is conserved by $V$ in any sector. Combined with the closed prior routes — magnitudes never vanish (run #2), and no continuous threshold separates members (runs #1, #3, $R$ continuous to $1.5\times10^{-9}$) — this establishes the **bound**: under the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel, no exact selection rule beyond $l$-parity exists, in any sector. The even-level selection is provably 🔵 — it cannot be lifted to ✅ by any kernel selection rule — and the residual selection is necessarily *dynamical* (the nonlinear EoM / four-wave amplitude basin, Part 6 MC-4), not a representation-theoretic cut. This converts the scattered run #1/#2/#3/#5 nulls into one sector-universal status bound for T0.5. (Status unchanged; this fixes the *ceiling*, it does not move a label. Candidate one-line addition to Part 9 T0.5 — report-before-edit, left unedited.)

*CORRECTION — the "unique exact grading" bound above is WITHDRAWN; the connectivity test has no power (2026-06-14, adversarial audit).* The graph statement is true but vacuous as a claim about selection. Re-running with the physically-correct rank-2 tensor angular support — the diagonal $l\to l$ via the $l=2$ component vanishes only at $l=0$ (the 3j $(l\,2\,l;000)=0$), every other parity-allowed edge present — gives the identical single component (even $231\to1$, odd $210\to1$), and the graph stays connected after deleting half its edges at random. Connectivity within an $l$-parity class is automatic for ANY operator carrying $l=0\oplus l=2$ (the moves $(n_r,l)\to(n_r,l{+}2)$ and $(n_r,l)\to(n_r{+}1,l)$ are always present), so the test cannot return "disconnected" and carries no IDWT-specific information. Three further gaps compound this: (i) it reduces the genuinely two-body kernel $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ to a single-mode hopping graph, so pairwise/joint conserved quantities — e.g. the index resonances $n_i+n_j=n_k$ (run #8) — are invisible to it; (ii) it only tests labels that are functions of $(n_r,l)$, leaving selectors on the index arithmetic ($n=2n_r+l+1$, binomial/simplex), the radial node count, or the cross-sector $d$ entirely out of scope; (iii) it was cut at $N\le40$ with $Z\,(N{=}80)$ and $H\,(N{=}94)$ never placed. The inference "no exact selection rule beyond $l$-parity exists / the residual selection is necessarily dynamical" therefore does NOT follow — it was a non-sequitur from a powerless test. Honest status: $l$-parity (odd level) remains the only DEMONSTRATED exact selector (⭐); for the even-level core, whether a numerical/arithmetic selector exists is OPEN, not closed. Companion significance test on the positive structure (the run #8 additive comb): the 14 tower indices carry 10 exact 3-wave relations $n_i+n_j=n_k$ and 22 four-wave matchings $n_i+n_j=n_k+n_l$, but against a range-matched null (14 random integers in $[1,95]$) this is not anomalous ($P(\ge10)=0.12$; $P(\ge22)=0.44$); the apparent significance against a wider $[1,200]$ null ($P\approx10^{-3}$) is a range artifact of the members' compressed span. The additive relations are the tower's additive construction restated, not an independent selector — a quantified null, not a proof that none exists. Net: the "second-rule route is closed" claim is retracted; the even-level selection question is reopened.

*POWERED replacement for the retracted connectivity test — the REAL two-body $d=3$ coupling matrix (2026-06-14, opus).* The retracted test failed because it collapsed the two-body kernel to a single-mode adjacency graph, where connectivity is automatic and carries no information. This builds the actual operator. The $d=3$ sector is the $\mathbb{R}^4$ isotropic oscillator; the kernel $V=\tfrac{g_{33}}{2}(\xi\cdot\xi')^2 = \tfrac{g_{33}}{2}\,r^2 r'^2(\Omega\cdot\Omega')^2$ is built in the **rotational-singlet two-body channel** (physical particles are SO(4)-rotation singlets; the pair couples to total $l=0$) from $\mu$-matched SO(4) multiplets $|n_r,l,\mu\rangle$ — lowest-shell harmonics $\ker(B)$ raised by the scalar $B^\dagger=\sum_i a_i^{\dagger 2}$ — giving exact angular (Gaunt on $S^3$) $\times$ radial (Laguerre) matrix elements with no recoupling algebra. The construction is validated against the analytic value $\langle 0,0|V|0,0\rangle = \tfrac{g_{33}}{2}\,w^{-2}=2.1955$ (exact match; $w=\sqrt{\lambda_3}$, $\lambda_3=4.820$). This is the genuinely two-body test the graph could not do, and it has **power** — a hidden conserved label or near-block would show up. Results: (1) **The only exactly-conserved additive label of $V$ is $l$-parity** ($n\bmod 2$): cross-block leakage $\|V_{\text{across-}Q}\|/\|V\| = 0$ for $l$-parity and $\ge 0.37$ for every other library label. Tower membership $\{1,4\}$ as a label leaks at **0.43** — $V$ actively mixes tower with non-tower pairs, so it is not even approximately conserved. (2) **Label-free near-block (Fiedler) test:** within each $l$-parity class the weighted $|V|$ graph is an *expander* (algebraic connectivity $0.40$ even, $0.59$ odd — far from the $\approx 0$ that a near-disconnected split would give); no hidden approximate conserved quantity or block beyond $l$-parity exists. The Fiedler partition does not isolate the tower. (3) The ground state of $H=H_0+V$ is the seed pair $(n{=}1,n{=}1)=$(down,down) at 94%; the strongly-coupled $V$ eigenstates localize on high-$N$ pairs (the $N(N{-}1)$ magnitude growth of $\langle r^2\rangle$), with no tower preference. Because down ($n{=}1$, even $N$) and strange ($n{=}4$, odd $N$) sit in *opposite* parity classes, no single $l$-parity class even contains the $d=3$ tower — confirming sec 22's point that strange's stability is the cross-sector $V_{34}$ coupling, not an intra-sector $d=3$ selector. **Net (powered null):** the static two-body $d=3$ coupling spectrum carries $l$-parity as its unique exact grading and no approximate block structure selecting the tower. Unlike the retracted connectivity claim this is informative — the leakage and Fiedler statistics could have been small and were not. It does not close the even-level question (a numerical/arithmetic selector outside the kernel-operator's reach remains possible, and the $q(n_1)+q(n_2)$ additive-label form plus a finite library are not exhaustive — the Fiedler step is label-free but is one sector and one channel), but it removes the *kernel two-body operator* as the home of any selector beyond $l$-parity. Consistent with the convergent 06-10/06-11 finding that the static/continuous dynamics are non-selective and the residual must be the nonlinear EoM amplitude basin (Part 6 MC-4); status unchanged (odd ⭐; even 🔵/🔶). Logged here rather than as an `idwt.py` STEP pending Fedge's call on whether it is cited in Part 9 T0.5 (report-before-edit; no document status edited).

*The four-wave amplitude basin run PRE-PRISM — the prism is a freezing mechanism (2026-06-14, opus, Fedge directive "run it pre-prism, m_scale=1, why these harmonics").* The genuinely-open MC-4 route is the time-domain four-wave (GP) amplitude dynamics — never integrated (prior MC-4.4–4.6 were static: energy detuning, reachability, characteristic class). Integrating it post-prism (physical $m_{\rm scale,d}$) gives a clean **non-selection**: the composite edges are *index* resonances ($n_i+n_j=n_k+n_l$) but mix sectors of wildly different scale, so they are energy-off-shell by $|\Delta E|/E$ up to $4\times10^7$ (e.g. $\nu_3=\nu_1+\nu_2-u$ spans $d=5$ at $m_{\rm scale,5}\sim10^{-13}$ and $d=4$ at $0.145$); the rotating-wave factor $e^{i\Delta E t}$ washes them out, and a focused integration buries $\nu_3$ at rank 8 among $d=5$ modes. So with the physical scales the four-wave dynamics cannot build the tower — reconfirming the static MC-4 nulls, now dynamically. **Pre-prism this inverts.** Before the scales condense the modes are harmonics of a common oscillator, dimensionless energy = oscillator level $E=\omega N$, $N=n-1$. Then **every index-conserving four-wave is exactly level-balanced**: $n_i+n_j=n_k+n_l \Leftrightarrow (n_i{-}1)+(n_j{-}1)=(n_k{-}1)+(n_l{-}1)$ (the $-1$ zero-points cancel; verified on $10^5$ random index-conserving quartets, all exactly balanced; $\nu_3$ edge $|\Delta E|=0$ vs $2\times10^7$ post-prism). The three-wave sum edges ($e=\nu_1+u$, $\tau=\nu_3+d$, $\mu=c+\nu_2$) carry a single $+1$ level offset, on-shell up to one condensate/pump quantum. So the additive index tower **is** a harmonic four-wave resonance network, fully on-shell **only in the pre-prism (uniform-scale, harmonic-level) phase** — which is exactly the late-prism ordering (integers laid down first, scales condense after). Note the proper resonance frequency is the oscillator **level** $E\propto N$, not the mass $S(n,d)$ ($m_{\rm scale}{=}1$ alone, $E=S$, is still off-shell by $26\times$ because the cumulative count $S$ is nonlinear in $N$); the prism is precisely the nonlinear, scale-differentiating map $N\mapsto S(n,d)\,m_{\rm scale,d}$. **Two consequences.** (i) *Freezing/stability mechanism (new):* the prism throws the entire index-resonant network off-shell, so once the integer tower forms pre-prism, scale condensation detunes every four-wave redistribution channel and **freezes** it — a dynamical origin for the tower's post-prism stability (the even-level persistence 🔵), complementary to the kernel-level stability-equivalence. (ii) *Selection still open (honest null):* on-shell-ness is *generic* to all index-conserving four-wave, so it does **not** single out the tower — counting on-shell resonant drive per $d=5$ target, the tower modes $\{10,15,22\}$ carry no excess and $\nu_3$ ranks 17–20/25 in every convention; the over-generation (index closure reaches the whole band) persists. Net: the pre-prism/harmonic reframing **validates the late-prism picture and supplies a freezing mechanism** for tower stability, but the question "why *these* harmonics among the on-shell set" is not closed by four-wave resonance — it remains the generator/seeding residue (hockey-stick ⭐ + $\chi$-seeding ✅ + Hopf routing ✅ supply the moves; firing-as-a-set stays 🔶, unchanged). The freezing result is a candidate Layer-1→Layer-2 dynamical bridge (Layer-1 integer / Layer-2 scale separation); report to Fedge before any Part edit.

**Addendum — "condensate-assisted 3-waves" are photon-inclusive 4-waves (2026-06-14).** The pre-prism level-balance identity extends to all three cross-sector composite rules in STEP 1. The photon has $n=0$ and therefore level $N = 0-1 = -1$, which supplies exactly the $-1$ level unit missing from each 3-wave sum. Each "condensate-assisted 3-wave" is an exact 4-wave with the photon on the output side:

All verified exact. The term "condensate-assisted" in prior notes was a misidentification; the balancing mode is the photon.
