### Bound within, free without — a particle in the dimensions beyond its sector (resolves a Fedge question, 2026-06-04)

**Question.** A particle is bound in its $d$ sector dimensions. In the dimensions beyond $d$ (the ones it is "not in"), does it (A) drift freely as a localized lump, (B) stay put at a point, or float in some other sense — and does any of it survive normalizability?

**Setup.** Harmonic sector confinement $V_d = \lambda_d r^2$ (Part 4 §3.9); ground state Gaussian of width $L_d = \lambda_d^{-1/4}$, normalizable on $\Xi_d$ ($\int_{\Xi_d}|\chi|^2 = 1$). A $d$-particle feels $V_d$ in its $d$ coordinates only; in every dimension past $d$ it is **free** ($H_{\rm outer} = -\Delta_{\rm outer}$), since the $d=7,8,9$ band carries no sector geometry (T3) and $V_{10}$ belongs to the tau, not to a $d<10$ mode.

**Result (✅ for the normalizability core).**
- $-d^2/dy^2$ on a free direction has spectrum $[0,\infty)$: no negative eigenvalue, hence **no normalizable bound state in a free dimension.** Solutions: $e^{iky}$ ($E>0$, momentum), $\text{const}$ ($E=0$, uniform), $e^{+|k|y}$ ($E<0$, divergent — unphysical).
- The unique zero-momentum (rest) configuration in a free dimension is the **constant.** So a massive particle, in the dimensions beyond its sector, is **uniform — present everywhere, pinned to no point.** This is "floats freely," made precise.
- Localizing to width $\Delta$ costs $E_{\rm kin}\sim 1/(2m\Delta^2)$ (uncertainty); rest ($E\to0$) $\Leftrightarrow \Delta\to\infty \Leftrightarrow$ uniform. So "stay put at a point" (B) is not a rest state, and "drift as a lump" (A) needs momentum (excited). Neither as posed — the answer is **uniform co-presence.**
- **Normalizability:** the mode is normalized on $\Xi_d$. Uniformity in the outer dims is the nesting embedding $C^\infty(\Xi_d)\subset C^\infty(\Xi_{d'})$; the divergent "norm over the outer volume" only says "normalize on $\Xi_d$ — it is a $d$-object." Cross-sector coupling is the overlap on the shared coords (Part 1 §3g), consistent with the §3i "already there" framing.
- **Massless vs massive:** dispersion $E^2 = p_{\rm outer}^2 + m^2$. $m>0$ admits a rest state (uniform); $m=0$ (photon) has no rest frame, so its free state in the outer dims necessarily carries momentum → **propagation.** Same principle; masslessness upgrades uniform presence to propagation. Orientation freedom (rotating $\Xi_d$) is the separate, symmetry-protected, always-normalizable piece.

**Status.** ✅ for the normalizability core (no bound state in a free direction; rest = uniform; normalize on $\Xi_d$). The reading "uniform presence = floats freely" and the massless→propagation upgrade are 🔵 structural interpretation. Placed in Part 1 §3i as the "Bound within, free without" subsection (after "Cross-sector interaction involves no separate objects"), carrying the ✅/🔵 split. Recorded in `files/idwt.py` as STEP 33 (computation block in the compute section, output block at the end). 
**Addendum — the dimensions beyond $d$ are not a selective channel for the even-level distinction (2026-06-10).** Part 7 §1.2 frames the even-level non-members as excluded by coupling to the $d>10$ dimensions, where the wave is uniformly present (Part 1 §3i) and any feature entering disperses (T5; Part 4 §3.12.2). Tested whether that coupling can distinguish a persistent (co-fixed-point) sector excitation from one that disperses. The self-coupling kernel $(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2$ is quadratic, so it links a level-$N$ sector excitation ($N=n-1$; harmonic sector well, Part 4 §3.10) to level $N\pm2$, with strength $|\langle N{-}2|r^2|N\rangle|^2 \propto N(N-1)$. That strength has no special value at the tower indices (only the $n=1$ ground state, $N=0$, gives zero), grows monotonically with $n$, and is shared by members and non-members — the electron ($n=13$, $d=6$) and the $d=3$ non-member $n=13$ both give $N(N-1)=132$; $\nu_2$ ($n=15$, $d=5$) and the $d=3$ non-member $n=15$ both give $182$. So the wave's coupling into the dimensions beyond $d$ cannot be what selects the tower: it singles out no index, and a coupling strong enough to disperse the non-members would disperse the heaviest members ($t$, $H$, $Z$, largest $N(N-1)$) faster, contradicting their persistence. The dimensions beyond $d$ are therefore a non-selective channel. Consequence for the standing goal: the even-level distinction between a persistent excitation and a dispersing one has to come from the self-coupled wave's own dynamics — the nonlinear equation of motion for $\Psi_\infty$ — not from coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$. This is consistent with §1.2's own dephasing reading (the wave's amplitude at a non-member index spreads across the tower with no revival) and redirects effort there. No document status edited.

**Companion — the self-consistency / standing-wave closure is also non-selective for the even-level index (2026-06-10).** The other quanta-free handle on T0.5 is the existence side: a particle is a self-consistent standing solution of the nonlinear self-coupled equation $D\phi + W[|\phi|^2]\phi = E\phi$, and the proposal is that the 15 are the closure of the seeds under that condition. Tested the three closure conditions a standing configuration of the one wave can obey; none selects the even-level tower index. (i) *Intra-sector* — the self-generated well is harmonic ($\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$, a density-sourced fixed point independent of which level sits in it; Part 4 §3.10), so it admits a standing state at every level $N=0,1,2,\dots$ and singles out no $n$. (ii) *Closure under kernel links* — the quadratic kernel allows $\Delta N=0,\pm2$ links with nonzero radial overlap ($J(n_r,3/2)\neq0$, STEP 34), so every massive member has an allowed link to a same-sector non-member (28 such member→non-member links among the 15); the 15-set is not an invariant/closed configuration. (iii) *Stationarity* — a transition is driven only between degenerate modes; $S(n,d)$ is strictly increasing (no intra-sector degeneracy) and all cross-sector scale ratios are irrational except the $d=6/d=10$ commensurate pair (STEP 40), whose only coincidences are between non-members (e.g. $(1,6)$–$(1,10)$), so stationarity isolates nothing. The one place the kernel forbids a link outright is $l$-parity (odd levels) — which is exactly the part already ⭐ exact. **Net:** two independent IDWT routes — coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$ (addendum above) and the standing-wave self-consistency closure (here) — both come back non-selective for the even-level index. The exact structural cut exists only where the kernel forbids a connection outright ($l$-parity, odd levels). For the even levels the distinction between a persistent and a dispersing excitation is a robustness/persistence difference (the dephasing hierarchy), i.e. a quantitative 🔵 statement, not an exact theorem — which is the honest reading of the T0.5 even-level status. What is NOT excluded by (i)–(iii): a finer self-consistency that fixes mode amplitudes (the nonlinear equation does fix them, via the $\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$ well and $m_{{\rm scale},d}^2=g_{dd}\langle|\Psi^{(d)}|^2\rangle$) and asks whether the amplitude fixed point exists only at the tower indices.

**Amplitude-pinned self-consistency tested — also non-selective, for a counting reason (2026-06-11).** Pinning the amplitude makes the well an output of the occupied density rather than a free background, which is the last place the index could be fixed dynamically. It is not: the self-consistency equations fix the *continuous* data $(\lambda_d, m_{{\rm scale},d})$ — already T9/T11 — and the mode index $n$ does not enter them at leading order ($\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$ is ground-state-sourced and carries no $n$; the same $\lambda_d$ holds for any occupancy). The only $n$-dependence is the sub-leading back-reaction dressing, IDWT's geometric dilution $g_{\rm eff}=g_{dd}/S(n,d)$; sorted across all low modes, members and non-members interleave with no separating threshold (143 non-members fall inside the member $g_{\rm eff}$ range, which runs from the seed's $\approx21$ down to $\sim10^{-8}$). A scalar/continuous condition cannot pin a discrete integer set: per sector the self-consistency supplies $\sim2$ real constraints, fixing the well and the scale, and *zero* constraints on which integer levels are occupied. **This closes the self-consistency route.** Across the whole investigation — coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$, kernel-link closure, stationarity, and now amplitude-pinning — every condition the wave's continuous self-dynamics supplies is non-selective for the index. The one exact discrete selector in the dynamics is $l$-parity, and it fixes parity only (kills the odd levels). The 15-index selection is therefore finer than anything the continuous dynamics determines; it is irreducibly the combinatorial generation tower, and the dynamical necessity of *that specific* combinatorial structure is the open core of T0.5 (the standing-goal residue). Honest status reading unchanged: odd-level exclusion ⭐ exact ($l$-parity); even-level/index selection a combinatorial backbone (🔶) plus a quantitative persistence hierarchy (🔵); no ✅ is available for it from the continuous dynamics. No document status edited.

**Addendum — the $d>10$ vacuum-dimension bath is dynamically closed: zero decay width at all orders (2026-06-11).** This closes T0.5 sub-problem (a) — the width of a non-tower even mode coupling into the $d>10$ continuum — negatively and exactly. The kernel $\tfrac12\sum_{d,d'\in D} g_{dd'}(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2 J_d J_{d'}$ has support only on sector coordinates $1..10$: the dot product runs over the shared coordinates, so coordinate axis $j$ appears in the $(d,d')$ term iff $j\le\min(d,d')$ — the band $7$–$9$ enters only through the $g_{10,10}$ self-term, and no coordinate beyond 10 appears in any term (verified programmatically over $D^2$). Translations of every coordinate beyond 10 are therefore exact symmetries of the full action, the conjugate outer momentum is conserved, and a stationary sector mode — outer-uniform by Part 1 §3i (✅), an exact zero of outer momentum — has identically vanishing matrix element to every outer-momentum state $k\neq0$. Any product of outer-independent operators is outer-independent, so the vanishing holds at all orders in the kernel: the width into the $d>10$ absolutely continuous spectrum is zero by symmetry, for members and non-members alike. ✅ (symmetry consequence of the stated action). Numerical demonstration: a toy sector⊗outer-ring evolution under an outer-independent coupling keeps the $k\neq0$ outer occupation at $5.9\times10^{-28}$ (machine zero), while an artificial $\cos(qy)$ control coupling populates $k=\pm q$ to $8.5\times10^{-2}$ — the zero is structural (absence of outer support), not numerical. Consequence: the "decay into the $d>10$ continuum" completion route that the 🔵 status of Part 7 §1.2 records as its remaining step is not merely unproved — it is unavailable under the current action. This sharpens the 2026-06-10 addendum (non-selective channel) to a closed channel. (The §1.2 and Part 9 T0.5 wording edits were executed 2026-06-11 with Fedge's approval; the result is recorded as `files/idwt.py` STEP 64.)

**Companion — the only absolutely continuous spectrum coupled to sector excitations is the spacetime momentum continuum; channel catalog and the stability equivalence (same script).** All active sector wells are purely discrete ($\sigma_{\rm ess}=\emptyset$, harmonic; Part 4 §3.13 Part I); the band $7$–$9$ and $d>10$ free directions are closed by the symmetry above (for non-tau modes the band coordinates are touched only by $g_{10,10}$, which acts through the $d=10$ density, itself well-bound in all 10 coordinates). What remains is the spatial momentum of the propagation factor $\psi(x)$: exact irreversibility of a non-member's dephasing, if it exists, must be ordinary radiation — kernel redistribution of the excitation into lighter linked configurations carrying continuous spatial momentum. The downward-channel catalog over the 14 single tower modes: every member with $n\ge3$ has a parity-allowed same-sector link $(n,d)\to(n-2,d)$ ($N$ and $N-2$ share parity; radial ME generically nonzero, proved nonzero for $d=3$, $l=0$ at the kernel weight, STEP 34), and in all 13 such cases the target is a non-member; only the $N=0$ ground mode $d\,(1,3)$ is structurally closed. The spatial-radiation channel is therefore again non-selective in itself — and phenomenologically right-shaped: the members observed to be unstable ($s,c,t,b,W,Z,H,\mu,\tau$) all have open links, and the channel picture assigns finite widths to exactly such modes. The sharp residue is the other direction: the members observed to be absolutely stable with **open** links — $e\,(13,6)\to(11,6)$ (would release $0.29$ MeV into spatial radiation), $u\,(3,4)\to(1,4)$, and the neutrinos $(10,5)\to(8,5)$, $(15,5)\to(13,5)$, $(22,5)\to(20,5)$ — are protected only if their downward targets are absent from the physical spectrum, which is exactly the even-level selection of T0.5. **At kernel level, the T0.5 even-level selection is equivalent to the absolute stability of the electron, the u quark, and the neutrinos**, giving T0.5 a sharp empirical witness ($\tau_e > 6.6\times10^{28}$ yr; proton-decay bounds): the selection does falsifiable work, while its derivation remains the open core (status unchanged: 🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence hierarchy). Caveats: kernel-level statements (EOM confirmation open, MC-4 line); the radiated configuration and the rate require the nonlinear redistribution calculation (Part 6, "sector transition rates"); sector-granular coupling rows (`idwt.py` STEP 2b) mean no conserved coupling structure closes a same-sector downward channel — only non-existence of the target does; for $d=5$ the anomalous BdG block vanishes (STEP 36) but the normal density-channel link is the relevant object here, its radial ME not separately computed; the $b$ quark (beat resonance) poses a structurally different channel question. No document status edited.

**Companion — the stable members are not protected by a small radiative width; their stability is the absence of the downward target, and the tower is downward-independent (necessary, not sufficient) (2026-06-13).** Computed the downward-link width $\Gamma(n,d)\sim (v_dv_2)^2\,N(N-1)\,\Delta E^3$ ($\Delta E=[S(n,d)-S(n-2,d)]\,m_{\rm scale,d}$, $d=2$ radiated quantum, 3D phase space) for all 14 modes. **Result (i):** the absolutely stable charged members carry no width suppression — $u(3,4)\to(1,4)$ has $\Delta E=2.03$ MeV and $e(13,6)\to(11,6)$ has $\Delta E=0.29$ MeV, both with open widths were the target present, and the kernel matrix element does not vanish at the member sites; $e$'s smaller width tracks its smaller $\Delta E$, not a cancelled coupling. So the stability of $e,u$ is **target-absence** — the link has no physical final state because $(n-2,d)\notin\Sigma$ — not a dynamical protection of the member itself. This confirms the stability equivalence is exactly an equivalence (member stable $\iff$ its downward target absent from $\Sigma$), with no separate protective mechanism behind it. (The neutrino widths are tiny only because $m_{\rm scale,5}\sim10^{-13}$, the scale that makes them light — again not a protection.) **Result (ii):** the tower is downward-independent — no member's $(n-2,d)$ is itself a member, equivalently no two same-sector members differ by 2 in $n$ (gaps $\{3\}$ d=3, $\{17,52\}$ d=4, $\{5,7\}$ d=5, $\{22\}$ d=6, $\{5,14\}$ d=2). A member cannot radiatively decay to a member: a genuine self-consistency property of $\Sigma$. **Result (iii):** it is not selective — within each sector "no two 2 apart" admits many same-parity subsets (47 candidates in d=2, 36 in d=4, …). Net: the radiative channel does not by itself select the even-level set; the residue is a set-level self-consistency (Σ downward-independent, and every member's downward target absent) that the generation tower satisfies but that many other sets also satisfy — the pinning is still the tower combinatorics, consistent with every prior null. T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

**Addendum — per-sector level-parity anatomy: the charged-lepton sectors are the unique purely even-level sectors (🔵, 2026-06-14).** Tabulating the level parity ($N=n-1$; $l=0$ present iff $n$ odd, the "even-level" class) sector by sector over the 15 members: $d=2$ (photon $n{=}0$, $W\,76$, $Z\,81$, $H\,95$), $d=3$ ($1,4$), $d=4$ ($3,20,72$), and $d=5$ ($10,15,22$) are each parity-**mixed**, whereas $d=6$ ($e\,13$, $\mu\,35$) and $d=10$ ($\tau\,23$) are **purely even-level** — every charged lepton has $n$ odd, so all three carry the $l=0$ contact harmonic. No sector is purely odd-level. Two consequences. (i) The structural correlate of charged-lepton point-likeness: the leptons are exactly the modes whose every member carries the $s$-wave/$l=0$ contact, while the quark ($d=3,4$) and neutrino ($d=5$) sectors mix $l=0$ and $l\ge2$ content. (ii) The purely-even-level pair $\{6,10\}$ is exactly the $\mu$–$\tau$-degenerate pair $g_{66}=g_{10,10}=1/n_s$ (T9c, $v_6=v_{10}=1/2$) and the Koide-exact pair (§23): three independent facets — pure even-level, coupling degeneracy, Koide exactness — attach to the same two terminal Hopf sectors, consistent with the meta-principle that the exact ($\bigstar$/$\checkmark$) lepton relations are the scale-free / prism-immune ones. Status $\textbf{🔵}$: the pattern is verified over the three charged leptons, but the oddness of $n=13,35,23$ is observed from the tower values, not derived; the natural structural home is the $6/10$ degeneracy, not a separate parity law. T0.5 unchanged; no Part edited.

### §23. Koide lepton-mass relation as a scale-free simplex identity (2026-06-06)

**Conjecture.** The Koide relation $Q = (m_e+m_\mu+m_\tau)/(\sqrt{m_e}+\sqrt{m_\mu}+\sqrt{m_\tau})^2 = 2/3$ (empirical to ~5 sig figs; listed "not derived" in `IDWT_paper.md`) follows from the IDWT lepton-sector structure.

**Setup.** Charged leptons: $e,\mu$ at $d=6$ ($n=13,35$); $\tau$ at $d=10$ ($n=23$, back-reaction $1+1/1680$). The lepton sectors share one mass scale, $m_{\rm scale,6}=m_{\rm scale,10}$ (Part 2 §9, Part 3 §0.8b). Each mass is that common scale times a pure simplex number, so the scale **cancels** in Koide's degree-0 ratio: $Q$ depends only on $S(13,6)=18564$, $S(35,6)=3{,}838{,}380$, and $S(23,10)(1+1/1680)=64{,}550{,}640$.

**Checked:**
- $Q_{\rm IDWT} = 0.666661$ vs $2/3 = 0.666667$ — deviation $-0.001\%$. Bare $S(23,10)$ (no back-reaction) gives $Q=0.66664$; the $+1/1680$ correction sharpens it.
- Non-triviality: with $e,\mu$ fixed, $Q$ swings strongly with the tau index — $n{=}21{:}\,0.591$, $22{:}\,0.629$, $\mathbf{23{:}\,0.6667}$, $24{:}\,0.702$, $25{:}\,0.736$. The index that the generation-tower co-fixed-point selection picks **independently** (n=23) is the one that lands on $2/3$.

**Result — two parts: a real positive reframing, and a PROVEN negative on the headline ("forced?") question.**

*Positive (structural, holds):* because the $d{=}6$ and $d{=}10$ leptons share one mass scale ($m_{\rm scale,6}=m_{\rm scale,10}$), $Q$ is exactly scale-free and reduces to a relation among three cross-sector simplex integers. At the independently selected indices $(13,35,23)$, $Q=0.6666611$ — within $8.3$ ppm of $2/3$, where neighbouring tau indices miss by whole percent ($n{=}22{:}\,0.6290$, $n{=}24{:}\,0.7024$). A genuine "structural near-coincidence."

*Negative (PROVEN, 2026-06-06): Koide $Q=2/3$ is NOT an algebraic identity of the simplex values.* Proof. Set $a=S(13,6),\,b=S(35,6),\,c=S(23,10)(1+\tfrac1{1680})$. Then
$$Q=\tfrac23 \iff (\sqrt a+\sqrt b+\sqrt c)^2=\tfrac32(a+b+c)\iff \sqrt{ab}+\sqrt{bc}+\sqrt{ca}=\tfrac{a+b+c}{4}.\quad(*)$$
The right side of $(*)$ is rational ($a,b\in\mathbb{Z}$; $c=451854481/7\in\mathbb{Q}$). But $a=2^2\!\cdot3\cdot7\cdot13\cdot17$ and $b=2^2\!\cdot3\cdot5\cdot7\cdot13\cdot19\cdot37$, so $ab=2^4\!\cdot3^2\!\cdot5\cdot7^2\!\cdot13^2\!\cdot17\cdot19\cdot37$ has squarefree part $5\cdot17\cdot19\cdot37=59755\neq1$; hence $\sqrt{ab}=1092\sqrt{59755}$ is irrational. A sum of square roots of positive rationals is rational only if each root is rational, and the three terms of $(*)$ are all positive (no cancellation). With $\sqrt{ab}$ irrational, the left side of $(*)$ is irrational, contradicting the rational right side. Therefore $(*)$ is impossible and $Q\neq2/3$ exactly. $\blacksquare$ Numerically $(*)$ misses by $426.7$ in $1.71\times10^7$ ($Q-2/3=-5.5\times10^{-6}$).

**Cross-sector extension (2026-06-06, null).** Each sector triple is (one common scale)×(combinatorial factor), so a scale-free $Q$ exists for all four. Computed: charged leptons $Q=0.6667$ (=2/3, −0.001%); up $(u,c,t)$ $Q=0.849$; down $(d,s,b)$ $Q=0.731$; neutrinos $(\nu_1,\nu_2,\nu_3)$ $Q=0.477$ (corr.) / $0.475$ (bare). Only the charged leptons hit a simple fraction. Best low-denominator rationals for the others are 17/20 (up, off 0.12%), 11/15 (down, off 0.35%), 9/19 (ν, off ~0.2–0.8%) — i.e. denominator $\sim$15–20 matched only to $\sim10^{-3}$, which is the generic spacing of denominator-20 fractions and therefore not structural. $Q$ simply tracks each sector's mass-hierarchy span ($Q\to1$ steep, $Q\to1/3$ degenerate). So Koide's $2/3$ is charged-lepton-specific — matching the empirical fact that Koide works for leptons and fails for quarks/neutrinos — and reveals no new cross-sector pattern. Do not re-chase clean-fraction $Q$ in the quark/neutrino sectors.

**Conclusion.** The "is Koide forced by the simplex structure?" question is settled: no. This is the expected and honest answer — the empirical Koide relation is itself only approximate ($\sim10^{-5}$), not an exact law; IDWT reproduces the lepton masses and therefore reproduces the empirical $Q\approx2/3$ to the same accuracy, without elevating it to a theorem (so it is not independent evidence beyond the mass fit). What stands as IDWT content is the scale-free reduction to three cross-sector simplex integers and the 8-ppm near-coincidence at the selected indices. Status: ⭐ for the non-identity proof (pure number theory); 🔵 for the structural near-coincidence. Do not re-attempt to prove $Q=2/3$ exact — it is provably not.

### §24. Null-model significance of the parameter-free dimensionless postdictions (2026-06-06)

**Question (self-directed).** A skeptic's first objection to any "masses from integers" theory is that the formula is flexible enough to fit anything. Quantify it: how unlikely is IDWT's agreement with the precisely-measured *dimensionless, parameter-free* quantities — treating every mode index as a *free* integer (maximally skeptical), with the sector scales only as derived from $m_e$ and $n_s$ (verified in `idwt.py`: $m_{\rm scale,d}$ come from the tower couplings, not refit per sector)?

**Method** (`idwt.py` STEP 38). For each quantity that is a ratio of simplex numbers fixed by one free index: $\varepsilon=|{\rm pred}-{\rm obs}|/{\rm obs}$ (floored at measurement error); grid spacing $g = S(n{+}1,d)/S(n,d)-1$ (the simplex grid is coarse at large $n$, so a tight hit is not generic even picking the nearest integer); luck $L=\min(1,2\varepsilon/g)$ — the chance the nearest grid point lands within $\varepsilon$ of the true value. Joint $=\prod L$ over independent indices/measurements.

**Quantities** (precisely measured, no correction-knob except the τ back-reaction):

| quantity | IDWT | obs | $\varepsilon$ | grid $g$ | $L$ |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| $m_\mu/m_e=S(35,6)/S(13,6)$ | 206.7647 | 206.76828 | $1.7\times10^{-5}$ | 0.171 | $2.0\times10^{-4}$ |
| $m_\tau/m_e=\tfrac{S(23,10)}{S(13,6)}(1{+}\tfrac1{1680})$ | 3477.19 | 3477.37 | $5.1\times10^{-5}$ | 0.435 | $2.3\times10^{-4}$ |
| $m_Z/m_W=S(81,2)/S(76,2)$ | 1.13500 | 1.13461 | $3.4\times10^{-4}$ | 0.0247 | $2.7\times10^{-2}$ |
| $m_H/m_W=S(95,2)/S(76,2)$ | 1.55844 | 1.55781 | $4.1\times10^{-4}$ | 0.0211 | $8.5\times10^{-2}$ |

(τ row: PDG 2024, $m_\tau = 1776.93\pm0.09$ MeV; its $\varepsilon$ is the measurement floor, fit residual $4.9\times10^{-5}$.) Joint $\approx1.1\times10^{-10}$ (≈1 in $9\times10^{9}$); even with a generous look-elsewhere ($\times100$ candidate quantities) $\sim10^{-8}$ (~$5\sigma$-scale). The two lepton ratios dominate because the $d=6,10$ grids are coarse — a sub-$10^{-4}$ hit on a 17–43% grid is the strong part.

**Result and the honest reading.** Even granting the skeptic *every index as a free integer*, the precisely-measured dimensionless ratios sit on the simplex grid far more tightly than a flexible fit would produce: the spectrum is **not** a generic "fit anything" structure. Caveats: (i) the $2\varepsilon/g$ luck model is order-of-magnitude, not a rigorous likelihood; (ii) conditional on the scales being derived (verified) not refit; (iii) selection is principled (precisely-measured + parameter-free) — looser predictions exist and are not cherry-pick-excluded ($g_A$ +4%, $f_\pi$ +2.1%, nucleon moments use fitted parameters). **Key structural point:** the *full* evidential weight hinges on whether the indices are forced from $n_s$ — the open T0.5 problem. If forced: ~2 inputs → these outputs, overwhelming. If free: still $\sim10^{-8}$ from grid tightness alone. Either way T0.5 is the load-bearing question; closing it converts an already-significant postdiction into a near-parameter-free one. Status: 🔵 (statistical, order-of-magnitude). Written up in Part 5 §2a with `idwt.py` STEP 38; superseded as the quantitative statement by the follow-up below (Part 5 §2b, STEP 39).

**Follow-up (2026-06-09): exact joint p-value + random-theory Monte Carlo** (`idwt.py` STEP 39; Part 5 §2b). The heuristic $\prod L$ replaced by two proper null models.

*Null A — random target position.* H0: each measured value sits at a uniformly random position in its local inter-rung cell, so the normalized distance to the nearest rung is $p\sim U(0,1)$; with measurement floor $f=\min(1,2\sigma/g)$ the per-quantity luck is $L=\max(p,f)$; statistic $X=-\sum\ln L_i$; joint $p=P(X\ge X_{\rm obs})$ computed exactly (convolution of the per-quantity densities, MC-validated at every resolvable tail depth) and by Fisher's $\chi^2_{2k}$ closed form (conservative under floors). Quantity set fixed by a pre-stated rule — dimensionless, parameter-free, measurement resolves the grid ($\sigma<g/2$): the four §24 ratios plus $\sin\theta_C$, $m_s/m_d$, $m_t/m_c$, $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ (8 quantities; conservative grid convention $\min$ over $n\to n\pm1$; one free index per quantity, the other anchored — the "both free" objection is Null B's job). The PMNS angles and $m_c/m_u$ fail the resolution rule (grid finer than current errors — uninformative either way); as consistency checks they pull $+0.30\sigma$, $+0.13\sigma$, $+0.19\sigma$, $-0.00\sigma$. Inputs: PDG 2024 + FLAG 2024 ($m_s/m_d = 19.81(13)$ — IDWT's 20 is $+1.5\sigma$, the largest pull in the set, scored as found). **Result: $X_{\rm obs}=31.56$, joint $p = 8.9\times10^{-11}$ (6.4σ) exact; $1.5\times10^{-7}$ (5.1σ) Fisher-conservative; $\times100$ look-elsewhere $\to 8.9\times10^{-9}$ (5.6σ); core-4 subset $3.8\times10^{-7}$ (4.9σ).**

*Null B — random theories.* Every mode index drawn independently and uniformly from its window (sector mass ≤ 1 TeV at the seed-chain scales; d=5 ≤ 1 eV: windows d=2:269, d=3:107, d=4:111, d=5:41, d=6:169, d=10:47); all 12 quantities recomputed per draw ($g_{55}$ fixed by seeds); scored by $T=\sum\ln\varepsilon_{{\rm eff},i}$. **Result: 0 of $8.4\times10^6$ draws (incl. halved/doubled-window runs) matched as well as IDWT $\Rightarrow p_B < 5\times10^{-7}$ (95% CL) at the stated windows; best random theory short by 36 ln-units.** Per-quantity chance match rates: $m_\mu/m_e$ $3\times10^{-5}$, $m_\tau/m_e$ 0 in all draws, $m_Z/m_W$ $2\times10^{-4}$, $m_H/m_W$ $4\times10^{-4}$, others $10^{-3}$–$10^{-2}$, PMNS $10^{-2}$–$0.3$. Status: 🔵 (statistical, now a proper likelihood under the stated nulls). The conclusion of the original audit stands with rigorous arithmetic; the load-bearing open question remains T0.5.

### §25. Tower edges as condensate matrix elements; the subtractive-edge sign (F5/F16, 2026-06-09)

Source: Fable-5 findings F5/F16/F9; computation `files/idwt.py` STEP 41. Oscillator proxy (T1: level $n\leftrightarrow$ Hermite degree $k=n-1$); the P6 condensate-linearized kernel supplies the degree-1 vertex (a single $\xi$ insertion).

**Additive edges = one degree-1 condensate insertion at top-of-band (⭐).** Each additive tower edge $n_c=n_a+n_b$ — $n_e=n_{\nu_1}+n_u$, $n_\mu=n_{\nu_2}+n_c$, $n_\tau=n_{\nu_3}+n_d$ — is the matrix element $\langle H_{n_c-1}\,|\,x\,|\,H_{n_a-1}H_{n_b-1}\rangle$ taken at its top-of-band component. The top coefficient is the leading-coefficient ratio $2^{k_a+k_b}/2^{k_a+k_b+1}=\tfrac12$ — positive, nonzero, with no leakage above (verified exactly per edge). So the single degree-1 raising insertion lands precisely at $n_c=n_a+n_b$, giving the additive DAG edges a kernel-matrix-element reading. (This corrects the F5-strengthened note's transcription "$\Leftrightarrow n_c=n_a+n_b-1$"; the bookkeeping $(n_c-1)=(n_a-1)+(n_b-1)+1$ gives $n_c=n_a+n_b$.)

**The unique subtractive edge carries the inclusion-exclusion minus (T8 gap (ii)).** $n_{\nu_3}=n_{\nu_1}+n_{\nu_2}-n_u$ is the one edge with a net degree change $-(n_u-1)=-2$ relative to the product — a lowering, opposite to the additive raising. The $-n_u$ is inclusion-exclusion (Part 2 §9c: $n_{\nu_1}=S(n_u,3)$ and $n_{\nu_2}=S(n_u,4)$ share the seed $n_u$, counted once too many), i.e. the cumulant/connected-correlator minus sign $\langle AB\rangle_c=\langle AB\rangle-\langle A\rangle\langle B\rangle$. The electron ($n_e=13$, itself seed-built) overlaps the subtracted shared-seed leg, so the $W[e,3]$ coupling inherits the minus: $\partial U_{e3}/\partial\theta_{13}|_{0^+}<0$ relative to the positive additive edges. This is the convention-independent **relative** sign that Part 10 §2 asserts; the overall branch ($\delta\to\pi$) is the PDG-convention bracket already stated in Part 10 §4. Identifies the mechanism for T8 gap (ii); gaps (i) and (iii) are untouched, so T8 stays 🔶.

**Photon protection consistency (F9).** The condensate vertex $2(\xi_d\!\cdot\!\langle\xi_{d'}\rangle)(\xi_d\!\cdot\!\delta\xi_{d'})$ is degree 1 (odd) only in the fluctuation leg $\delta\xi_{d'}$ and degree 2 (even) in the spectator leg $\xi_d$; the photon's own $d=2$ leg is always the even spectator, so $m_\gamma=0$ (Part 3 §16.2) survives the degree-1 vertices that drive the tower edges.

Placement: the explicit gap-(ii) mechanism is recorded in Part 10 §2 (with the matching wording in the §4 status note), here, and in `idwt.py` STEP 41. T8 remains 🔶 — gaps (i) and (iii) are untouched, and the overall branch stays the §4 convention bracket.

**Addendum — full production census in segment terms; the insertion dichotomy (❓, 2026-06-10, Fedge late-split discussion).** Writing every production of the tower DAG as $n_c = \sum(\text{operands}) - \text{overlap}$ (rungs of a common ladder; sharing $k$ rungs subtracts $k$), all 13 productions are consistent and the overlap takes only four values:

| overlap | productions | reading |
|---|---|---|
| 0 | additive edges e, μ, τ, H-additive | one degree-1 condensate insertion above level addition (the ⭐ result above; the "+1 joint rung") |
| 1 | every g-rule join: up-from-strange, W, Z, H | exact level addition — insertion-free; shares one rung |
| n_u = 3 | ν₃ | shared-base inclusion-exclusion (documented above) |
| n_charm−1 = 19 | top ($S(n_e,2) - (n_{\rm charm}-1)$) | the §12 factor 19, appearing here as an overlap |

The new content beyond the ⭐ result above is the dichotomy: the fermion-type edges all carry exactly one condensate insertion (overlap 0), while every g-rule join — which produces the three heavy bosons and the up — is insertion-free pure level addition (overlap 1). Hockey-stick evaluations (ν₁, ν₂, charm) are themselves segment concatenations of the lower Pascal column, which is just the identity restated. Status ❓: a consistent organizing reading with two genuinely patterned cells (the insertion dichotomy; the factor-19 overlap), no mechanism for why boson joins are insertion-free. Companion Test A (sector assignment from blind-lattice invariants) is the §15 null of the same date.

**The d=2 even-insertion selection rule — mechanism for the insertion dichotomy (🔶, 2026-06-10).** The dichotomy above reduces to documented structure. The degree-1 condensate vertex exists only where a sector condensate $\langle\xi_{d'}\rangle\neq0$ supplies the linearization (Part 1 P6, STEP 41); and the all-orders photon-mass theorem states that the condensate-linearized vertices "remain even (degree 2) in the photon's own d=2 variable" (Part 3 §16.2) — there is no odd vertex in the d=2 variable, the same fact that protects $m_\gamma = 0$ in condensate backgrounds. Proposed selection rule: **a tower production landing on a d=2 mode carries an even number of condensate insertions in its own variable; matter-sector targets are unconstrained.** Checked in the T1 Hermite proxy (top-of-band landing exact in all cases):

- W, Z, H g-joins: 0 insertions (even ✓), landing at $n_f + d - 1$ with the $-1$ as the shared vacuum unit (✅, Part 3 §11);
- the Higgs additive closure $n_H = n_u + n_{\rm charm} + n_{\rm top}$ (🔶, Part 2 §6): exactly 2 insertions (even ✓) — the rule renders the two documented Higgs routes mutually consistent rather than competing;
- fermion edges e, μ, τ: exactly 1 insertion (odd — available only off d=2);
- counterfactual odd-insertion boson indices 77, 82, 96 are unoccupied; insertion-free fermion counterfactuals 12, 34 unoccupied (22 is occupied but as (22,5)=ν₃, a different sector).

One structural fact — no d=2 condensate — thus yields both $m_\gamma = 0$ and the boson $-1$: the insertion dichotomy is the photon-protection mechanism seen from the production side. Honest limits: (i) the bridge from single-variable proxy insertion count to multi-leg vertex L-parity in the d=2 variable is stated, not derived — that is the 🔶 gap; (ii) the rule does not explain why matter edges use exactly one insertion (odd is allowed, not forced); (iii) it does not single out routes — even-insertion alternative boson routes exist arithmetically (e.g. top+up+down = 76; the §15 route-multiplicity null applies), so the rule constrains channel parity, not route choice.

Placed (2026-06-10, Fedge-approved): `idwt.py` STEP 55; Part 3 §11 (mechanism paragraph after the −1 derivation); Part 3 §16.2 (production-side corollary); Part 2 §6 (insertion-parity note before the n_u status paragraph). Carries 🔶 in all locations with limits (i)–(iii) summarised in Part 3 §11.

**Addendum — ray-classification audit of the dimensionless postdictions (consistent, 2026-06-10; late-prism move (a)).** Test of the late-prism prediction that a dimensionless quantity built within one ray (one sector scale, the degenerate $d=6/d=10$ pair, or a pure angle) is prism-immune — fixed at the integer layer, so its only residual is a pure-number (Level-2) correction plus measurement floor — while a quantity crossing rays carries derived scale ratios (Level-1 residuals). Classified the STEP 39 resolving set (8 quantities plus the $m_c/m_u$ consistency check) and recomputed residuals against PDG 2024. Findings: (i) every correction applied to an intra-ray quantity is a pure number with no scale ratio — GTC $\varepsilon=1/(280\sqrt7)$, back-reaction $1/1680$, $\nu_3$ shift $1/35$, Cabibbo curvature $1/240$ — the central auditable demand passes with no exceptions; (ii) no intra-ray quantity carries a large unexplained residual: $m_s/m_d$, $m_t/m_c$, $m_c/m_u$ and $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ sit within their measurement floors, and the scale-free $m_\mu/m_e=S(35,6)/S(13,6)$ sits at $1.7\times10^{-5}$ (its pure-simplex precision floor; it exceeds the $2\times10^{-9}$ mass-ratio measurement floor but carries no correction term and no scale dependence). Honest limit: the prediction's magnitude-separation form (intra-ray residual $<$ cross-ray) is only weakly confirmed — the worst intra-ray residual is $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ at $3.8\times10^{-2}$, larger than any cross-ray residual, but it is measurement-floor-limited (floor $2.6\times10^{-2}$), not unexplained. The discriminating content that passes is the correction-*type* prediction (pure number vs scale ratio), not the residual-magnitude ordering. Supports late-prism item 4; cross-checks the Part 2 §12 two-layer split without requiring an edit to it.

**Addendum — mixing angles are scale-free lattice quantities (consistent, 2026-06-10; late-prism move (b)).** Test of the prediction that the lattice/mass-basis misalignment is fixed before scales exist, so no mixing angle may carry a mass-scale ratio. Checks: (i) **scale-invariance** — rescaling every $m_{\text{scale},d}$ by an arbitrary $\kappa$ leaves all three PMNS angles unchanged ($\max|\Delta| = 0$); the CKM forms contain no scale token at all. (ii) **Scale-cancellation mechanism (the structural finding):** the PMNS angles, recomputed from the masses $m_{\text{scale},d}S(n,d)$ instead of the bare counts $S(n,d)$, give identical values — because every mode-pair a PMNS angle compares shares one scale. $\sin^2\theta_{12}$ compares $\nu_1,\nu_2$ (both $d=5$, intra-ray); $\sin^2\theta_{23}$ and $\sin^2\theta_{13}$ compare $n_\mu$ ($d=6$) with $n_\tau$ ($d=10$) — the degenerate pair $m_{\text{scale},6}=m_{\text{scale},10}$. The angles are scale-free not by a formula choice but because they only ever compare scale-sharing modes; a cross-ray pair would leave a surviving scale ratio and the angle would not be prism-immune. This is the same degeneracy that makes Koide (§23) and the audit-(a) $m_\tau/m_e$ entry prism-immune, here seen in the mixing sector. (iii) **Residuals** vs PDG 2024 all sit within measurement floor: CKM $\sin\theta_C$, $|V_{cb}|$, $A$ at $0.1$–$0.4\%$; PMNS $\sin^2\theta_{23,12,13}$ at $0.5$–$1.1\%$; $|V_{ub}|=|V_{td}|=0$ at tree level (the open non-zero route is the Hopf Chern–Simons geometric phase, Part 5 §3f — not a mass scale). (iv) corrections/couplings are pure numbers: Cabibbo $1+1/240=1+\chi(\mathbb{CP}^1)/(24\,S(n_s,3))$; $g_{55}=96/g_{22}=96/722.5$ rational ($\sqrt7$ cancels); $|V_{cb}|$ and $A$ bare simplex ratios with no correction. Honest form distinction: the CKM angles fit the strong "lattice number $\times$ small pure correction" form item 5 states literally; the PMNS angles fit only the weaker scale-free form — a rational-coupling-weighted ($g_{55}$) average of two lattice ratios, not a single lattice number with a perturbative correction. Both pass the falsifiable scale-content claim. Supports late-prism item 5; no document edit warranted — the mixing-angle derivations (Part 3 §12, Part 5 §3g–3i) already use only counts and couplings.

**Addendum — single-input structure, the algebraic split tower, and the k₀=16 "triple coincidence" audited to a double (2026-06-10; Fedge question: does the spectrum exist "all ×1" then split, or form as observed?).** Four results bearing on the late-prism hypothesis. (i) **One dimensional input.** Every sector scale satisfies $m_{\text{scale},d}=m_e\,c_d$ with $c_d$ a pure seed-built number ($m_{\text{scale},5}$ included, via the cross-sector fixed point $m_{\text{scale},5}m_{\text{scale},4}^2=(n_u/n_s)m_{\text{scale},6}^3$); the full 15-mass spectrum is $m_e\times[c_d\,S(n,d)]$ — one anchor plus the integer seed $n_s=4$. (Gravity adds a second input $\Lambda/G_\infty$, Part 4 §3.12.4; the mass spectrum does not.) (ii) **Algebraic split tower (⭐ identity).** The split factors $c_d=m_{\text{scale},d}/m_e$ form a clean minimal-polynomial-degree tower over $\mathbb{Q}$: $c_6=c_{10}=1/S(n_e,6)$ rational (deg 1); $c_2=\sqrt{g_{22}/g_{66}}$ and $c_5\propto\sqrt7$ quadratic (deg 2); $c_3=\sqrt{g_{33}/g_{66}}$ and $c_4$ quartic (deg 4, a $\sqrt{}$ of a $\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt7)$ number). The degree is set by how $\sqrt7=\sqrt{n_s+n_u}$ threads each scale formula (odd inner power of $\sqrt7\to$ quartic). The comb teeth $S(n,d)$ are integers, so the integer lattice and the scale overlay are genuinely distinct algebraic objects — the split carries integers to irrationals, not a trivial refactor — while both stay fixed by the one seed. (iii) **The k₀=16 "triple coincidence" is a double in cross-sector reach.** The three expressions $16=n_s^2=n_e+n_u=n_{\rm charm}-n_s$ all hold at $n_s=4$ (paper §5.3), but $n_s^2$ is the *definition* of $k_0$, and $n_{\rm charm}-n_s=n_s^2$ reduces to the $d=3$ simplex identity $S(n_s,3)=n_s(n_s+1)$ ($\Leftrightarrow(n_s+2)/6=1\Leftrightarrow n_s=4$) — internal to the quark sectors. The only equality reaching the $d=6$ lepton sector is $n_e+n_u=n_s^2$. Both $B=n_e+n_u$ and $C=n_{\rm charm}-n_s$ are $n_s=4$-specific (each singles out $n_s=4$ uniquely for $n_s<500$; their intersection $\{4\}$ re-derives the b-quark-beat uniqueness), but the genuinely cross-sector content is a double (quark-side $k_0\leftrightarrow$ lepton-side $n_e+n_u$), not a triple. The "triple coincidence" wording is literally correct as three coincident expressions; "double in cross-sector reach" measures a different quantity (how many of the three bridge two sectors), so the two statements do not conflict. RESOLVED (2026-06-10, Fedge): the late-prism ordering settles it in favour of "triple." Cross-sector reach is a post-prism notion — the index arithmetic lives in one sector-blind integer lattice and the sectors attach downstream — so at the layer where the coincidence lives there is no "quark-internal vs cross-sector" distinction to demote $C$ with; all three are integer-lattice characterizations on equal footing. Independent of prism timing, the precise structure is: $A$ is the definition; $B$ and $C$ are two *independent* non-trivial coincidences (their $n_s$-solution sets intersect only at $\{4\}$, so neither is redundant — $C$ is not "near-tautological"), each forcing the seed. The documents keep "triple coincidence," now affirmatively justified; Part 2 §8 gained one sentence stating the definition/two-coincidence split and the sole cross-sector index pair. (iv) **Discriminator (the answer to the question).** The dependency is asymmetric: $S(n,d)$ and the seed $n_s=4$ are pure combinatorics with no scale input ($n_s=4$ is selected by an integer eigenvalue condition, the $4/7$ resonance), while the scales $c_d$ are functions of the integers and nothing flows back. So the integer layer is **logically/generatively prior** to the scales — "integers first" follows from the dependency structure alone (⭐). The earlier "underdetermined / same object" reading conflated two questions: *observational* distinguishability of a temporal "before" (which would need a condensation equation of motion — not derived) is genuinely open, but the *generative-order* question is settled by the asymmetry. What remains ❓ is therefore only the dynamical dressing of the prism (a massless phase existing in cosmic time, a condensation event switching scales on), which "integers prior" does not depend on. Net: the late-prism's core ordering claim — the integers generate the scales — is established; the structural two-layer factorization (sector-blind integer comb × seed-locked irrational scales) is exact; only the thermal/temporal phase story stays open (move (d) of the late-prism notes). Wording item RESOLVED (2026-06-10, Fedge): "triple coincidence" kept across all locations (Part 2 §8, Part 5 §5, Part 6) — affirmatively justified by the late-prism sector-blind ordering, not merely tolerated. See the resolution under (iii) above.

### §26. Single-electron double slit — exact 6D separation, the marginal pattern, and the one-slit excitation (2026-06-10)

Question (Fedge): a d=6 electron passes through one slit — what carries the slit separation $D$ into its landing statistics, given the sector confinement? Resolved (all four checks pass).

1. **Where the asymmetry is (the keystone).** No three of the electron's six dimensions are special (Part 1 sector reality); the split in this experiment belongs to the apparatus. Panel, source, and screen are baryonic, hence d=3 structures (colour confinement, Part 1 §2.4): each has structure in its three dimensions and is uniform through the electron's other three. The sector well is the electron's own self-binding (width $L_6$, Part 4 §3.9) and marks out no direction; what it binds is the excitation, and it does not narrow the configuration the excitation rides. In the separated problem the well term enters on the coordinates the apparatus has no structure in — Part 8 §14.2 writes $V_6(|\xi_{4,5,6}|)$ for hydrogen, a split anchored there by the d=3 nucleus and here by the d=3 panel, not by the observer. "The electron is confined" (the excitation is compact) and "the configuration spans both slits" are statements about two different objects — both true. [Correction of record: this entry first framed the well as acting on "the hidden three" coordinates per se; Fedge flagged the 3+3 split as an observational artifact wrongly placed in the dynamics, and the article and this entry were rewritten apparatus-anchored, 2026-06-10.]
2. **Separation ✅.** The slit panel is a potential built from 3D sources → by the projection theorem (Part 3 §0.8a) uniform in $\xi_{4,5,6}$ → the 6D problem separates exactly (Lemma 1 structure): $\Psi=\psi(\mathbf{r},t)\,\chi(\xi)$ with the sector factor a spectator (marginal deviation between distinct $\chi$: $8\times10^{-16}$). Transmission counterpart of the §15 tunnelling entry (same mechanism, complementary face).
3. **Pattern ✅.** $\psi$ obeys the standard observable equation with the two-slit boundary; the d=3 marginal $|\psi|^2$ carries both scales — envelope from slit width, fringes at $\lambda L/D$ (measured/theory $=0.99$; Bach et al. 2013 geometry $\to 44\ \mu$m). Marginal Exactness (Part 11 §6.1) applied to the interferometer: IDWT moves no number. Slit height: aperture uniform along it → no structure along it (bands run parallel to the slits) — consistent with experiment.
4. **Trajectory layer 🔶 (logged for the record; ruled OUT of public articles by Fedge 2026-06-10 — articles carry established results only).** The IDWT wave equation implies continuity for the marginal with current $j=\mathrm{Im}(\psi^*\nabla\psi)/m$ — its own conservation law, not an import. Any definite-trajectory ontology reproducing the marginal at every plane (the Part 8 §14.4 frontier) must transport $\rho$ along $j$; integrating the canonical field $v=j/\rho$: 5000 trajectories, every one passes exactly one slit, zero symmetry-plane crossings, ensemble lands as the fringes (corr 0.978 with $|\psi|^2$), slit-B-blocked → envelope only, no fringes. Cross-framework disclosure: $v=j/\rho$ coincides with the de Broglie–Bohm guidance law; the IDWT motivation ("the excitation is a feature of the wave and moves with the wave's local transport") is stated, not derived — the excitation equation of motion remains the open item, hence 🔶. Which-path check: an orthogonal apparatus tag on one branch drops fringe visibility $1.000\to0.071$ while the envelope survives.

One line: the asymmetry is the panel's, the wave's configuration is at both slits, the electron is at one — $D$ enters through the configuration of the one wave the excitation rides.

**Addendum (2026-06-10, Fedge question: is the configuration channel the ONLY way?).** The derived kernel contact gate (§28, STEP 59–60) closes the alternatives quantitatively. An electron threading a slit of width 62 nm (Bach et al. geometry) passes no closer than ~31 nm to the panel walls; the kernel contact gate at that distance is $\ln\Omega = -(3.1\times10^4)^2/(2\cdot2) \approx -2.4\times10^8$ — identically zero. So not only the $D$-fringes but even the $w$-envelope cannot come from kernel contact with the panel: NO contact-class mechanism (bouncing, Duane-style panel momentum exchange) operates at slit scales in IDWT. The remaining channels each die independently: hidden-coordinate route — projection theorem (§15, §26 item 2); source-encoded statistics — delayed-choice (apparatus reconfigured in flight, statistics follow the final configuration); panel-only mechanisms — fringe visibility depends on the transverse coherence of the incident beam at fixed panel geometry, so the pattern tracks the prepared configuration, not the apparatus alone. What remains is the d=2 zero-mode (EM) shaping of the wave's observable-coordinate configuration — matter sculpting $\psi$ through the established couplings (the same structure as $V_{\rm Coulomb}$ entering the observable factor in Part 8 §14.2 Lemma 1), with the landing statistics the marginal of that configuration. The comb $S(n,d)$ filters the SECTOR factor — what an excitation is (mass, charge, sector) — not the observable configuration; the configuration's continuous, matter-coupled dynamics is the established wave equation itself. No new interaction channel is involved.

### §27. Sector-well covariance — the well rides with the mode; absolute-origin reading excluded (2026-06-10)

Question (Fedge, from the double-slit work): what anchors the sector well's coordinates; why does the well not impede free flight; how do Part 1 §3i (confined in all $d$ sector dimensions) and Part 8 §14.2 ($V_6$ on $\xi_{4,5,6}$ only) coexist?

**Exclusion of the absolute reading (✅ by reductio).** Part 4 §3.10's self-term $V_{\rm self}(\xi)=g\int|\chi(\xi')|^2(\xi\cdot\xi')^2 d\xi'$, read in absolute sector coordinates, gives a mode of internal spread $s$ centered at $X$ the displacement energy (exact for isotropic $\rho$, MC-confirmed)

$$U_A(X)/g = |X|^4 + (2s^2/d)|X|^2 + s^4/d,$$

a quartic pinning to the origin of $\Xi_d$. At hydrogen's Bohr radius ($a_0 \approx 5.3\times10^4$ in sector units, base unit $L_6/\lambda_6^{-1/4} \approx 1$ fm) the pinning term is $g\,U_A \approx 2\times10^{18}$ against an internal $E_0 = 3$: the absolute reading forbids macroscopic motion and is inconsistent with Part 8 §14.2's own ✅ Bohr spectrum. Excluded by the documents' established results.

**Mode-frame (covariant) reading (🔶 adopted as the minimal completion).** Evaluating the self-term in the mode's own frame, $V(\xi)=g\int|\chi(\xi')|^2((\xi-X)\cdot(\xi'-X))^2 d\xi'$ with $X$ the centroid: $U_B = g\,s^4/d$, $X$-independent. The §3.10.3 fixed point is untouched — $\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$, $E_0=d\sqrt{\lambda_d}$, $L_d=\lambda_d^{-1/4}$ reproduce §3.10.4 for all six sectors exactly, because §3.10 computed in the mode frame ($X=0$) all along; every published number is frame-local and unchanged. Label 🔶 because covariantization is a (minimal) completion of the kernel's written form, motivated rather than derived.

**Consequences (verified numerically).** (i) The well travels with the excitation: boost ansatz $\Psi=e^{i(P\cdot x-Et)}\chi(x-Vt)$ closes with $V=P/E$, $E^2=P^2+m^2$, $m^2$ the internal eigenvalue — Part 1 §3i's center motion recovered with no preferred coordinates. 1D nonrelativistic dynamics: the boosted self-bound mode translates at exactly $v$ (fitted 0.5000, width drift 0.00%, well co-moving); the absolute-kernel twin released at $X_0=5$ oscillates pinned in $[-5,5]$. (ii) "Bound within, free without" completes to: bound about its center in all $d$ of its dimensions; the center free in all of them. No three of a particle's dimensions are marked by the well. (iii) Hydrogen: the center's observable components feel the nucleus-anchored Coulomb term; internal structure spectates with smearing correction $\Delta E/|E_{1s}| = 4\sigma^2 = 2.86\times10^{-9}$ ($\sigma=L_6/a_0$; numeric = analytic to 4 digits) — same order as the proton-finite-size items Part 8 §14.4 catalogues. Part 8 §14.2's $H_{\rm eff}$ is exact to that accuracy with no 3+3 split of the well: §14.2's "$V_6(|\xi_{4,5,6}|)$" support is the spectating sector factor in the nucleus's split, not a property of the electron's six dimensions.

**Harmonization.** Part 1 §3i and Part 8 §14.2 are consistent under the covariant reading: "confined in its own $d$ sector dimensions" = internal structure bound about the traveling center, equally in all $d$; free flight = the center; the only special three in any experiment belong to the baryonic ($d=3$) apparatus. Parked sub-question: whether the cross-sector kernel terms $(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2$ need the same pair-frame reading (presumably yes; all established coupling numbers are frame-local evaluations, unchecked). Placed (2026-06-10, Fedge-approved): `idwt.py` STEP 58; Part 4 §3.10.2 (covariance note); Part 1 §3i (bound-within completion); Part 8 §14.2 (r/ξ split anchoring paragraph); notebook index regenerated.

### §28. Cross-sector kernel covariance — contact is a consequence, not an assertion (2026-06-10)

Question (spun off from §27; Fedge: "Derive it"): what is the covariant form of the cross-sector kernel terms $g_{dd'}(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2$, and do any established numbers change? (`idwt.py` STEP 59.)

**Setup.** Modes A (sector $d$, centroid $X_A$) and B (sector $d'$, centroid $X_B$) couple on their shared subspace ($d_{sh}=\min(d,d')$, Part 1 §3g); per-component shared-subspace variances $a^2, b^2$; $R = X_A - X_B$. Closed forms for all two-point covariant readings (each MC-verified):

| Reading | $U/g$ | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| absolute | $(X_A\cdot X_B)^2 + b^2\|X_A\|^2 + a^2\|X_B\|^2 + d_{sh}a^2b^2$ | changes under global translation — EXCLUDED ✅ |
| pair-centroid | $\|R/2\|^4 + (a^2+b^2)\|R/2\|^2 + d_{sh}a^2b^2$ | mutual quartic confinement of every pair ($g_{36}U_1 \approx 1.1\times10^{18}$ at $R=a_0$, vs Coulomb-only e–p) — EXCLUDED ✅ |
| each-own-frame | $d_{sh}a^2b^2$ | $R$-independent; pair energy never vanishes at separation (cluster decomposition fails) — EXCLUDED ✅ |

**Forced conclusion ✅.** No two-point polynomial moment survives. The only covariant reading left is contact-gated: $U(R) = g_{dd'}\,\Omega(R)\,d_{sh}a^2b^2$ with $\Omega(0)=1$, decaying on the mode-width scale. The $(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2$ factor is the local geometry of the coupling at a contact event, evaluated in the contact frame — exactly how every established coupling computation uses it, so all published values are $\Omega(0)=1$ evaluations, unchanged. "The kernel is a contact structure" (Part 3 §0.6; Part 11 §6.3 premise) is thereby a structural consequence of covariance. At $A=B$, $R=0$ the form reduces to the §27 / STEP 58 self-term $g s^4/d$ (verified to 1e-12).

**Gate profile — derived ✅ (addendum 2026-06-10, same day; Fedge: "Do both"; `idwt.py` STEP 60).** Three established inputs fix $\Omega$ uniquely: (i) the kernel action term is bilinear in the kernel currents ($L_{dd'} = (g/2)\int(\xi\cdot\xi')^2 JJ$, Part 3 §0.6) — linear in each mode's intensity — so the pair energy is a bilinear functional $U = \iint \rho_A(x)\rho_B(y)F(x-y)$; (ii) covariance + the exclusions above force $F$ to decay; (iii) the action carries no length constant of its own (the $g_{dd'}$ are dimensionless seed-built numbers), so $F$ has zero intrinsic range — the scale-free point contact. Hence $\Omega(R) = [\rho_A\star\tilde\rho_B](R)/[\rho_A\star\tilde\rho_B](0)$, the normalized density overlap. Gaussian sector ground modes: $\Omega(R) = \exp(-R^2/(2(a^2+b^2)))$, range $\sqrt{a^2+b^2}$. Corollary (exact): same-sector contact range $= \sqrt{2\sigma_d^2} = \lambda_d^{-1/4} = L_d$ — the sector localization length IS the same-sector contact range. Ranges (sector units ≈ fm): e–e $= L_6 = 1.414$ — the Part 11 §6.3 range premise, derived; e–p 1.108; quark–quark (3,4) 0.780 — sub-fm strong-force scale; e–τ 1.414; ν–e 1.495. Gate at $R=a_0$: $\ln\Omega \approx -1.1\times10^9$ (the e–p kernel contact term in hydrogen is closed beyond any bound). Long-range physics untouched: EM is the massless non-compact d=2 zero mode (no width gate; Part 3 §16, §0.8a); gravity is curvature (Part 4 §1).

Placed (2026-06-10): `idwt.py` STEP 59, STEP 60; Part 4 §3.10.1 (covariance note, cross terms + gate derivation); Part 3 §0.6 (contact-as-consequence sentence); Part 11 §6.3 (premise-derived pointer); notebook index regenerated.

### §29. Internucleon contact range — deuteron inverse check (2026-06-10)

Question (Fedge: "Do both", second half): does the derived kernel contact range survive quantitative contact with nuclear physics? (`idwt.py` STEP 61; placed in Part 8 §11.)

Nucleons are d=3 colour-singlet composites (Part 1 §2.4) → the N–N kernel gate carries the derived same-sector range $L_3 = \lambda_3^{-1/4} = 0.675$ (sector units ≈ fm). Independent cross-check: a gate built from the measured proton charge radius ($\sigma^2 = r_p^2/3$, $r_p = 0.8409$ fm CODATA) gives 0.687 — the d=3 sector width and the measured nucleon size agree to 2%.

**Inverse check (range fixed, depth solved for).** Contact well $V(r) = -V_0\exp(-r^2/(2R_c^2))$ (the gate profile itself), reduced mass $m_{N,\rm IDWT}/2$, Numerov shooting on the s-wave at the measured deuteron binding $E_B = 2.224566$ MeV (CODATA):

| gate | $R_c$ (fm) | $V_0$ (MeV) | $V_0/\Lambda$ ($\Lambda = N_c f_\pi = 282$ MeV) |
|---|---|---|---|
| N–N ($L_3$) | 0.675 | 154 | 0.55 |
| q–q (3,4) | 0.780 | 120 | 0.42 |
| N–N (measured $r_p$) | 0.687 | 150 | 0.53 |

The depth the kernel must supply is an order-unity fraction of the IDWT hadronic scale. The solved mode's rms half-separation is 1.79 fm vs the measured deuteron matter radius ≈ 1.97 fm (shallow-state universality). 🔵 Status: the range is fixed by the derived gate (✅-chain from §28); the depth $V_0$ is the open number — same class as the Part 8 §11 confinement-level problem. NOT an identification or a binding prediction; an inverse constraint that the kernel's eventual depth derivation must hit ($V_0 \approx 0.55\Lambda$ at the $L_3$ gate). 🔶

**Addendum — second-order structure selected; required depth = Λ within 2% (same day, 2026-06-10; Fedge: "Finish it all if possible"; `idwt.py` STEP 62).** The first-order profile above was the placeholder; the established colour energy law selects the order. Two colour singlets have $\vec N_A = \vec N_B = 0$, so the first-order inter-singlet colour energy vanishes ($E = \lambda_c|\vec N|$, Part 8 §5.3): the leading N–N kernel term is SECOND order in the gated contact (colour van der Waals, the §17b mechanism in the colour sector), which squares the gate — $V(R) = -V_0\,\Omega(R)^2$, $R_c = (\text{gate range})/\sqrt2$: $L_3$ gate $\to 0.477$, $r_p$ gate $\to 0.486$. Profile and range carry no freedom; $V_0 = \kappa^2/\Delta$ ($\kappa$ = singlet→non-singlet contact matrix element, $\Delta$ = non-singlet gap; both $\lambda_c$-class). Inverse result: measured $E_B = 2.2246$ MeV requires $V_0 = 288.9$ MeV $= 1.02\,\Lambda$ ($L_3$ gate) and $280.0$ MeV $= 0.99\,\Lambda$ ($r_p$ gate), $\Lambda = N_c f_\pi = 282$ MeV — **the required depth equals the hadronic scale within 2% on both gates**. 🔵 Forward, parameter-free ($V_0 = \Lambda$ exactly): $E_B = 1.62$ / $2.43$ MeV ($L_3$/$r_p$), bracketing the measured 2.2246; shallow-state depth sensitivity makes the inverse form the robust statement. rms(r/2) = 1.71 fm vs measured ~1.97. Remaining open: derive $\kappa,\Delta$ (equivalently $\lambda_c$) from the kernel; spin-tensor channel (deuteron is spin-1; this is central s-wave). Placed: Part 8 §11 (block rewritten: range ✅ / form ✅ / depth-measured 🔵 / open 🔶); `idwt.py` STEP 62.

**Addendum — κ and Δ from large-N_c colour structure (2026-06-10; `idwt.py` STEP 63).** The IDWT large-N_c structure (N_c = χ(CP²) = 3) fixes the leading-order identification. (a) κ = √N_c × Λ: each of the N_c quarks contributes colour amplitude Λ at the hadronic threshold (g_eff = 1 at n = n_s in the d=3 sector), and their baryon-level sum carries the standard √N_c large-N_c enhancement → κ = √3 × 282 MeV ≈ 489 MeV. (b) Δ = N_c × Λ (one-baryon colour excitation gap): the colour energy law E = λ_c|N⃗| with |ΔN⃗| = 2 for one colour flip (root-vector length from |n⃗|² = 4/3, Part 8 §5.3), together with the baryon confinement energy ≈ N_c Λ (proton mass formula), gives Δ = λ_c × 2 = N_c Λ ≈ 846 MeV; hence λ_c = N_c Λ/2 = N_c² f_π/2 ≈ 423 MeV. (c) V₀ = κ²/Δ = N_c Λ²/(N_c Λ) = Λ — **exact in large-N_c power counting, no free coefficient**. 🔶 Status: the O(1) coefficients are the leading large-N_c values; exact kernel matrix elements require collective-mode identification of the colour-singlet baryon (same open problem as §5.3 λ_c). Spin-tensor channel (³S₁–³D₁ for J=1 deuteron) remains open.

### §30. The complete mass spectrum as a closed form in $N_c$ (⭐, 2026-06-10)

**What was checked.** Whether every one of the fifteen SM masses can be written $m = m_e\times f(N_c)$ with $f$ an exact closed form in the single integer $N_c=\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)=3$ — the spectrum-level completion of T15, which previously traced the mode indices and couplings (not the masses with corrections) to $N_c$ (sympy exact arithmetic).

**Result (positive, ⭐).** All fifteen close. Each $f$ is assembled from three $N_c$-determined layers — the simplex counts $S(n,d)$ (indices via T15d), the six scale ratios $m_{{\rm scale},d}/m_e$ (T9/T11/T15c–e), and the four corrections — with no constant entering from outside the $N_c$-chain. The corrections are themselves $N_c$-pure: $\varepsilon = (2/\sqrt{2N_c+1})/[(N_c+1)^2 S(N_c{+}1,4)]$, $\delta_\tau = 1/[N_c(N_c+1)^2 S(N_c{+}1,4)]$, $\delta_{\nu_3}=1/S(N_c{+}1,4)$, reducing at $N_c=3$ to $1/(280\sqrt7)$, $1/1680$, $1/35$. Substituting $N_c=3$ reproduces the canonical `idwt.py` masses to machine precision: **maximum relative deviation $5.7\times10^{-16}$ across all fifteen.** Sample closed forms: $f_e\equiv1$ (anchor); $f_{\rm up}=\sqrt{N_c}(N_c+1)/(2N_c+1)^{1/4}$; $f_{\rm strange}=\sqrt2(N_c+1)^{5/2}(N_c+2)(N_c+3)(2N_c+1)^{1/4}/12$; the boson and $\nu$ forms are nested-binomial rationals in $N_c$ (full list in the script output).

**Status and placement.** ⭐ identity-level: it is an algebraic consequence of the already-established $N_c$-forms of indices, couplings, and corrections — it asserts the spectrum's *form*, $m_e\times f(N_c)$, not the accuracy of the underlying derivations (those keep their own labels). The single dimensional input is $m_e$; mass ratios are fixed by $N_c$ alone. No new numerical value enters — every quantity already lives in `idwt.py` (the corrections at lines 404/440/449 are already in seed-traceable form). Placed: Part 9 Corollary T15g.

### §31. The three-ray law: tower depth and sector dimension are linearly locked (2026-06-12, Fedge directive)

**What was searched.** Joint patterns over the triple (mode index n, tower depth k, sector dimension d), at Fedge's direction. Depth is the minimal-route derivation depth k_min: the length of the shortest documented derivation (Part 2 §6 DAG plus the idwt.py STEP 1 cross-check routes), computed by relaxation — seeds and the photon at depth 0; the T15 Euler product $n_{\rm top} = \chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)\chi(\mathbb{CP}^5)$ counted as a depth-1 production from geometric constants (run #5: the top is an irreducible input, not derived from lighter modes). Resulting depths: photon, down, up = 0; strange, ν₁, ν₂, top = 1; charm, μ, e, ν₃, W = 2; τ, Z, H = 3.

**Result (the pattern): every matter mode and the photon — 12 of the 15 — satisfies $d - k_{\min} \in \{2, 3, 4\}$ exactly.** The spectrum occupies three parallel slope-1 rays in the (k, d) plane, each anchored at one of the three depth-0 modes:

| ray | anchor (k=0) | k=1 | k=2 | k=3 |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| d = k+2 | photon (d=2) | strange (d=3) | charm (d=4) | — |
| d = k+3 | down (d=3) | top (d=4) | ν₃ (d=5) | — |
| d = k+4 | up (d=4) | ν₁, ν₂ (d=5) | e, μ (d=6) | τ (d=7 slot → 10) |

Equivalently: **each derivation step advances the sector dimension by exactly one** — the tower climbs the Hopf chain at one dimension per depth step, in three parallel fronts offset by the anchors' dimensions {2, 3, 4}. Three structural features fall out:

- **The τ displacement is the ray hitting the excluded sector.** The d = k+4 ray at depth 3 lands on d = 7 — the S⁷ total space excluded by Rule A — and the τ sits in d = 10, the terminal sector, instead. The ray law predicts *where* the displacement must occur (the seed ray, depth 3) and the exclusion mechanism is already documented (T3); the two fit together with no adjustment.
- **The heavy bosons are off-ray.** W, Z, H (all d = 2, depths 2, 3, 3) are the only modes violating the ray law — precisely the g-rule cascade off the top (§15 run #5). The gauge branch is orthogonal to the dimensional climb: matter climbs, the cascade drops to d=2.
- **A timing corollary with selective power.** Matter sector d is occupiable only at depths $d-4 \le k \le d-2$: d=3 closes after depth 1, d=4 after depth 2. Added as a gate to the run-#8 closure, this cuts the d=3 false positives from 95 to 5 and d=4 to 36 (total FP 556 → 412; the d ≥ 5 sectors stay saturated because the late-depth value pool is large). It is the first documented gate that constrains *when* a sector can fire rather than the production channel type.

**Companion observations.** (i) New closed form $n_{\nu_3} = S(a, 5) + 1$ — the seed chain $S(a,3), S(a,4)$ continued into the ν's own sector d=5, with the universal +1 = n_down attaching at the home-sector step; equals the documented inclusion-exclusion form identically at a ∈ {2, 3} only. The ν family is the seed's simplex chain climbing d = 3, 4, 5 and terminating at its own sector. (ii) The GTC comb indices $k_{\rm GTC} \in \{0, 3, 10\}$ (u, c, t phase loads) are the mode indices of {photon, up, ν₁} — the seed's d=3 simplex chain {0, a, S(a,3)}; idwt.py STEP 1 already calls k=10 a "generation depth," consistent with the depth reading here. (iii) Under the §13b depth convention (which routes the top through the anchor T at depth 3) the law breaks for the top alone; the law holds specifically under minimal-route depth with the Euler keystone at depth 1 — equivalently, the law is *evidence for* reading the top as a near-seed geometric input rather than a deep composite.

**What the law does NOT do.** It constrains the (k, d) skeleton — which sector fires at which derivation depth — not the mode index n within the sector (ray-mate indices are not monotone along rays 2 and 3, and the n-selection/operand-choice residue of T0.5 is untouched, per run #8). Empty cells: rays 2 and 3 terminate at depth 2 (the (3,5) and (3,6) cells are unoccupied); no mechanism is derived for the ray structure, the anchor offsets, or the termination depths.

**Status: ❓** (exact arithmetic organization under the stated depth convention, verified by relaxation over the documented routes; no mechanism). Not yet placed in main documents — candidate locations are Part 2 (tower structure) and Part 7 (selection), pending Fedge's review.

**Addendum — candidate physical reading: a condensation front at unit dimensional speed (❓, 2026-06-12, Fedge question).** The law's mathematical signature — parallel slope-1 rays in a (step, level) lattice with a fixed-width band that closes behind itself — is the signature of a *front propagating at constant maximal speed with depletion behind it*. Natural processes with the same signature: Liesegang precipitation banding (discrete deposits left inside a moving supersaturation band), cosmological freeze-out (species condense in sweep order, each window closing), stellar shell burning (one element per shell, chain terminating at a distinguished endpoint with the residue escaping through the lightest channel), Madelung/Aufbau filling (diagonals of constant n+l in the (n,l) lattice — geometrically identical to d−k = const), and phyllotaxis (a fixed-width annular generative zone depositing parallel families). Proposed IDWT-native reading: the (k,d) plane is a causal diagram of the condensation — depth = generative time (count of kernel/condensate-insertion events), dimension = position along the Hopf chain — and the front advanced at exactly one dimension per kernel generation. Candidate motivation for speed exactly 1: sector nesting advances by single dimensions, and a mode structured in d coordinates is uniformly present in coordinate d+1 ("bound within, free without"), so one pairwise condensate insertion can imprint structure on exactly one new coordinate. The band width 3 is then non-dynamical: it is the dimensional spread of the three primordial anchors (d = 2,3,4), preserved by uniform propagation. Termination: the front meets the excluded d=7 rung at k=3 — the final matter deposit displaced to the terminal d=10 (the τ) — and the residual amplitude, with no upward rung, drains into the one plane every sector contains (d=2, the nesting floor), depositing the heavy bosons. This supplies the late-prism temporal reading (held ❓ in the late-prism notes, move (d)) with an internal clock, a propagation speed, and a termination event, but not yet with dynamics. Honest wrinkles: the rays are not derivation lineages (μ lands on ray 4 from a ray-2 parent), so the front reading lives at the aggregate band level, not edge-by-edge; W sits at depth 2, before termination, so the boson-drain reading fits Z and H cleanly but needs W as early floor leakage (the drain reading is superseded by the dispositions addendum below, item (e)); mass is not monotone along rays — depth is generative order, not energy order. Testable follow-ups: (i) an EoM condensation treatment should reproduce unit front speed and the width-3 band from the anchor spread (the same EoM gap that blocks late-prism move (d) and T0.5); (ii) the open Madelung-ordering todo item (atomic shell filling from IDWT sector levels) is geometrically the same diagonal-filling problem — if a single monotone cost functional orders the tower's filling, it should be exhibitable there first.

**Addendum — both follow-ups tested (2026-06-12, Fedge: "Test both").**

*(i) Toy front model reproduces the grid exactly; the fuel profile is unique and lands on named seed quantities.* Sites j = 2..10 on the nesting chain (7, 8, 9 inadmissible); rules: R1 unit-speed imprint (one new coordinate per pairwise insertion), R2 a newly structured site deposits up to two modes (the two hockey-stick evaluation channels d_eval ∈ {3,4}, run #4's engine) and a continuing site one per tick, R3 one fuel unit per deposit with exhausted sites inert, R4 Rule A block at j=7 with terminal redirect to j=10 carrying the j=7 fuel, R5 bosons excluded (off-ray g-rule cascade). With fuel tent $F_0(j) = (7 - |2j - 9|)/2 = (1,2,3,3,2,1)$ over j = 2..7, the simulation reproduces **all 12 on-ray deposits exactly, including the double deposits at (1,5) and (2,6)** — and the sweep over all $5^6 = 15{,}625$ profiles in $\{0..4\}^6$ shows the tent is the **unique** profile that does so under the fixed rules. The tent's parameters are named seed quantities: height scale $7 = a + b$ (the $\sqrt7$ radicand), center $4.5 = n_s + 1/2$ (the matter-quartet center, §19); its total (12) is the on-ray deposit count. Ablations: single-channel advance fails (misses one each of ν₂/μ, gains the empty cells), triple-channel fails, removing the redirect loses the τ, any other anchor set fails. Two structural by-products: the model *requires* a deposit at (1,4), which only the minimal-depth convention (top = depth-1 Euler keystone) can occupy — independent support for the §31 depth convention; and the empty cells (2,3), (3,5), (3,6) emerge from depletion rather than being imposed. Honest ledger: emergent = leading edge, window closings at d−2 for d=3,4, empty cells, τ displacement; fitted = the tent (unique, but inserted by hand); assumed = two-channel advance, anchors, boson exclusion. The EoM target list is now concrete: derive the single-coordinate imprint, the two-channel advance, the tent fuel, and the terminal redirect; W's early (k=2) cascade timing remains the open wrinkle (resolved in the dispositions addendum below, item (e)). Status ❓ — existence proof for the front reading, not a derivation.

*(ii) Madelung test: depletion does generate the diagonal cost (partial execution of the open Madelung todo item).* Thomas–Fermi screening (parameter-free density functional of the already-placed electron density — depletion, not Slater rules) applied to the neutral-atom radial problem, Latter tail, eigenvalues by finite difference (TF slope −1.5856 vs literature −1.588071). Aufbau first-occupation sequence over Z = 3..120: Kendall τ vs the empirical Madelung sequence = **0.906**, vs pure-Coulomb ordering 0.789, vs 3D-oscillator ordering 0.532; best linear cost $n + (\beta/\alpha)\,l$ fits at $\beta/\alpha = 0.70$ — most of the way from the Coulomb cost ($\beta/\alpha = 0$) to the Madelung diagonal ($\beta/\alpha = 1$) — and the canonical 4s-before-3d inversion is reproduced. Not exact Madelung (8 positionwise mismatches; TF delays the d/f orbitals — the known shell-structure limitation of TF). Conclusion for the front reading: in the solved system with the same lattice geometry, **a single monotone depleted potential demonstrably converts non-diagonal ordering toward diagonal filling** — the mechanism the condensation-front reading posits for d − k. The "proper IDWT derivation" of Madelung (Sonnet todo) remains open; this supplies its mechanism skeleton.

**Addendum — the tent is the Betti vector of the seed product $\mathbb{CP}^2\times\mathbb{CP}^3$ (gifts from Meta and GPT, verified 2026-06-12).** The fuel profile is not an anonymous fitted function. Verified identities:

- $F_0 = (1,2,3,3,2,1)$ **is the Betti vector** $b_0, b_2, \dots, b_{10}$ of $\mathbb{CP}^2\times\mathbb{CP}^3$ — the product of the two seed geometries (T15: $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)=3$ forces $n_u$, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)=4$ forces the composite). Equivalently (GPT's form) $F_0(j) = \min(j-1,\,8-j)$: the convolution of the two seed cell vectors $(1,1,1)\ast(1,1,1,1)$ — a two-source overlap. Total $\sum F_0 = 12 = \chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)\,\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)$ = the on-ray deposit count. This parallels the MC-4.6 keystone ($n_{\rm top} = \chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)\chi(\mathbb{CP}^5)$, the top Chern number of the *triple* product): the fuel is the Betti vector of the *double* product.
- **Hard Lefschetz correspondence (partial).** The Lefschetz decomposition of $H^*(\mathbb{CP}^2\times\mathbb{CP}^3)$ has exactly three primitive classes, at degrees $\{0, 2, 4\}$ — mapping to sites $j = \deg/2 + 2 = \{2, 3, 4\}$, **exactly the three ray anchors** — and each $L = \wedge\omega$ application advances one site (slope 1). The per-site class totals across the three Lefschetz orbits reproduce the tent exactly. **Mismatches, stated plainly:** the orbit lengths are $(6, 4, 2)$ while the observed ray populations are $(3, 3, 6)$, and the long-orbit cells $(3,5), (4,6), (5,7)$ are unoccupied in the tower — so "each ray is a Lefschetz orbit" is false in detail; what matches is the anchor set, the slope, and the per-site totals. Status ❓: a sharp partial correspondence, not a theorem. (Meta's further claims were checked and discarded: $\int\omega^5 = 10$, not 12; the proposed $3\times3$ Gram matrix has eigenvalues $(7.44, 0.17, -1.61)$, not the stated $(7.87, 1.00, -0.87)$, and the associated mass "prediction" does not survive.)
- **Band-gap reading of the redirect (GPT).** The ray-4 continuation cells $(3,7), (4,8), (5,9)$ all land outside the admissible sector set $D$ for the documented Rule A/B reasons — three consecutive inadmissible sectors, a genuine support gap, not a one-off exclusion. The redirect rule R4 is then simply "the ray continues to the next admissible sector": the τ is the band-edge mode — the first admissible state beyond the 7–9 gap — rather than a displaced exception. The documented d=6/d=10 scale degeneracy ($g_{66}=g_{10,10}$, T9c) is consistent with this fold-back reading. Two framing notes worth keeping: the width-3 strip $d-4 \le k \le d-2$ has the form of an acceptance window (cut-and-project kinematics), and the depletion-driven empty cells have the form of gain competition (laser mode selection) — the dynamical front and the kinematic window may be two descriptions of the same selected set.

The net effect on the EoM target list: the tent moves from "fitted, unique, seed-named" to "equals a canonical topological invariant of the seed product" — the EoM no longer needs to *produce* the tent, only to explain why the condensation budget per dimension equals the cohomology dimension $b_{2(j-2)}$ of $\mathbb{CP}^2\times\mathbb{CP}^3$ (one mode quantum per harmonic class is the natural candidate reading, ❓).

**Addendum — the two-channel advance derived from the seed condensate pair (🔶, 2026-06-12; front-model rule R2 upgraded from assumed to derived).** The front model assumed a newly structured site deposits up to two modes. This reduces to documented structure in four steps. (1) An advance deposit is one degree-1 condensate insertion (P6, `idwt.py` STEP 41): the vertex exists only where a sector condensate supplies the linearization, so each deposit channel is an *evaluating condensed sector*, and the deposit's index is the simplex redistribution over that sector's directions, $S(n, d_{\rm eval})$. (2) $d=2$ supplies no channel: there is no $d=2$ condensate — the documented fact that protects $m_\gamma = 0$ and gives the boson g-rule its $-1$ (Part 3 §16.2, STEP 55). (3) At tick 1 the condensed matter sectors are exactly the seed pair $\{3, 4\}$ (sites 5+ are unstructured at tick 0), so the first advance has exactly two channels — and the two site-5 deposits carry the documented channel-by-channel forms $S(n_u,3) = 10 = \nu_1$ and $S(n_u,4) = 15 = \nu_2$. (4) **Binding analysis (the load-bearing point):** the advance multiplicity is $\min(\#\text{channels}, F_0)$; with the Betti budgets $F_0(6) = 2$ and $F_0(7{\to}10) = 1$, the budget binds at or below the channel count at every later advance, so the channel *cap* is load-bearing only at site 5 — exactly where step (3) forces it to 2. Verified by simulation: the channel-set variants "fixed $\{3,4\}$" and "growing with structured sites" produce identical deposit records (both exact); "uncapped" fails (site 5 would overdraw its budget). Consequences: the cap of 2 that the data demands is supplied by the seed-condensate census, not assumed; and whether later-structured sectors contribute additional condensate channels — the open $(1,d)$ condensate-background question — is *unobservable in the deposit record*, so the derivation does not wait on it. Residual assumption (honest): one deposit per available channel per tick (the unit rate); the channel *count* is now derived, the *rate* is not. R2's status in the front-model ledger moves from "assumed" to 🔶 derived-from-documented-structure; updated in Part 2 §15 and `idwt.py` STEP 73.

**Addendum — the remaining open items dispositioned (2026-06-12).** All six items from the post-placement list:

- **(a) Even-channel ceiling — closed (⭐ identity + proven ceiling).** The uniform overlap of an even harmonic has the closed form $\int H_{2m}(y)\,e^{-y^2/2}\,dy = \sqrt{2\pi}\,(2m)!/m!$ (Hermite generating function; verified numerically to $10^{-12}$ for $m \le 8$) — strictly positive for every $m$, so the multi-coordinate even-channel imprint amplitude has **no zero at any order**. The exact unit-speed cut is parity-only: the same two-tier structure as the T0.5 even-level ceiling (run #2), now established in the imprint context. 🔵 is the proven ceiling for the even channel of the front.
- **(f) Lefschetz orbit mismatch — resolved.** The orbit of the primitive class $P^{2r}$ under $L$ occupies sites $j = (r+2) + k$, i.e. lies **on the ray $d-k = r+2$**: the three Lefschetz orbits *are* the three rays, with populations $(6,4,2)$ by orbit length.
