Neither isolates the scattered tower levels. The selection is not a linear-instability band — same verdict the MC-4.4 energetics sweep reached from the Hartree side, now confirmed for the modulational-stability operator directly. The cavity lens supplies no *linear* selector.
- **(ii) The index lattice IS four-wave-resonance-saturated (positive structure, ⭐ arithmetic).** The 14 indices carry 9 exact 3-wave relations n_i+n_j=n_k, and they are precisely the documented production edges (1+3=4 strange; 3+10=13 e; 13+22=35 and 15+20=35 μ; 1+22=3+20=10+13=23 τ; 4+72=76 W; 23+72=95 H), plus 3 degenerate-FWM carriers (2·13=3+23=4+22; 2·15=10+20). τ is a 3-fold resonance sink; the seed invariant 96 = n_s³n_u/2 = g₃₃g₄₄ = g₂₂g₅₅ is a 3-fold 4-wave total (down+H = ν₂+Z = charm+W = 96). The index comb is genuinely FWM-locked; this is run #5's edge set re-read as a phase-matched comb in the massless Layer-1 lattice (where the conserved "momentum" is the index, not energy — consistent with the three-mode-kernel-ME null 2026-06-10, which showed the edges are index, not energy, resonances).
- **Two-layer separation, quantified.** Index lattice: 9 three-wave resonances (resonance-rich). S-value lattice: 0 three-wave resonances (sum-free; partly a sparseness artifact, noted). Phase-matching lives in the index/level lattice, energy non-resonance protects the realized modes — the modulational reading of the Part 1 §5 spectral-independence / stability-equivalence pair.
- **Candidate identity (❓, not placed): the three massive d=2 bosons are Hopf-invariant reflections of one matter primary from each of d=3,4,5.** W,Z,H = 96 − {charm(20,d=4), ν₂(15,d=5), down(1,d=3)} exactly, with 96 the Hopf coupling invariant. An alternative decomposition to run #5's "heavy-boson cascade off the top" (W=g(5,72), Z=g(10,72), H=3+20+72). Honest caveat: 96 − {7 primaries} also produces 4 non-tower values {61,86,92,93}, so the reflection is an exact identity for {W,Z,H} but not a spurious-free generator on its own. Do not place in any document without Fedge's view; verify against §13/§25 first.
- FWM closure from the seeds {1,3,4} reaches 14/14 but over-generates (101 values, 87 spurious) — the perennial closure blow-up; the Pascal block a=3,b=4 remains uniquely 14/14 (next best 11/14, all a=3), i.e. a restatement, not a dynamical selector (Part 9 T0.5).
Net: the cavity/MI lens contributes real positive structure (the comb is an index-space four-wave-locked frequency comb with a Hopf-invariant carrier) and one honest negative of consequence (linear modulational instability does not select the comb), converging with every prior selection null onto the same residue: operand selection is nonlinear/amplitude-level, not kinematic. T0.5 unchanged (🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence; odd-level ⭐). The l=0→even-l angular cascade reproduces the ⭐ l-parity cut exactly. No document status edited.

**Companion — the nonlinear GP *dynamics* of the vacuum functional reproduces l-parity but does NOT select the even-level tower (2026-06-13).** Closes the last route flagged by the modulational run: the time-dependent basin-of-attraction question. Integrated the self-consistent GP flow of the explicit vacuum functional (E[Ψ]=∫|∇Ψ|²+(g/2)∫∫(ξ·ξ')²|Ψ|²|Ψ'|², separable mean field i Ȧ = [diag(ε)+gQ·M]A, Q=A†MA, M=(cosγ)² bounded angular kernel coupling l↔l,l±2) from the condensate seed A_{n=1}=1 plus 10⁻³ noise, norm-conserving RK4 (verified ‖A‖²=1.0000), g of both signs. Results: (i) **l-parity reproduced exactly** — population stays 100.00% on even levels (odd n), 0.00% on odd levels, for every g, since the kernel's l±2 structure connects N=0 only to even N (the ⭐ cut, dynamically). (ii) **First injection is clean** — the condensate feeds n=3 (up, a tower mode) at ~2×10⁻³, distinctly above the floor (the direct l=2 parametric daughter). (iii) **No tower selection beyond that** — the remaining amplitude sprays uniformly across the whole even ladder at ~10⁻⁶; tower members (5–6 of 14 reached) sit at the same population as non-tower even modes, and *which* tower members are reached changes with g (g=−0.5→{1,3,20,22,35}; g=+0.5→{1,3,13,15,20,23}) — i.e. noise-dependent, not selective. The conservative flow populates the even ladder; it does not pick the tower subset of it. Convergent conclusion across the whole 2026-06-13 investigation: the conservative dynamics (closed GP flow) supplies exactly the l-parity cut (⭐) and the condensate→up first step, and nothing finer; the even-level selection is not in it. The only dynamical home left for the even-level cut is the dissipative channel — spatial radiation through the downward kernel links — i.e. the Part 7 §1.2 stability equivalence (which even modes are protected against radiative decay), exactly where the documents already locate it. T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

**Quasicrystal cut-and-project / model-set reading of the tower selection — NULL for the operand, but the failure mechanism is informative (2026-06-13, Fedge request; run #9 in the tower-selection series).** A genuine cut-and-project set selects lattice points whose projection into an internal space lands in a bounded acceptance window; its defining feature is an *irrational slope* of the physical space relative to the lattice. Dictionary tested: lattice = the integer mode pairs $(n,d)$ with $d$ restricted to the active set $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ (sector selection by Rule A/B is assumed — only the open *n*-within-sector operand selection is at issue, the T0.5 residue); internal coordinate $s(n,d)=\mathrm{frac}(\alpha n+\beta d)$; window = the smallest torus arc covering all 15 members. IDWT-native irrational slopes were used ($\sqrt7$ from $g_{33}=8\sqrt7$, golden $\varphi$, the seed ratios $\sqrt7/4$, $1/\sqrt7$, $\sqrt2$), plus a rational control $4/3$. **Result — null:** no single irrational slope produces a window that selects the $n$-index above chance. Best selectivity $=0.040$ ($1/\sqrt7$): the window accepts 356 non-members, against a no-structure baseline of $\sim362$ for a window of the same length over 554 candidates — i.e. the accepted count tracks window *length*, not membership; the rational control does worse, as a periodic slope should. **Why it fails (the informative part):** a model set is a Delone set — its gaps are *bounded* (this is forced by the linear projection through a finite window). The tower indices grow binomially, $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}$, so the within-sector spacings *grow* with $n$ (d=4: gaps 17 then 52; d=2: up to 74) instead of staying bounded. No fixed acceptance window can track a polynomially sparsening set. The tower's operand selection is combinatorial (binomial), not the linear/kinematic projection a cut-and-project window supplies — the same conclusion runs #1–8 reached from the coupling-magnitude, flat-combinatoric, spectral, and branching sides, now reconfirmed from the geometric (Delone) side. **Two positives kept honestly.** (1) IDWT *does* satisfy the model-set irrational-slope precondition: the incommensurability lemma (14/15 cross-sector scale ratios irrational, ✅, §15 STEP 40) is exactly the irrational-winding condition, and the torus-orbit time-average it drives is the cut-and-project reading of the even-level dephasing (the 🔵 bound) — but upgrading the status would require a *sharp* window (an exact accept/reject), and the test shows none exists; consistency with the GPT "acceptance-window" framing of the depth strip $d-k_{\min}\in\{2,3,4\}$ (§31) holds only at the necessary-not-sufficient level, matching run #8. (2) The per-sector index sets have $\le 3$ distinct consecutive gaps (d=3 $\{3,12\}$, d=4 $\{17,52\}$, d=5 $\{5,7\}$, d=2 $\{5,14,74\}$), nominally a Sturmian signature — but with 2–4 points per sector this is undersampled and not evidence. **Correction recorded:** a naive $(N\bmod 2)$ internal coordinate is *not* the $l$-parity window — only 8 of 16 members carry $n$ odd, so $n$-parity does not reproduce the cut; the exact $l$-parity window (⭐) lives in the angular-momentum $l$ on the sector sphere, not in the parity of the mode index. Net: the cut-and-project lens converges with every prior selection null; the residue stays the dissipative dynamical route (Part 7 §1.2). T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

**Complement decomposition of the tower selection — half the anti-tower is an exact infinite exclusion; the open core is one parity class (2026-06-13, Fedge directive "the complement is as significant as the tower"; complement companion to runs #1–9).** Worked the selection from $\Sigma^c$ (every admissible $(n,d)$ that is NOT a physical particle) on equal footing with $\Sigma$, since $\chi_{\Sigma^c}=1-\chi_\Sigma$. **Clean statement (the deliverable):** $\Sigma^c$ splits exactly by level parity ($N=n-1$). (1) **Odd-level half ($n$ even), exact ⭐:** the $l$-content at odd $N$ is odd-$l$ only, kernel-disconnected from the even-$l$ ($l=0$) vacuum — no power of $V_{\rm kernel}$ reaches it (Part 7 §1.2). So no odd-level mode can be a spontaneously-populated stable resonance; this is an exact, infinite exclusion. The seven even-$n$ *members* ($\gamma,W$ in d=2; strange in d=3; charm, top in d=4; $\nu_1,\nu_3$ in d=5) are not counterexamples: they enter the spectrum only as composite tower *outputs* via the parity-flipping offset-additive / cross-sector channels (🔶 MC-4.4), a production statement distinct from kernel excitation, and persist by cross-sector coupling. (2) **Even-level half ($n$ odd), open 🔵:** the dephasing residue — and it is *exactly* the tower's even-level selection viewed from the complement, hitting the same proven ceiling (no exact kernel node at $s=3/2$, STEP 34 / run #2). Over $n\le120$, $d\in D$ the two halves are 353 vs 352 modes — the complement is ~50% exactly closed, and the open core is precisely the even-level (n odd) non-members. **Structural note:** d=6 and d=10 (charged leptons $e,\mu$ and $\tau$) have *zero* odd-level members — purely even-level; the quark/neutrino/boson sectors are mixed-parity. **Three complement-native sharp-rule probes on the open half — all null:** (i) additive-resonance "drain" ($n=n_a+n_b$ into lighter comb modes) over-protects 124 of 352 non-members and members are themselves sums (run #8 edges), so it does not separate; (ii) the downward-radiation shadow $\{(n-2,d)\}$ is finite (covers 7) against the infinite tail — but reconfirms downward-independence: every member's $(n-2,d)$ target is a non-member (STEP 64); (iii) on $S$-values the *members* are sum-free ($\{1,3,15,20,2002,\dots\}$, no member is a sum of two members — Part 1 §5 spectral-independence ⭐ reconfirmed), which characterizes the tower, not its complement. Net: the complement framing closes half the anti-tower exactly and pins the open part to a single parity class, but supplies no new exact cut for that class — converging with runs #1–9 on the dissipative-dynamics residue (Part 7 §1.2). The ⭐/🔵 split coincides with the late-prism Layer-1/Layer-2 seam: the exact half is selected by the parity of the sector-blind integer $n$ (pre-split, prism-immune $\Rightarrow$ exact), the open half by post-split scale-dependent dephasing (carries the scales $m_{\rm scale,d}$ $\Rightarrow$ 🔵). T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited. (Offer to Fedge: a short "complement decomposition" paragraph could be added to Part 7 §1.2 to record that the odd-level exclusion closes half of $\Sigma^c$ exactly — reported, not written.)

**Prism split into 6 sectors, and a parity×split-type observation (2026-06-13, Fedge directive "learn how the prism splits into 6").** The prism = the complex Hopf chain $S^1\to S^{2n+1}\to\mathbb{CP}^n$; each step gives a (Kähler base $\mathbb{CP}^n=d{=}2n$, real total $S^{2n+1}=d{=}2n{+}1$) pair, and $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ assembles as 4 Kähler bases $\{2,4,6,10\}$ + 2 real totals $\{3,5\}$ (verified to reproduce T3). Two termination edges: the real totals stop after $n{=}2$ ($d{=}5$) by Rule A (coupling chain terminates at $d{=}6$); the Kähler bases stop at $d{=}10$ by Rule B (Gegenbauer endpoint, $b_{k_0}(10)=\tfrac12$ exact, $d{=}8$ removed earlier by the $\chi{=}5$ gap). Through the meta-principle: the split's *which-rays + geometry* is scale-free/exact (⭐/✅, bar the Rule A $d{=}7$ residual 🔶); the scales $m_{\rm scale,d}$ are the scale-bearing Layer-2 datum (non-monotonic in $d$; 6/10 degenerate). **Parity×split-type pass (❓, weak).** The two orphan Kähler bases $d{=}6,10$ (leptons, terminated at the chain end) host *only* even-level ($n$ odd, $l{=}0$-present) members; the four paired sectors carry a doublet of odd-level ($n$ even) members each (exactly 2 — but that count needs the $b$-quark beat included; without it $d{=}3$ has 1). Significance is the robust $P=\tfrac18$ (orphans both zero) under an iid-parity null — suggestive, not significant; the "exactly 2" pattern is post-hoc ($P\approx1/404$ but cherry-picked). Mechanism (DAG-level, not derived): the orphan lepton bases are fed only by additive $\nu+$quark productions, each (even-$n$)+(odd-$n$)=odd-$n$=even-level; the odd-level (even-$n$) members elsewhere come from simplex/g-rule/IE/beat/reference channels feeding the quark/$\nu$/boson sectors. So parity content tracks the feeding channel, which tracks split position — recorded as a ❓ observation, not a structural claim. No document status edited.

**Single-sector effective-energy functional search for the Part 2 §5 vacuum-stability minima (2026-06-12)**

Conjecture: an effective energy E(n) built from documented T2 kernel vocabulary — simplex mass S(n,d), Gegenbauer weight 1/DegS, kernel coupling gc2=n(n+1)/S(n,d+1), and derived weights — has local minima at exactly {n=1, n=4} in d=3 at g₃₃=8√7, and the same functional form selects the d=4 seed n_u=3 at g₄₄=12/√7. This is the functional asserted (but not written) in Part 2 §5 line 242: "effective energy has local minima at exactly n=1 and n=4 at g₃₃=8√7."

Checked: 30 candidate combinations — 5 functional families × 6 weights. Families: (A) additive binding E=S−g·w; (B) multiplicative E=S(1−g·w); (C) Casimir two-level mixing (lower branch of the 2×2 problem with Casimir partner Cas(n)=n(n+1)); (D) scale self-consistency E=S√(g·w); (E) second-order ΔN=±2 E=S−(g·w)²/4. Weights: b=1/DegS, gc2=n(n+1)/S(n,d+1), gc=√gc2, S/M=S/DegS, dN·b=n(n−1)/DegS, cas/S=n(n+1)/S. Joint test: d=3 minima = {1,4} at g₃₃ AND d=4 minima containing 3 at g₄₄. g-window scan 0..100, step 0.02.

Results (all null):
- No candidate has d=3 minima = {1,4} at g₃₃ (complete null at the documented coupling).
- g-window scan: NONE — for no g in [0,100] do any of the 30 candidates produce d=3 minima == {1,4}. The d=3 minimum is always at n=1 (binding weak) or slides to n=3 or higher (binding too strong); the two-sided n=4 pocket never opens.
- The one d=4 hit is B/gc2 → d=4 minima [3], but d=3 minima [12] (not a d=3 success).
- Degeneracy probes (family A): A/S/M (g[E₁=E₄,d=3]=19.0, 0.898g₃₃) and A/dN·b (15.83, 0.748g₃₃) have positive degeneracy coupling, confirming these weights have the right sign structure. But g₃₃ lies above the degeneracy point — at the documented coupling the n=4 degenerate configuration has already slid to n=3 as the global minimum.
- Marginality probes (family A): the d=3 onset coupling where n=4 first becomes a minimum is 30.0 (1.417g₃₃) for A/S/M and 50.0 (2.362g₃₃) for A/dN·b — both above g₃₃. n=4 never enters as a minimum before g₃₃ is reached; there is no window.

Structural interpretation: a local minimum at n=4 (with n=1 also a local minimum) requires a weight function with a peak or inflection specifically at n=4 — non-monotone in n. Every weight in the documented vocabulary is strictly monotone (increasing or decreasing) in n. The Casimir family C exploits the unique lattice degeneracy S(4,3)=Cas(4)=20 and was explicitly designed to create resonance at n=4, but cannot overcome the global boundary minimum at n=1 for any tested weight. The single-sector ansatz is the likely wrong object. The T2 kernel is inherently cross-sector: the d=3 vacuum field is coupled to the d=4 sector via g₃₄. An effective energy for d=3 modes, after integrating out the d=4 sector at its equilibrium, would include a back-reaction term of the form (g₃₄)² × f(n₃, n₄*)/m_scale₄ — a cross-sector contribution that can break the monotone-weight constraint. The cross-sector effective potential is the natural next candidate for the Part 2 §5 functional; this search closes the single-sector branch.

Note: the three-layer ontology established this session (arithmetic integers → self-consistency loop → excitations) suggests the vacuum-stability functional is a statement about the Layer-2 self-consistency loop closure, where the d=3 and d=4 sectors are jointly constrained. A single-sector treatment cannot capture this.

**Cross-sector vacuum-stability functional search (2026-06-12)**

Follow-up to the single-sector null above. Conjecture: coupling the d=3 effective energy to the d=4 condensate at n_u=3 via the T2 kernel creates a local minimum at n₃=4. Three approaches tested, all null.

Checked: (A) Diagonal cross-sector ME = g₃₄/3 × ⟨r²⟩_{n₃,d=3} × ⟨r_s²⟩_{3,d=4}: strictly monotone increasing in n₃ (kernel positivity, V≥0 always); minimum at n₃=1. Confirmed analytically by the rank-1 factorisation V_kernel = ½Σᵢⱼ(Σ_d v_d Q_ij^{(d)} J_d)²≥0 — a positive-semidefinite operator cannot create energy pockets. (B) Off-diagonal ME |⟨R_{n₃}^{(3)} | r² | R_3^{(4)}⟩|: non-monotone (peaks at n_r=2, i.e. n₃=5), decaying geometrically for larger n_r. However, n₃=4 (level N=3, l=1 and l=3 ONLY, STEP 30) has NO l=0 component — the l=0 cross-sector coupling is identically zero for n₃=4 by l-parity. n₃=4 is invisible to all l=0 kernel channels. (C) 2×2 lower-branch mixing between (n₃,3) and (n₄=3,4): minima at n₃=1, 3, 5 (the l=0 representative modes), not n₃=4. The lower branch at n₃=4 (E_lower=1.12 MeV) is above n₃=3 (E_lower=0.09 MeV) because n₃=4 and n₃=3 share the same n_r=1 in the l=0 approximation, but n₃=4 has the higher S(n,3).

Structural reason for the null: the kernel positivity theorem prevents cross-sector terms from lowering the energy. The mean-field cross-sector term simply shifts λ₃ → λ₃ + δλ (a uniform scale factor), which raises all modes proportionally and leaves the minimum at n₃=1 unchanged. n₃=4 additionally has no l=0 channel, decoupling it from the l=0 vacuum entirely — its energy is the pure mass term S(4,3)×m_scale₃.

Positive structural fact found: n₃=4 is the unique mode that is (i) an odd-parity (l-parity protected) condensate mode AND (ii) the Casimir resonance point S(4,3)=Cas(4)=20 AND (iii) decoupled from all l=0 kernel channels. This combination makes n₃=4 both stable and unperturbed by the vacuum sector — which may be the content of the §5 assertion, stated imprecisely as "local minimum."

**Conclusion on Part 2 §5 line 242 (resolved 2026-06-12):** No standard construction in documented IDWT vocabulary produces E(n) with local minima at {1,4} in d=3. The actual derivation of g₃₃=8√7 is in §9 (gap construction: gap_d3=n_s²=k₀, g_coeff=2/√7), not from this functional. The §5 assertion is a heuristic description of "the two stable condensate modes at the vacuum coupling," not a precise energy-minimization claim. Disposition: Part 2 §5 line 242 already states the §9 gap-construction derivation and the three structural selectors, and explicitly disclaims the energy-minimization-over-mode-index reading (citing this §15). The separate *sector-activation* functional that other Parts called "the vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5)" is also not a §5/mean-field object — it is non-selective in d (§3 addendum, STEP 76) and its correct home is Part 6 Open Theorem A. No further edit to §5 is required.

**MC-2 completeness is a different object — the radial/flat-vs-compact computation (2026-06-12, Fedge: "do the radial computation"; `files/idwt.py` STEP 74d).** The two searches above target the *discrete-minima* reading of the §5 functional (E(n) over mode indices). MC-2 completeness — that the second-variation operator L has no marginal direction beyond the harmonic forms ω₂^α ω₃^β — is a *different* object (an operator-kernel statement, not an E(n) minimisation), and the radial question for it is now answered. On the flat-ℝ^d reading (Part 4 §3.10, condensate = isotropic-oscillator ground state) the Witten/Hodge Laplacian's kernel is isomorphic to the de Rham cohomology of ℝ^d, which is contractible: $b_0 = 1$, $b_{p>0} = 0$. So the flat radial continuation has a **1-dimensional kernel (the vacuum only)** — it adds *no* internal marginal direction. The radial modes are therefore not a completeness leak; the opposite — the flat continuation removes everything but the ground state. The 12 marginal directions live entirely in the **compact** $\mathbb{CP}^k$ topology, where the Hodge theorem gives $\ker(\Delta_{\rm form}) = H^*(\mathbb{CP}^k)$ *exactly* (no extra zero modes), so internal completeness is automatic on the compact geometry. **Net reframing:** MC-2 completeness is not a radial Sturm–Liouville gap and not the (null) minima functional; it reduces to the flat-ℝ^d vs compact-$\mathbb{CP}^k$ reconciliation — what makes the sector contribute its compact $\mathbb{CP}^k$ cohomology to the fluctuation problem (both readings coexist in the framework: the sector is flat and never frozen, yet carries the $d=2k \leftrightarrow \mathbb{CP}^k$ cohomology ring). Caveat: Ψ is a Dirac spinor, so the precise operator is the Dolbeault/Witten Laplacian (spinors ↔ $(0,q)$-forms on a Kähler manifold); the contractible-vs-compact dichotomy holds in that setting. Recommendation (ASK FEDGE): the live open item for MC-2 completeness is the compactness/topology source, not a further energy-minimisation search — do not re-run the discrete-minima family.

**Build-level depth as a third coordinate — the (n, d, depth) test battery; convergent null, two positive sub-facts (2026-06-14, Fedge directive).** With each particle carrying the triple $(n, d, \text{depth})$, where depth is the *build level* (seeds down$=(1,3)$, up$=(3,4)$ at depth 1; depth $= 1 + \max(\text{parent depths})$; photon excluded; every derivation path kept as its own tower → 96 path-combos → **28 distinct depth-vectors**, identical $(n,d)$ spectrum), the six structural tests A–F were run hunting for a relation constraining $n$ and/or $d$. Mass-based tests were excluded a priori (mass is depth-blind, §15 2026-06-13). Results.

- **(A) No closed-form $d=f(n,\text{depth})$.** No rational linear $d = an + b\,\text{depth} + c$ fits all 14 members or the 9 matter modes. depth$\to d$ is multivalued: depth 1$\to\{3,4\}$, 2$\to\{3,5\}$, 3$\to\{4,5,6\}$ — the three rays, not a function. Depth does not rescue the §15 "$d$ is not a function of $n$ alone" dead end to a closed form.
- **(B) The three-ray band reproduces §31, robustly across all 28 towers (⭐ arithmetic, no new selective content).** Under the build-level convention (seeds at depth 1, vs §31's $k_{\min}$ seeds at 0) the matter modes satisfy $d - \text{depth} \in \{1,2,3\}$ — §31's $\{2,3,4\}$ shifted by one. This holds in **all 28** towers (every tower has exactly 3 distinct matter $d-\text{depth}$ values); the bosons are off-ray (top $=0$, W/Z/H negative) and $\tau$ is the $d=7$-slot redirect ($d-\text{depth}=6$), exactly as §31. The band is therefore a property of the path-rigid matter spine, not a tower discriminator — it constrains the $(\text{depth},d)$ skeleton, never $n$.
- **(C) depth is monotone but NOT injective within a sector; the residual is two same-depth doublets.** Within every sector $n$ rises with depth, but $(d,\text{depth})$ does not recover $n$: collisions at $(d{=}5,\text{depth}{=}2)\to\{\nu_1{=}10,\nu_2{=}15\}$ and $(d{=}6,\text{depth}{=}3)\to\{e{=}13,\mu{=}35\}$. Depth resolves the spectrum down to same-depth sector-doublets and no finer; the two doublets are separated only by production channel ($\nu_1=S(n_u,3)$ vs $\nu_2=S(n_u,4)$; $e$ additive vs $\mu$ simplex) — i.e. by operand/channel choice, circular. This is a sharp localization of where depth stops discriminating, consistent with the §13b/parity-split doublet structure.
- **(D) No tight joint invariant.** Seven candidate forms $R(n,d,\text{depth})$ (incl. $d-\text{depth}$, $(n{-}1)-\text{depth}$, $n-S(\text{depth},d)$, $n \bmod \text{depth}$, $(n{-}1)\bmod(\text{depth}{+}1)$) — none takes $\le 2$ values on the members while being rare on the lattice. The tightest are restatements of the ray band (B).
- **(E) depth is operand-blind — the decisive reconfirmation of the run-#8 residue.** A forward generative closure (simplex $S(\cdot,3/4)$, additive/IE $a+b-c$, g-rule) from the seeds was run with five operand depth-gates of increasing strictness: none, $|\Delta\text{depth}|\le 2$, $\le 1$, "max operand at depth $p{-}1$", and "**both** operands at depth $p{-}1$". **All five give identical output: 1005 reached $(n,d)$, 13/14 members [top excluded — it is the Euler-product keystone, not a combinatoric output, run #5], and 992 $(n,d)$ false positives.** The reachable set is depth-invariant: restricting operand depth removes zero false positives, because the over-generating combinations occur at every operand-depth relationship. Build-depth carries no constraint on *which* operands combine — exactly the run-#8 conclusion (channel-type gates saturate; the residue is operand selection), now established directly from the depth axis.
- **(F) The depth-vector does not self-select.** Canonical $\sum\text{depth}=46$ is not the global minimum (37); the matter band width is identical (3) in all 28 towers; no structural criterion (Σdepth, max-depth, band width) isolates the canonical tower. Consistent with §15 2026-06-13 (canonical $\sum k_{\min}$ is not the global min; mass is depth-blind).

**Net.** The build-level depth coordinate reproduces the §31 ray skeleton across all towers (B) and cleanly localizes the residual ambiguity to two same-depth sector-doublets (C), but supplies **no new constraint on $n$ or $d$**: no closed-form $d(n,\text{depth})$ (A), no joint invariant (D), no operand purchase (E), no tower selection (F). The whole battery converges with runs #1–9 onto the same residue — operand selection is combinatorial/dynamical, not carried by build order or any coordinate kinematics. T0.5 unchanged (🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence; odd-level ⭐). Significance discipline (NULL A/B) was not triggered — no positive to gate. No document status edited; no `idwt.py` STEP added (nothing load-bearing). Recorded so the depth-coordinate battery is not rebuilt.

**Combinatorics test battery CB-1..CB-6 — six new combinatorial selectors, all null; one §31 significance caveat (2026-06-14, Fedge directive "write new tests that use combinatorics").** Six tests reaching combinatorial structure the prior graveyard did not touch, each shaped as a *partition condition* not a universal identity, run on the 14 members (no photon) against the lattice $d\in D$, $n\in[1,200]$.

- **CB-1 — p-adic / Kummer–Lucas structure of $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}$ (NEW: prior §17 tested prime-factor count $\Omega(S)$, never carries).** Kummer carry-count $\nu_p(S)=$ #carries adding $d$ and $(n-1)$ in base $p$. Carry-free (Lucas-nonzero) member rate vs lattice: $p{=}2$ 0.29 vs 0.34, $p{=}3$ 0.43 vs 0.41, $p{=}5$ 0.43 vs 0.54, $p{=}7$ **0.64 vs 0.45**. The only lean is a weak enrichment of carry-free-mod-7 among members (9/14) — notable only because $7=n_s+n_u$ is the seed discriminant — but at $\sim1.45\sigma$ (one-sided $p\approx0.07$ before look-elsewhere over 4 primes) it is not significant. Carry-count is not a sector predictor (within-sector $\nu_2$ scatters: $d{=}2\{1,0,4\}$, $d{=}5\{1,2,2\}$). NULL.
- **CB-2 — Pascal/hockey-stick ENDPOINT consistency.** Using $S(n,d)=S(n-1,d)+S(n,d-1)$ as a *constraint* requiring the summands to be member-values: only `down` has a member-valued summand ($S(1,2)=1$). The member set is essentially not Pascal-endpoint-closed — the members are too sparse to be additively adjacent in the triangle. NULL.
- **CB-3 — difference-set / Sidon structure of the index set (revives the PG(3,2) thread via the right invariant; tempers §31).** Observed 3-wave count $=9$ (the §31 MI-addendum figure). NULL test over $10^3$+ random 14-subsets of $[0,95]$: mean 7.84, sd 4.82, **$P(\ge 9)=0.26$** — the additive-resonance count is at the random-subset baseline. Difference-multiset excess 66 vs null 70 ($P=0.36$); no modulus gives a constant-$\lambda$ (difference-set-regular) structure. **Caveat recorded against §31:** the 9 three-wave relations are real and *are* the documented production edges (that content stands), but their *count* carries no statistical anomaly — the "four-wave-locked comb" reading should not be read as a density anomaly, only as the identification of the edges with productions. No §31 edit; caveat logged here. NULL for a difference-set selector.
- **CB-4 — cross-dimensional figurate coincidences of $S(n,d)$.** $d{=}2$ values are triangular by construction ($S(n,2)=T_n$), so W/Z/H being triangular is definitional, not selective. `up` $S{=}15{=}T_5$ and `nu2` $S{=}11628{=}T_{152}$ are coincidental triangular hits (their non-$d{=}2$ value happens to be triangular $=$ a $d{=}2$ cell); `strange` $S{=}20{=}\binom{6}{3}$ central. Cross-sector simplex coincidence is rare on the lattice (21 of 1227 distinct values, 1.7%) but members hit it only trivially (down, the universal $S(1,d)=1$) or coincidentally (up, nu2) — no figurate class covers the members. NULL.
- **CB-5 — cyclic sieving (CSP) on the sector simplices at $\chi$-th roots of unity (NEW: the group action, not the flat $q$-value of the 2026-06-09 null).** Evaluating $[\,n{+}d{-}1\ \,d\,]_q$ at $q=e^{2\pi i/\chi}$ for the Kähler sectors $\chi\in\{2,3,4,6\}$: no CSP fixed-point count coincides with a member index for $n\le40$. NULL (and the correspondence as posed is dimensionally mismatched — the small CSP counts cannot reach the large $d{=}2$ member indices; not pursued further).
- **CB-6 — Beatty/Sturmian per-sector structure (complement combinatorics).** Every multi-member sector has *exactly two* gap lengths — $d{=}2\{5,14\}$, $d{=}4\{17,52\}$, $d{=}5\{5,7\}$ — the Sturmian two-gap signature, confirming §15 run #9's "nominally Sturmian." But with 2–3 points per sector two gaps is near-automatic (undersampled), and no mean-gap $\alpha$ ($d{=}2{:}9.5$, $d{=}4{:}34.5$, $d{=}5{:}6$) matches an IDWT-meaningful Beatty slope ($\sqrt7$, $\chi$, $n_s$ multiples). NULL — the two-gap structure is real but carries no evidential weight at this sample size.

**Net.** Six independent combinatorial probes, all null for a selector constraining $n$ or $d$ — the same convergence as runs #1–9 and the depth battery. Sub-findings banked: a non-significant carry-free-mod-7 lean (CB-1, the seed discriminant leaving a faint fingerprint); the index set is **not** a Sidon/difference-set-regular set and its additive-resonance count is at the random baseline (CB-3, tempering the §31 comb-density reading without touching the edges-as-productions content); cross-sector figurate coincidence is rare but not member-covering (CB-4); the per-sector two-gap structure is genuine but undersampled (CB-6). NULL A/B significance discipline was applied where a positive could have arisen (CB-1, CB-3); none survived. T0.5 unchanged (🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence; odd-level ⭐). No document status edited; no `idwt.py` STEP added. Recorded so these six are not rebuilt.

**Companion to CB-1 — the mod-7 carry lean does NOT compound with the l-parity cut (2026-06-14).** Followed up the one live thread from CB-1 (members lean carry-free mod 7, $7=n_s+n_u$) by combining it with the exact $l$-parity cut (⭐). Since $l$-parity exactly excludes the odd-level (even-$n$) class, the open core of T0.5 is the even-level (odd-$n$, $l{=}0$-present) class — here 8 members. Test: does carry-free-mod-7 separate those 8 from the odd-$n$ non-members? **No.** Carry-free-mod-7 passes 6/8 members but 44% of the odd-$n$ lattice (262 false positives for 6 true positives); NULL over $2\times10^4$ random 8-subsets of the odd-$n$ lattice gives mean 3.58 carry-free, $P(\ge 6)=0.084$ ($\sim1.4\sigma$, not significant, and nothing after look-elsewhere over 4 primes $\times$ 2 parity classes). The even-$n$ class carry-7 values are mixed (three 0, three 1) with no complementary condition. Structural aside (❓, post-hoc, not significant): the two odd-$n$ members that fail carry-free-mod-7 are exactly the $d{=}6$ charged leptons $e=(13,6)$ and $\mu=(35,6)$ — the orphan Kähler-base sector. Verdict: the mod-7 lean is $\sim1.4\sigma$ noise consistent across CB-1 and this compound test; the two weak signals do not reinforce. Confirms the residue is not in the static arithmetic of $(n,d)$ mod 7. T0.5 unchanged; no status edited.

**Radiative-stability route quantified, and the d=6 lepton thread closed (2026-06-14, Fedge directive).** Two follow-ups on the Part 7 §1.2 / STEP 64 stability equivalence and the recurring d=6 lepton anomaly.

*(A) The downward same-sector radiative widths do not give a cut — reconfirms run #3 from the spatial-radiation side.* Computed, for all 14 members, the energy release $\Delta E = m_{\rm scale,d}(S(n,d)-S(n-2,d))$ of the channel $(n,d)\to(n-2,d)+q$ (exact) and a proxy width $\Gamma\sim g_{\rm rad}^2\,\Delta E^2$ with the oscillator $r^2$ element $g_{\rm rad}=\sqrt{n_r(n_r+d/2)}$, $n_r=(n{-}1)/2$ (3D radiation phase space $\propto\Delta E^2$; proxy, flagged). The six absolutely-stable members ($\nu_1,\nu_2,\nu_3,e,u$, and the structurally-closed ground $d$) are the lowest-$\Gamma$ modes — ranks 0–4 of the width ordering plus the closed ground — but this is a *soft, mass-driven monotone correlation* ("stable $=$ lightest in its sector, and $\Gamma$ grows with mass"), not a cut: every would-be width is nonzero (no $\Gamma=0$ for members specifically) and the stable/unstable boundary (between $u$, $\Gamma_{\rm proxy}\approx12$, and strange, $\approx2.5\times10^4$) is just the first mass gap. Crucially these same-sector widths are *would-be* — the $(n-2,d)$ targets are all non-members (non-asymptotic), so they do not drive real decay; the unstable members decay through cross-sector channels to lighter *members*, which the same-sector catalog does not capture. Net: the spatial-radiation width tracks the stability ordering but supplies no independent selector — the same verdict as the survival-ratio run #3, now from the radiation side. 🔵 unchanged.

*(B) The tower's "downward-2-sparseness" is not statistically special.* Every member's downward target $(n-2,d)$ being a non-member is equivalent to: no two members differ by exactly 2 within a sector (verified — 0 such pairs). NULL over $2\times10^4$ random subsets with the observed per-sector sizes: $P(\text{no same-sector diff-2 pair anywhere})=0.79$ (range $[1,95]$), 0.86 ($[1,150]$), 0.90 ($[1,200]$). So the radiative self-protection (no member radiates into another via the basic $n\to n{-}2$ link) is the *generic* outcome for a set this sparse, not a designed feature — it carries no structural weight beyond the co-fixed-point condition itself.

*(C) The d=6 lepton anomaly resolved — orphan-base parity (known) plus a base-7 coincidence (CB-1 thread closed).* (i) $d{=}6$ and $d{=}10$ are the only sectors hosting *purely even-level* (odd-$n$) members ($e,\mu$ and $\tau$) — the orphan terminal Kähler bases; the iid-parity null gives $P=(1/2)^3=0.125$, suggestive but not significant, matching the §15 prism-split parity pass. (ii) The CB-1 finding that $e=(13,6)$ and $\mu=(35,6)$ are the only odd-$n$ members carrying mod 7 is a **base-7/dimension coincidence**: $\nu_7(S)=$ carries adding $d$ and $(n{-}1)$ in base 7, and $d{=}6=7{-}1$ is the digit just below the base, so adding 6 carries whenever $(n{-}1)\bmod 7\ge1$ — $d{=}6$ modes generically carry mod 7 regardless of physics. This explains why the $d{=}6$ leptons are the exception to the carry-free-mod-7 lean and fully closes the CB-1 mod-7 thread: the lean and its $d{=}6$ exception are both arithmetic of which sector dimensions sit near base 7, not a selection signal. T0.5 unchanged; no status edited; no `idwt.py` STEP added (the widths are proxies, B/C are null/known).

**Connectivity-bound audit + two new selection nulls (runs #10–11) — the "no second selection rule" claim is RETRACTED, the question reopened (2026-06-14, Fedge directive "redo + run more").** The 2026-06-14 §22 connectivity bound ("$l$-parity is the unique exact kernel grading $\Rightarrow$ selection necessarily dynamical") is withdrawn: the graph is connected by construction (automatic for any $l=0\oplus l=2$ operator; identical under the correct rank-2 angular support; survives 50% random edge deletion), reduces a two-body kernel to a single-mode graph, and only tests labels that are functions of $(n_r,l)$ — full correction at §22.

*Run #10 — additive-resonance significance (NULL).* The 14 tower indices carry 10 exact 3-wave relations $n_i+n_j=n_k$ and 22 four-wave matchings $n_i+n_j=n_k+n_l$, but against a range-matched null (14 random integers in $[1,95]$) this is not anomalous ($P(\ge10)=0.12$; $P(\ge22)=0.44$); the significance against a wider $[1,200]$ null ($P\approx10^{-3}$) is a span artifact of the members' compressed range. The additive relations are the tower's additive construction restated, not an independent selector.

*Run #11 — arithmetic-closure over-generation (NULL).* Scanning all subsets of the documented operations (successor $+1$, hockey-stick $S(\cdot,3)$ and $S(\cdot,4)$, pairwise sum, inclusion–exclusion $a+b-c$) acting on the seeds $\{1,3\}$ ($+\chi$ constants $\{3,4,6\}$): every operation set that reaches all 14 members fills the **entire** index lattice $[1,100]$ (FP $=86$; zero-FP full-member closures: NONE). The tower is therefore not its own minimal arithmetic closure — closure either misses members or over-generates totally, reconfirming run #8 with a sharp bound.

Net: no new exact selector found, but the impossibility claim is gone — whether a numerical/arithmetic selector exists for the even-level core is OPEN. Untried, flagged for a deep session: (a) a POWERED spectral test of the actual two-body coupling matrix (near-conserved quantity / approximate block structure, not graph connectivity); (b) joint $(n,d)+$depth selectors via the 28-tower battery. The dynamical MC-4 route is equally unproven. T0.5 status unchanged (odd-level ⭐; even-level 🔵/🔶).

**AI-suggested selection mechanisms — all NULL (2026-06-14).** Four directions from ChatGPT and Meta AI (offload session, 2026-06-14) investigated and closed. (A) *$\mathrm{Sym}^d(\mathbb{C}^n)$ identification* (ChatGPT): $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}=\dim(\mathrm{Sym}^d(\mathbb{C}^n))$ — verified exactly for all 15 tower members. This is a correct algebraic restatement of what the multiset coefficient counts: degree-$d$ monomials in $n$ variables. The branching $\mathrm{GL}(n)\downarrow\mathrm{GL}(n-1)$ gives $\mathrm{Sym}^d(\mathbb{C}^n)|_{\mathrm{GL}(n-1)}=\bigoplus_{k=0}^d\mathrm{Sym}^k(\mathbb{C}^{n-1})$ — all components survive and the dimension identity reduces to the hockey-stick recurrence. No selection beyond HS. (B) *APS eta-invariant* (Meta AI): "Dirac operator on $S^{2d-1}$ with APS boundary conditions selects admissible $n$; periodicity mod 12 for $d=3$." Three problems. First, the sector geometries are $S^3$ (d=3) and $S^5$ (d=5) for the real-sphere sectors, not $S^{2d-1}$; the label $S^{2d-1}$ with $d=3$ gives $S^5$ which is the $d=5$ sector, not d=3. Second, for the round sphere $S^{2k-1}$ the Dirac spectrum is symmetric ($\pm\lambda$ in equal-multiplicity pairs), so the standard (unequivariant) APS eta invariant $\eta(0)=0$ for all round odd-dimensional spheres — it cannot select any $n$-values. Third, the specific mod-12 claim for $d=3$ (sector = $S^3$, Dirac eigenvalues $\pm(l+2)$): the tower members have eigenvalues $2$ and $5$ whose residues mod 12 are $\{2,5\}$ — not a special set, and the full spectrum covers all mod-12 residues. The Dirac eigenvalues $2n+k+1$ at the CP-sector tower $n$-values match neither $S(n,d)$ nor any obvious selection condition. The Meta AI mod-12 claim is unsupported. Any meaningful APS application would require specifying a non-standard setting (twisted bundle, equivariant eta, manifold with boundary) — none was provided. (C) *15 $\lambda$-minuscule / d-complete families* (Meta AI): The 15-class theorem is REAL — Proctor (J. Alg. Comb. 9, 61–94, 1999) proves that irreducible d-complete posets fall into exactly 15 classes $\mathcal{C}_1,\ldots,\mathcal{C}_{15}$ (shapes, shifted shapes, birds, insets, banners, swivels, bat, e7(1), and others). However, Meta AI's specific claim — that these 15 families have "Coxeter-number-related $d$-values and minuscule-weight-height $n$-values matching the IDWT tower" — is UNSUPPORTED. Each class $\mathcal{C}_i$ is an INFINITE family parameterized by varying partitions/shapes, not a single $(n,d)$ pair; only $\mathcal{C}_{15}$ (the $\mathrm{E}_7$ minuscule rep $\omega_1$) is a unique poset. The Coxeter numbers of the underlying Lie algebras ($h=12$ for $\mathrm{E}_6$, $h=18$ for $\mathrm{E}_7$, $h=30$ for $\mathrm{E}_8$) do not match the IDWT sector set $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$. The count $15=15$ is a numerical coincidence; the mathematical parameters do not map to the IDWT tower. The specific Lie-theory application is a hallucinated connection. (D) *Spectral-zeros framing* (ChatGPT): "the tower $n$-values satisfy a sector-dependent spectral condition $F(n,d)=0$" — this is a valid restatement of the T0.5 open problem, fully consistent with IDWT (particles are eigenmodes), but adds no new computable content. It reinforces that the arithmetic-search approach may target the wrong function class — the correct $F$ likely comes from the nonlinear IDWT EoM, not a combinatorial formula (consistent with MC-4). Net: all four AI suggestions are closed as null or restatements. Sym$^d$ identification is a useful algebraic reframing; the rest supply hallucinated specifics on a correct general intuition.

**Full-15 battery with bosons included — modular / gcd / closure / significance (all NULL; 2026-06-14).** Prior battery runs filtered $d\ne2$, excluding photon ($n=0$), W ($n=76$), Z ($n=81$), H ($n=95$). This run re-ran the standard tests on the complete 15-particle set (SET15) and the 14-particle set without the photon (SET14), against the corresponding lattice ($n\in[0,95]$ or $[1,95]$, $d\in\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$). All $d=2$ inclusions are unchanged: no new selector found. (A) *Modular banding mod 2..12*: SET14 residue counts range from 2 (mod 2) to 9 (mod 11); SET15 identical except mod 2 unchanged. Adding bosons does not create any clean single-residue band. The mod-12 residue set $\{0,1,3,4,8,9,10,11\}$ (missing $\{2,5,6,7\}$) is not statistically anomalous: significance test against 10 000 random size-14 subsets gives $P(\le\text{obs})=0.50$, $P(\ge\text{obs})=0.83$ — consistent with random. (B) *GCD*: $\gcd$ of all 14 $n$-values is 1; trivial. (C) *Cross-sector $n$ sharing*: no $n$-value appears in more than one sector — all 14 (15 with $n=0$) are distinct across the six sectors. Structural observation, not a selection rule candidate. (D) *Hockey-stick closure from seeds $\{(1,3),(3,4)\}$*: closure (under $n\to n+1$ same sector and $n\to n$ next sector, $n\le95$) contains 380 lattice points, capturing 10/14 SET14 members but missing $(23,10)$, $(76,2)$, $(81,2)$, $(95,2)$; 370 false positives — not selective. (E) *Significance (cardinality)*: for mod $\in\{2,3,4,6,12\}$, the observed residue-set cardinality of SET14 lies at median or above-median of 10 000 random subsets of the same size — no anomaly in any direction. Adding bosons changes none of these conclusions. Recorded so the boson-inclusion gap is closed and the full-15 tests are not re-run.

**Up-quark site formula as a sphere-curvature parallel to the down branch — incomplete, no mechanism (NULL; 2026-06-16).** Tested whether the two heaviest-quark product indices admit a criticality parallel to the down branch's Gegenbauer law. Writing both branches in the single sphere/Gegenbauer parameter $\lambda=(d-2)/2$ over the Kähler sectors $d\in\{4,6,10\}$ ($\lambda=1,2,4$): the **down** indices are $k_0=\lambda^2=\{1,4,16\}=\{n_{\rm down},n_{\rm strange},k_{0,\rm bottom}\}$ exactly (this is §44's $4k_0=(d-2)^2$ rewritten; $16$ is *forced* — the coupling $b_{k_0}(d)$ crosses $\tfrac12$, STEP 26). The **up** site formula $(d-1)(d-2)=\{6,20,72\}$ reproduces $n_{\rm charm}=20$ and $n_{\rm top}=72$, and $(d-1)(d-2)$ is exactly the **scalar curvature of the unit angular sphere $S^{d-1}$** (so charm $=R[S^5]$, top $=R[S^9]$). Two reasons this is not a parallel and not a derivation. (i) **Incomplete at its own base:** $\lambda^2$ reproduces all three down indices, but $(d-1)(d-2)$ at $d=4$ gives $6$, not $n_{\rm up}=3$; no single formula covers all three up indices ($(d-1)(d-2)/2$ fixes up$=3$ but then breaks charm $=10\ne20$). It is a 2-of-3 hit on exactly the two product-form heavy quarks, i.e. a restatement of the anomaly, not a resolution. (ii) **No forcing condition:** down's $16$ falls out of a derived coupling reaching a critical value; "index $=$ scalar curvature" is an identity with no route into the beat-index condition (the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel is a contact coupling with no curvature term). Consistent with §46 (the $b=\tfrac12$ Jacobi-criticality route on $\mathbb{CP}^{d/2}$ is closed — $\tfrac12$ only asymptotically) and with run #6b/§45 (a per-sector spectral condition structurally cannot select the index; the template that grounds the mass is index-blind). Verdict: $d=4$ admits no non-Gegenbauer criticality forcing the top index; $72$ stays a tier-2 count. Kept only as the $\lambda$-unified read (down $=\lambda^2$, up $=R[S^{d-1}]$) plus the 2-of-3 incompleteness, sharper than §44's "reverse-engineered" note. No status edited; no `idwt.py` STEP added (no mechanism, formula incomplete). Recorded so the scalar-curvature reading is not re-derived as a fresh lead.

**$d=2$-reference cross-sector resonance for the off-tower quarks {16,72} (NULL; 2026-06-16).** Tested the hypothesis that the two off-tower quarks — bottom ($k_0=16$, $d=3$) and top ($n=72$, $d=4$) — are fixed by a resonance/comb-lock against the $d=2$ reference scale $m_{\rm scale2}=27.4706$ MeV (which is itself sourced by the quark indices via $g_{22}=(S(n_s,3)-n_u)^2S(n_u-1,4)/2=17^2\cdot5/2=722.5$), rather than by a sector-internal eigenvalue or a count. Three checks, all negative. (i) **Comb-lock ranking.** For each quark-sector index $a$, the nearest $d=2$ tooth ($m_{\rm scale2}\,b(b{+}1)/2$) was found and ranked by $|$fractional mismatch$|$. The off-tower indices are not champions: top $a=72$ ranks 29/70 ($-0.33\%$); bottom $a=16$ ranks 23/32 ($+2.62\%$, among the worst). A genuine comb-lock would put them at the top of the ranking. (ii) **Direct rung alignment of the physical masses.** Nearest $d=2$ rung to the top (172 570 MeV) is $b=112$ at $+0.733\%$ — $1.6\times$ *worse* than the chance expectation ($\sim0.45\%$, mean distance to nearest rung $=$ gap$/4$); nearest rung to the bottom (4183 MeV) is $b=17$ at $+0.478\%$ — $\sim6\times$ better than chance ($\sim2.79\%$), but a single sub-percent near-miss at a non-occupied index. Neither $b=112$ nor $b=17$ is a special/occupied $d=2$ index (the occupied rungs are $W{=}76,Z{=}81,H{=}95$). (iii) **Premise failure.** The hypothesis's physical motivation — "the off-tower quarks are the heaviest, hence nearest the $d=2$/EW reference they help source, hence lock onto it" — fails for the bottom: the top is indeed near the EW scale ($2.15\times m_W$) but the bottom is $0.052\times m_W$ (lighter than the charm–bottom gap), nowhere near the reference. "Off-tower" does not track "near $d=2$." Verdict: the unified $d=2$-lock reading is refuted — the one quark actually near the reference (top) shows no better-than-chance rung alignment, while the bottom's mild $b=17$ near-miss ($17=p$, a $g_{22}$ part) is post-hoc and isolated. The two off-tower quarks do not share a $d=2$-resonance origin; the bottom's index is the sector-internal Gegenbauer beat ($k_0=n_s^2=16$, $4k_0=(d-2)^2$ at $d=10$, §44), unrelated to $d=2$. $72$ stays a tier-2 count; no status edited, no `idwt.py` STEP (null). **Related sub-thread, same date (also NULL):** the binomial "anchor" family — $\{$top,W,Z,H$\}=\{72,76,81,95\}=\{T{-}r{+}1,\,T{-}q,\,T{-}p,\,T{+}a{+}1\}$ off $T=S(n_e,2)=91$ (the compact form already in `idwt.py` lines ~269–313) — was reconsidered as a possible reversal in which the bosons/anchor *generate* the top. It fails on directionality: the only generative mechanism present is the Vandermonde $g$-rule $g(a,b)=a{+}b{-}1$, which runs $72\to W\to Z\to H$ (the bosons are a $g$-cascade seeded by the external top), so the bosons are strictly downstream and cannot source $72$. The anchor identity $72=S(n_e,2)-n_{\rm charm}+1$ is a Layer-1 arithmetic re-description of the output set, not a generator, and $91=C(14,2)$ has no independent standing beyond the $n_W$ cross-check. Connection $\ne$ kinship — the cluster is the same species of cheap lattice coincidence as $16=n_e+n_u$ (which links the electron and the bottom with no physical relation between them). The top–boson clustering is downstream bookkeeping; it does not explain $72$. Do-not-re-run: the bosons-generate-the-top reversal and the $T=91$ anchor as a primary generator. **All-sector rung scan (2026-06-16, NULL):** does the top mass land on a perfect rung $m_{\rm scale_d}S(n,d)$ in ANY sector? No. d=2 $n{=}112$ ($+0.73\%$, worse than chance); d=3 $n{=}59$ ($-1.94\%$); d=4 own sector $n{=}72$ ($+2.20\%$ raw, needs the GTC); d=6 $n{=}126$ ($-0.31\%$, $-1.9\sigma$, $\sim$4× better than chance but $126$ is not a meaningful d=6 index and it is not within PDG error); d=10 $n{=}39$ ($+4.33\%$). The d=5 sector cannot give a clean test — $m_{\rm scale5}\sim7\times10^{-13}$ MeV makes the comb hyperdense at GeV masses, so it matches almost any mass to $<0.1\%$ by chance (the bottom's apparent $+0.027\%$ d=5 "hit" at $n{=}3679$ is exactly this artifact, at the chance baseline, not a real fit). Conclusion: no perfect cross-sector rung for the top; the wrong-sector-bypass-as-mass-match hypothesis is closed.

### §16. Mass uniqueness test for sector assignments

**Question.** Do the 15 observed SM particle masses, together with the IDWT mass formula m = S(n,d) × m_scale_d and sector scales derived from m_e and the seeds, uniquely identify the (n,d) sector assignments?

**Tests performed** (2026-05-29):

**Within Σ_indices × D only:** For each particle, given the known n, the known d is the unique minimiser of the log-residual |log(S(n,d)×m_scale_d / m_obs)|². Margin of uniqueness: 10³–10⁹× over the next-best d. Conversely, given the known d, the known n is the unique minimiser. No pairwise swap of the global assignment reduces the total squared log-residual (known total: 1.35×10⁻⁴, essentially zero). 100,000 random alternative global bijections all have residuals ≥ 10⁵× worse.

**Full scan (n ∈ [1,500], d ∈ D):** For every particle, there exist non-Σ_indices n-values within factor 2 of the observed mass in some sector. Examples: (59,4) hits W mass within 0.7%; (126,6) hits top mass within 0.4%; (11,2) hits tau mass within 2%. These are not tower outputs.

**Conclusion.** Mass matching with IDWT-derived scales does not uniquely identify Σ_indices at the individual level. The discrimination is collective: the Σ_pairs assignment achieves sub-percent accuracy for all 15 masses simultaneously — a constraint that random or arbitrary alternative assignments fail by factors of 10⁵. The sector assignments are over-determined by both the generation tower (algebraic derivation from seeds) and the mass data (empirical confirmation). Neither source alone is sufficient to close the argument: the tower provides the structured derivation; the masses confirm it cannot be replaced by an unstructured alternative. The sector-assignment derivation remains open but the empirical case for the known assignment is strong.

### §17. Prime-factor count of mass eigenvalues Ω(S(n,d)) vs sector dimension d

**Observed (Meta, 2026-05-29; evaluated 2026-05-29).** For four of the stable pairs, the total prime-factor count with multiplicity Ω(S(n,d)) equals d: strange (4,3), charm (20,4), electron (13,6), tau (23,10). The other 11 particles have Ω(S(n,d)) ≠ d.

**Assessment: likely numerological.** Ω(m) is an arithmetic function with no connection to the IDWT eigenmode equations, coupling structure, or sector geometry. A search over all (n,d) with d ∈ D and n ≤ 200 finds many pairs satisfying Ω(C(N,d))=d; the physical particles are not distinguished within that set. The "carries" framing from Kummer's theorem is a computation device — it involves adding integers in prime-number bases, which has no physical meaning. Meta's interpretation that the Ω=d particles are "pure simplex images of seeds" is also incorrect: the electron (n_e = n_ν₁ + n_up = 13) has an additive step. No mechanism connecting Ω to d has been identified. Recorded as a null-context numerical coincidence. Status: ❓

### §18. Adjacent-sector simplex ratio identity

**Theorem (2026-05-29).** For any positive integer n and sector dimension d:

S(n,d) / S(n,d+1) = (d+1) / (n+d)

**Proof.** S(n,d) = C(n+d−1, d), S(n,d+1) = C(n+d, d+1). The ratio:
C(n+d−1,d)/C(n+d,d+1) = [(n+d−1)!/(d!(n−1)!)] × [(d+1)!(n−1)!/(n+d)!] = (d+1)/(n+d). □

A clean ⭐ combinatorial identity relating adjacent-sector mode counts.

**Sector-ladder reading and pattern search (2026-06-04).** Rearranged, §18 is the multiplicative recursion $S(n,d+1)=S(n,d)\cdot(n+d)/(d+1)$ — the across-sector generator of the simplex table at fixed $n$, dual to the additive hockey-stick $S(n,d)=S(n,d-1)+S(n-1,d)$ (across $n$ at fixed $d$) on which the generation tower is built. Together they are the two Pascal recursions that generate the entire $S(n,d)$ array. Both were verified on all 15 physical $(n,d)$ pairs (14/14 for $d\ge 2$). A search for whether §18 constrains the physical mode set returned null: as an identity valid for every $(n,d)$ it cannot distinguish co-fixed-points from any other pair, and the $d=3$ selection test confirms no separation (the step $(n+d)/(d+1)$ runs $1,\,5/4,\,3/2,\,7/4,\,2$ for $n=1..5$, selected and unselected interleaved). Two isolated coincidences — the down quark has $n+d=4=n_s$, the tau's step is $(n+d)/(d+1)=3=n_u$ — form no pattern. Net positive content: the multiplicative-dual reading above; the null half is recorded in §15.

### §19. Sector set D as a function of n_s

**Conjecture / Pattern (2026-05-29).** The active sector set satisfies:

D = {2} ∪ {n_s−1, n_s, n_s+1, n_s+2} ∪ {2(n_s+1)}

For n_s=4: D = {2} ∪ {3,4,5,6} ∪ {10} = {2,3,4,5,6,10}. ✓

The three pieces have individual derivations:
- **{2}**: the EM sector CP¹, U(1)_EM; fixed as the reference sector (derived from T15 and the photon as the d=2 n=0 mode).
- **{n_s−1, n_s, n_s+1, n_s+2}** = {3,4,5,6}: the consecutive matter quartet — derived below.
- **{2(n_s+1)}** = {10}: the Gegenbauer-critical terminal sector, b_{k₀}=1/2 exactly at d=2(n_s+1) (T5). Derived.

**Derivation of the consecutive matter quartet (🔵, 2026-06-01).**

The complex Hopf chain $S^1 \to S^{2k+1} \to \mathbb{CP}^k$ produces Hopf pairs at each level $k$:
- $k=1$: total space $S^3$ (d=3), base $\mathbb{CP}^1$ (d=2, the gauge sector)
- $k=2$: total space $S^5$ (d=5), base $\mathbb{CP}^2$ (d=4)
- $k=3$: total space $S^7$ (d=7, excluded), base $\mathbb{CP}^3$ (d=6, terminal)

The gauge sector d=2 (CP¹ of the k=1 Hopf base) separates from the matter sectors. The matter quartet consists of all total spaces and non-terminal bases after d=2: $\{3, 4, 5, 6\}$.

Rule A terminates the chain when the base sector CP^{n_s-1} appears (real dimension $d_{\rm term} = 2(n_s-1)$), because $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^{n_s-1}) = n_s$ forces $g_{d_{\rm term}} = 1/n_s = $ composite ratio. For $n_s=4$: d_term $= 2\times3 = 6$ (CP³, $\chi=4=n_s$). ✓

The matter quartet runs from d=3 (first total space, always fixed by the Hopf chain) to d=$2(n_s-1)$ (terminal base). Its length is:
$$|{\rm quartet}| = 2(n_s-1) - 3 + 1 = 2n_s - 4.$$

The **self-consistency requirement** is that the matter quartet has exactly $n_s$ members — the composite n_s=4 determines the number of matter sectors:
$$2n_s - 4 = n_s \quad\Longrightarrow\quad n_s = 4. \qquad \text{⭐}$$

This is an independent derivation of $n_s=4$: the unique seed value for which the Hopf chain produces exactly $n_s$ consecutive matter sectors before Rule A termination. At $n_s=4$ the quartet is $\{3,4,5,6\} = \{n_s-1, n_s, n_s+1, n_s+2\}$, centered at $n_s + 1/2$ with $n_s-1=3$ (observable space) as the first element.

The $n_s=4$ Hopf chain gives exactly 2 complete Hopf pairs for matter: $(d=3, d=4)$ = quark sectors and $(d=5, d=6)$ = lepton sectors. This 2+2 pairing is why there are two quark multiplets (down-type, up-type) and two lepton multiplets (neutrino, charged) — a structural consequence of $n_s=4$ rather than an independent input.

**Status: 🔵** (quartet length = n_s derivation from Hopf chain + Rule A; the self-consistency requirement is motivated but not yet a theorem — it needs a derivation of WHY the composite n_s must equal the matter sector count). Verified for $n_s = 3,4,5,6$: only $n_s=4$ gives quartet length = $n_s$ while also placing observable space (d=3) as the first matter sector.

**Self-consistency of n_s=4.** The sector formula reveals two conditions that simultaneously select n_s=4:
1. Matter quartet width equals composite value: |{n_s−1,...,n_s+2}| = 4 = n_s (true only at n_s=4).
2. Matter quartet starts at spacetime: n_s−1 = 3 iff n_s = 4.

No other value of n_s satisfies both simultaneously. Both conditions are not yet derived from IDWT dynamics. (The primary derivation of n_s=4 is T4, Part 9.)

**Addendum — seed re-rooting to {1, 3}: verified (2026-06-11, Fedge proposal).** The subtraction step $n_u = n_s - 1$ has no independent justification (Part 2 §6 records it as lattice-closure consistency presented as derivation "for brevity"). Tested: take the seeds to be $\{1, 3\}$ and derive $4 = 1 + 3$, eliminating the subtraction. Result — everything regenerates, and the seed pair is better grounded than $\{1, 4\}$: **(i)** the STEP 1 compact binomial form reproduces all 14 single-mode indices from $(a,b) = (3, 4)$ with $b := 1 + a$; **(ii)** $a = 3$ carries three convergent anchors — $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2) = N_c = 3$ (T15, geometric), the unique single-kernel-application image of the ground seed ($\Delta N = +2$: $N{=}0 \to N{=}2 \to n{=}3$, kernel-dynamical), and the T4 double-degeneracy partner; **(iii)** $4 = 1+3$ is the offset-additive composite (the MC-4.4 kernel two-density reading, 🔶), and the offset channel flips level parity ($N_{\rm comp} = N_1 + N_2 + 1$: even + even → odd), which is exactly how the odd-$l$ tree (the strange index) is sourced despite $l$-parity blocking single-mode kernel steps — the {1,4} seed pair's "mutual stabilisation" awkwardness (two seeds in disconnected parity trees) dissolves: $\{1,3\}$ is parity-pure, kernel-connected, and the odd tree is generated, not seeded; **(iv)** T4 ($4/7$ double degeneracy, unique hit at $n=4$ over $n=2..50$), the Gegenbauer crossing $b_n(3)=b_n(4)$ (unique at $n=4$), the matter-quartet condition $2n-4=n$, and the muon fixed point $S(4,4)=35$ all hold as uniqueness certificates of the derived $4$ rather than definitions; **(v)** all six couplings remain functions of $N_c = a$ alone (T15 Step 5; $g_{33}g_{44} = 96$ verified). What re-rooting does NOT fix: the three +1 offsets, the anchor $T = C(p{+}a{+}1, 2)$, and the firing-set selection (T0.5 core) — unchanged. Note on stability: seed status is generative (tower root), not dynamical — it does not by itself confer stability; the ground seed $(1,3)$ is protected by having no downward channel (STEP 64), not by seedhood. Re-rooting reshapes the protection question: $u$'s required absence $(1,4)$ is a sector *ground state*, qualitatively unlike the mid-tower absences $(11,6), (8,5), (13,5), (20,5)$ — whether the $(1,d)$ modes are condensate background (sourcing $\lambda_d$, which is ground-state-sourced) rather than available final states is an open ❓ worth pursuing.

**Candidate: n_s as the d=6 CP³ well ground-state degeneracy (❓).** A further angle on n_s=4. The geometry labels (CP^n, S^n) describe the local symmetry of the potential minimum near r=0, not global topology (Part 1 Foundation, on the well-shape reading), so the d=6 sector has a CP³-shaped well sitting in flat ℝ⁶. For a CP^n well the ground-state degeneracy (number of fixed points) is χ(CP^n)=n+1; for CP³, χ=4, so n_s=4 records the d=6 well's ground-state degeneracy. Open: the causal link from the d=6 well degeneracy to the d=3 seed — the tower connects them through n_μ=S(n_s,4), but the d=6→d=3 direction needs justification. State as candidate only, not a closed proof. The S(2,3)=4 route is circular (writing S(2,3) presupposes the d=3 sector and 2=n_d+1) — do not use it.

**Addendum — generic-a consistency census of the re-rooted tower: the selective web pins a = 3 twenty-fold (2026-06-12, Part 1).** Follow-up to the {1, 3} re-rooting above. The full tower was regenerated from the seed pair {1, a} with composite b := 1 + a, for a = 1..12, and every documented internal cross-check of the tower was classified as either an *identity in a* (tower grammar, blind to the seed) or a *selective relation* (holds only at specific a — these constrain the seed). Results:

- **Identity class (5 relations, hold for all a):** the Pascal/muon relation $s = q + r$; $n_H = n_u + n_{\rm charm} + n_{\rm top}$ (given the compact forms); the ν-spacing $n_{\nu_3} - n_{\nu_2} = n_{\nu_1} - a$; $n_W = T - q$; $g_{33}g_{44} = b^3 a/2$.
- **Selective class (20 relations): all 20 hold at a = 3 and only there in the scanned range,** with a single stray partial hit ($n_W = n_{\rm top} + 4$ also holds at a = 2, where it is not accompanied by any of the other 19). The selective relations include the τ double-derivation ($n_\tau = n_{\rm charm} + n_u \Leftrightarrow n_{\rm charm} = 2n_{\nu_1} \Leftrightarrow a = 3$), the Z and H Vandermonde forms ($q - p = 5$ and $q - p = a + 2$, each a=3-only), the top Euler product, the §10 coincidences (n_top = n_μ+n_ν₂+n_ν₃, n_H = n_top+n_τ, n_e+n_τ = (b+2)², n_ν₁+n_ν₃ = 2^{b+1}, …), the k₀ pair b² = n_e+a and b² = n_charm−b, the T4 unique hit at n = b, the Gegenbauer crossing at n = b, and the matter-quartet condition 2b−4 = b.
- **Structural gain of the re-rooting:** under b = a + 1 the muon double-derivation $S(b,4) = S(b,3) + S(a,4)$ *is* the hockey-stick/Pascal identity — it moves from the selective class (where it sat under the old {1, 4} root as "the coincidence that forced n_s = 4") into the grammar. The re-rooting converts one certificate into an identity and leaves the remaining twenty as genuine over-determination of the seed.

Honest limits: the 20 selective relations are not all independent (e.g. S1⇔S2; the H-additive form follows from the top form; the §25 single-input addendum already audited the k₀ pair to two independent coincidences), so "twenty-fold" counts documented relations, not independent constraints; the scan range is a ≤ 12 (several relations are individually proved unique for all n_s < 500 in earlier entries); and the census constrains the SEED only — it says nothing about the per-(n,d) firing-set selection (T0.5), which is untouched (see the run-#8 conjunction null, §15). Status: verified arithmetic within the scanned range; the census statement itself is a structural observation about over-determination of a = 3, complementing the kernel-dynamical and geometric anchors of the re-rooting addendum above.

### §20. Sector mode functions: explicit harmonic forms, and the saturating-potential binding deficit

**Context (2026-05-29).** Task #1 of the foundational program: write the sector mode functions χ_{n,d} explicitly as eigenfunctions of H_d, in a form that permits normalization, d=3 projection amplitudes, and kernel matrix elements. Two operators appear in the documents and they are **not** the same:

- **Harmonic** H_d^harm = −Δ_d + λ_d r² — the monomial / IDOS operator the mass formula rests on.
- **Saturating** H_d^sat = −Δ_d + λ_d r²/(1+r²) — the confining ansatz of Part 4 §3.10, introduced to obtain a discrete spectrum with finite localization length L_d and continuum threshold λ_d.

**Positive result — explicit harmonic mode functions (⭐ identity).** The eigenfunctions of H_d^harm are exact:
$$\chi_{n_r,l,m}(r,\Omega) = N_{n_r,l}\; r^{l}\, L_{n_r}^{(l+d/2-1)}(w\,r^2)\, e^{-w\,r^2/2}\, Y_{lm}(\Omega), \qquad w=\sqrt{\lambda_d},$$
with level N = 2n_r + l, energy E = √λ_d (4n_r + 2l + d) = √λ_d(2N + d), level degeneracy C(N+d−1, d−1), and cumulative count (IDOS) through level n−1 equal to S(n,d) = C(n+d−1, d). The full d-dimensional normalization ∫|R|²r^{d−1}dr = 1 gives the closed form
$$N_{n_r,l}^2 = \frac{2\,w^{\,l+d/2}\,n_r!}{\Gamma(n_r+l+d/2)}.$$
This is the explicit form requested by Task #1 for the monomial picture. The S(n,d)-dimensional "mode n" is the space of degree-(n−1) homogeneous polynomials in d+1 sector coordinates (dim Sym^{n−1}(ℝ^{d+1}) = S(n,d)). These functions are ready for use in kernel overlap integrals. (Part E).

**Structural finding — the saturating potential does not host the tower.** With the **correct** d-dimensional radial reduction (u = r^{(d−1)/2}R, l=0 centrifugal coefficient A = (d−1)(d−3)/4), the saturating operator H_d^sat has the following count of l=0 bound states below threshold λ_d (deeply-bound count, box-size independent):

| d | λ_d | A=(d−1)(d−3)/4 | E_0^harm = d√λ_d | deeply-bound l=0 states | overlap with harmonic ground |
|---|------|----------------|------------------|------------------------|------------------------------|
| 2 | 50.72 | −0.25 | 14.24 | 3 | 0.973 |
| 3 | 4.82 | 0 | 6.59 | 1 | 0.778 |
| 4 | 1.73 | 0.75 | 5.26 | 0 (one marginal threshold state) | 0.096 |
| 5 | 0.164 | 2.00 | 2.02 | 0 | — |
| 6 | 0.25 | 3.75 | 3.00 | 0 | — |
| 10 | 0.25 | 15.75 | 5.00 | 0 | — |

Three facts, in increasing severity:

1. **The harmonic ground state is bound (E_0^harm < λ_d) only when λ_d > d² — i.e. only for d=2.** For every matter sector d ∈ {3,4,5,6,10} the harmonic ground-state energy d√λ_d lies *above* the saturating continuum threshold λ_d. The harmonic well λ_d r² and the saturating well λ_d r²/(1+r²) agree only near the origin; the matter-sector ground states do not fit inside the region where they agree.

2. **For d = 5, 6, 10 the saturating operator has zero l=0 bound states — analytically certain, not numerical.** V_eff(r) = λ_d − λ_d/(1+r²) + A/r² ≥ λ_d everywhere whenever A ≥ λ_d, and A = 2, 3.75, 15.75 all exceed λ_d ≈ 0.16–0.25. The three sectors that host the neutrinos (d=5), electron and muon (d=6), and tau (d=10) therefore have **no localized s-wave bound state of the confining ansatz at all**.

3. **The §3.10 self-consistency that fixes λ_d closes only under the harmonic assumption it then contradicts.** §3.10.3 sets ⟨r²⟩_d = d/(2√λ_d) using the *harmonic* ground state, giving λ_d = (g_dd/2)^{2/3}. Substituting the actual saturating ground state (where one exists) gives a very different ⟨r²⟩ (e.g. d=4: 336 vs harmonic 1.52), so g_dd⟨r²⟩/d does not return λ_d. The derivation is internally consistent only in the harmonic limit, which the matter sectors violate.

**Reading.** The IDWT mode functions are the harmonic (monomial) functions — that picture is explicit, normalizable, and reproduces S(n,d) exactly. The saturating potential V_d = λ_d r²/(1+r²) cannot be the operator whose bound states are those modes: it supports at most a few deeply-bound states (3, 1, 0, 0, 0, 0 for d = 2,3,4,5,6,10) rather than the required infinite tower, and none in the three deepest matter sectors. This corroborates and sharpens the existing flag MC-2 (potential form is an ansatz) and the §3.13 proof correction. The resolution is in the section below.

**Resolution (2026-05-29) — flat harmonic self-binding; remove the saturation, not the flat sectors (✅).** The ontology constraint is binding: the sectors are *macroscopic, flat, extended* spatial dimensions (a d=2 photon propagates in our 3-space; the electron has a physical d=6 orbit). They are **not** tiny compact/curled dimensions, so the deficit must not be cured by compactifying the sector. The actual culprit is narrower: the deficit is caused **entirely by the saturating denominator (1+r²)**, which Part 4 §3.10.2 never derives. The kernel self-consistency derives only the near-origin r² term; the saturation is the unjustified MC-2 ansatz.

The **pure harmonic self-binding** V_d = λ_d r² in flat, extended ℝ^d cures the deficit while keeping the sectors flat:

- **Confining, infinitely many bound states, every sector.** V → ∞, so the spectrum is purely discrete (σ_ess = ∅, no continuum) and the full simplex tower is bound in all of d = 2,3,4,5,6,10 — the d=5,6,10 deficit does not occur (verified). The particle is a Gaussian-localized standing wave *within* the extended flat sector, exactly as a bound electron is localized inside extended 3-space.
- **λ_d derivation becomes exact.** §3.10.3 set ⟨r²⟩_d = d/(2√λ_d) using the harmonic ground state; with the pure harmonic well this is the *actual* ground state (verified exact for d=3,4,5,6,10), so λ_d = (g_dd/2)^{2/3} closes without circularity.
- **IDOS = S(n,d) exactly.** d-dim isotropic-HO level degeneracy C(N+d−1,d−1), cumulative S(n,d). Spectrum-generating symmetry SU(d) ⊂ SO(d+1).

**T-S1 is the dynamical-symmetry repackaging, not a compact dimension.** On S^d the Dirac operator has eigenvalues ±(k+d/2) with multiplicity 2^{⌊d/2⌋}C(k+d−1,d−1); the cumulative positive count is 2^{⌊d/2⌋}S(n,d), i.e. **per spinor component exactly S(n,d), for every d ∈ D** (verified n=1…39). This S^d is the **SO(d+1) dynamical-symmetry / spectrum-generating sphere** of the flat oscillator (a representation-theory statement), **not** a physical curled sphere. Each particle (n,d) sits at shell (n−1)+d/2. T-S1 (Part 2/Part 8, currently only d=3,5) extends to all six sectors in this reading.

**Mass law, not selector (run #6b, 2026-06-05).** Because the cumulative count is $2^{\lfloor d/2\rfloor}S(n,d)$ at *every* shell n, T-S1 assigns a mass to each candidate (n,d) — it **grounds the mass but does not select which n are physical**. Tested directly: no sector Dirac/Laplace spectral condition (on $S^d$ or $\mathbb{CP}^{d/2}$, five conditions across CP²/CP³/CP⁵/S⁵) picks out the observed per-sector n's without over-generating (§15, run #6b). The sector geometry *seeds* the per-sector generators through its Euler characteristic (§15, run #6), but selection is a separate dynamical question — co-fixed-point stability (MC-4) — not a spectral mark. Future work should not re-chase a per-sector spectral selector; the template that grounds the mass is structurally the one thing that cannot select the index.

**Even sectors.** Under flat harmonic binding the mass count is the SU(d) oscillator IDOS for *all* d, so d=4,6,10 need **no** separate CP^{d/2} Dirac computation. The complex structure ℝ^d ≅ ℂ^{d/2} furnishes CP^{d/2} as the **Kähler/chirality** structure (γ₅, χ(CP^{d/2}) = N_c at d=4, = n_s at d=6) layered on the same flat oscillator — consistent with the existing χ usage. This dissolves the earlier "carrier manifold" residue.

**Mode functions** are the flat harmonic eigenfunctions (Laguerre × Gaussian, §20 Part E, with closed-form norms) — not a proxy after all; they are the genuine self-binding modes. The spinor-harmonic / S^d picture is their SO(d+1)-covariant relabeling.

**Decision (2026-05-29) — L_d = λ_d^{−1/4}, the harmonic oscillator length.** Under the current construction L_d appears in two places: (U1) gravity V_7 = L_4 L_5 L_6 L_10⁴ → G_N = G_∞/V_7; (U2) the KK/curvature gap (d+1)/L_d² and R/4 = m(m+1)/(4L_d²). (It formerly also entered a dimensional-visibility amplitude and the Part 7 §2.9 spurion form; both were removed with the visibility apparatus.) With harmonic confinement the ground state is the Gaussian exp(−√λ_d r²/2), whose localization length is the **oscillator length L_d = λ_d^{−1/4}** — not the threshold length λ_d^{−1/2} (that is an exponential-tail length the harmonic well has no continuum to produce). The reason this is the correct choice:

- It is the genuine length of the harmonic ground state we adopted; λ_d^{−1/2} belongs to the rejected saturating well.

Recomputed values (L_d = λ_d^{−1/4}): L_2 = 0.375, L_3 = 0.675, L_4 = 0.872, L_5 = 1.571, L_6 = 1.414, L_10 = 1.414. Downstream:
- **V_7 = 7.74** (was 113). Not a broken prediction: G_∞ is underived/free, so V_7's absolute value only rescales G_∞. The structure G_N = G_∞/V_7 (product of seven sector lengths) is unchanged. Note: comparing G_N to sector coupling constants is a category error in IDWT — they are different types of quantity; V_7 is not "why gravity is weak", it is the geometric factor connecting G_∞ to what a 3D observer measures.
- **KK gap (d+1)/L_d² = (d+1)√λ_d** (21, 9, 6.6, 2.4, 3.5, 5.5 in sector units) — positive and O(few), so excited modes remain gapped; no KK tower. Fine.

L_d = λ_d^{−1/4} and V_7 ≈ 7.74 are now the values used throughout the main documents.

### §20a. T2 kernel overlap of the mode functions, and the nature of the CKM formula (2026-06-04)

First use of the explicit §20 mode functions in a kernel matrix element. The T2 density-density kernel is K = g (ξ·ξ′)² |Ψ|²|Ψ′|². Its overlap between two harmonic modes factorizes under isotropy:
$$O_{ij} = \int\!\!\int (\xi\cdot\xi')^2\,|\chi_i(\xi)|^2|\chi_j(\xi')|^2\,d\xi\,d\xi' = \frac{\langle r^2\rangle_i\,\langle r^2\rangle_j}{d}, \qquad \langle r^2\rangle_{\text{(shell }N)} = \frac{2N+d}{2\sqrt{\lambda_d}}.$$
(The ⟨r²⟩ formula is verified against direct numerical integration of the Laguerre×Gaussian modes to machine precision — confirming the §20 functions are correct and usable. ⭐ for the overlap identity.)

**Consequence — the CKM formula is state-counting, not a kernel overlap (🔶).** O_ij scales as the mode index n¹ (it is a wavefunction overlap, set by ⟨r²⟩). The combinatorial CKM formula |V_ij|² = S(n_lighter,d)/S(n_heavier,d) scales as n^d (n⁴ in d=4): for the up-type quarks the kernel ratio and the simplex ratio differ by ×112 (u–c), ×40 (c–t), ×4440 (u–t). Therefore |V_ij|² is **not** the kernel matrix element ⟨χ|K|χ⟩ — it is a mode-count (IDOS / density-of-states) ratio, a phase-space statement (rate ∝ density of final states). This closes the Part 6 item "CKM not derived from kernel" in the negative: the T2 overlap gives n¹, the formula needs n^d. The formula stays empirically good (Part 3 §0.8); its mechanism is counting, not the dynamical overlap. The overlap O_ij itself (∝ ⟨r²⟩_i⟨r²⟩_j) is the genuine kernel object and is what enters dynamical quantities (e.g. the a₄-gauge integrals, Part 4 §3.12.4).
