### §34. T0 spectral-triple foundations: summability, spectral dimension, compact resolvent, self-adjointness (2026-06-13, `files/idwt.py` STEP 80)

Closes or advances four of the seven Part 9 T0 open items for the **physically relevant operator** — the internal Dirac operator $D_{\rm int}=\bigoplus_{d\in D}D_d$ on the finite active sector product (equivalently the projected $P_{\xi^0}DP_{\xi^0}$ of T0), whose eigenvalues are the masses $m_{{\rm scale},d}\,S(n,d)$.

**Item 3 — $p$-summability (✅, computed).** $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}\sim n^d/d!$, so $\zeta_d(s)=\sum_{n\ge1}S(n,d)^{-s}$ has abscissa of convergence $1/d$; equivalently $K_d(t)=\sum_n e^{-tS(n,d)}\sim a_0^{(d)}t^{-1/d}$ with $a_0^{(d)}=\Gamma(1+1/d)(d!)^{1/d}$ (matches the T0/T14 Weyl coefficient; the $d=2$ ratio $K_2/(a_0 t^{-1/2})\to1$, $=0.99920$ at $t=10^{-6}$). Since $D$ is finite (6 sectors), $\zeta_{\rm int}=\sum_{d\in D}\zeta_d$ has abscissa $\max_d 1/d=1/2$, attained at $d=2$. So $|D_{\rm int}|^{-p}$ is trace-class iff $p>1/2$ — the triple is $p$-summable for every $p>1/2$, summability dimension $1/2$.

**Item 7 — spectral dimension (✅ computed, with a correction to the stated expectation).** $d_s=$ rightmost pole of $\zeta_{\rm int}=1/2$, set by the slowest-growing (dominant) sector $d=2$. This is the summability dimension of the **mass operator** (eigenvalues = masses $\sim$ cumulative state counts $\sim n^d$), **not** the geometric dimension of $M_\infty$. T0 item 7's expectation "$d_s$ equals the effective dimension of $M_\infty$" therefore does not hold: because IDWT identifies mass with a cumulative count, $|D|$ grows far faster than the Weyl growth of a manifold Laplacian, pushing the zeta pole down to $1/2$. (Flagged for the T0 writeup.)

**Item 2 — compact resolvent (✅ internal, with the standard spacetime caveat).** Each $D_d$ has purely discrete spectrum with $S(n,d)\to\infty$ ($\sigma_{\rm ess}=\emptyset$, Part 4 §3.13); a finite direct sum of such operators has discrete spectrum diverging to $\infty$, so $(D_{\rm int}-z)^{-1}$ is compact. The full $D$ on $M_\infty$ includes the spacetime part $-i\gamma^\mu\partial_\mu$ on $\mathbb{R}^{3,1}$ (continuous spectrum), so the full resolvent is not compact — compactness is a statement about the internal/sector operator, exactly as for any spacetime spectral triple.

**Item 1 — self-adjointness (✅ for the physical operator; full $\infty$-dim $M_\infty$ open).** Each $D_d$ is a Dirac-type operator on the complete flat manifold $\mathbb{R}^d$ with confining potential $V_d=\lambda_d r^2$. The free Dirac operator on a complete manifold is essentially self-adjoint on $C_c^\infty$ (Chernoff, finite propagation speed); the confining $r^2$ potential is the relativistic (Dirac) oscillator, ESA on $C_c^\infty$ — the squared operator is a Schrödinger operator with potential $\to+\infty$ at infinity, hence limit-point at infinity (Faris–Lavine). A finite direct sum of ESA operators is ESA, and the spacetime free Dirac operator is ESA (Chernoff), so the full physical operator (finite active product $\times$ spacetime) is ESA. **Residual:** the genuinely infinite-dimensional $M_\infty$ (all coordinate sectors, $d\to\infty$) is the open part T0 flags; the physical spectrum uses only the finite active $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$, where ESA is rigorous.

**Item 5 — KO-dimension (obstruction located, not closed).** The naive count of per-sector real dimensions mod 8 is $\{d \bmod 8\} = \{2,3,4,5,6,2\}$, summing to $22 \equiv 6 \pmod 8$. But assembling a single KO-dimension needs a global real structure $J$, and that is structurally obstructed in two sectors: $d=4$ ($\mathbb{CP}^2$) is **spin$^c$, not spin** ($\mathbb{CP}^n$ is spin iff $n$ is odd, since $c_1=(n+1)H$; $n=2$ fails), so it carries a spin$^c$ Dirac operator but no canonical real structure; and $d=5$ ($S^5$) admits **no charge-conjugation $C$** (the same fact that forbids $0\nu\beta\beta$, Part 8), so no Majorana-type real structure. So item 5 is not merely "uncomputed" — the framework's real structure is sector-dependent and obstructed at $d=4,5$, which is physically meaningful (it is tied to the chirality / Majorana-absence structure), not a single integer waiting to be filled in. The spin sectors are $d\in\{2,3,5,6,10\}$ ($\mathbb{CP}^1,S^3,S^5,\mathbb{CP}^3,\mathbb{CP}^5$); only $d=4$ is spin$^c$-only.

**Items 4, 6 — close by standard NCG (2026-06-13, natural smooth subalgebra).** A spectral triple with compact resolvent (item 2) and bounded commutators $[D,a]$ yields a Fredholm module ($F=D|D|^{-1}$, $[F,a]$ compact; Connes) — **item 4 ✅**. On the natural smooth subalgebra ($C^\infty$ of bounded gradient $\otimes$ constant matrices), $[D,a]=\gamma^\mu(\partial_\mu a)$ is bounded (matrix factor constant), and the iterated $\delta^k(a)$ ($\delta=[|D|,\cdot]$) are higher-derivative multiplications, all bounded — **item 6 ✅** (standard regularity of the smooth algebra). The only residual for both is fixing the smooth subalgebra precisely (a Fréchet/bounded-derivative completion), a definitional choice, not an obstruction. **All seven T0 items are now resolved for the physical internal triple** (with the caveats: spacetime continuum, full $\infty$-dim $M_\infty$, KO obstruction, smooth-subalgebra choice). Written into Part 9 T0.

**Part 8 §14.3 consistency check (resolved, no conflict).** The flag — does STEP 81's observable SO(3)$\subset$SO(6) coincide with Part 8 §14.3's SU(4)$\supset$SU(3)$\supset$SO(3) orbital chain — resolves cleanly: the two decompose **different representation spaces**. Part 8's $\mathrm{Sym}^L(\mathbb{C}^4)$ (the SU(4) spinor symmetric powers, dim $\binom{L+3}{3}$; cumulative $\binom{L+4}{4}$, which skips 18564) classifies the low-lying orbital/bonding states (chemistry $s,p,d,f$); STEP 81's $\mathbb{R}^6$ oscillator (the SO(6) vector, level dim $\binom{N+5}{5}$; cumulative $=S(n,6)$) is the sector-mode count carrying the mass. Both use the same physical observable SO(3); there is no inconsistency. Only the oscillator reproduces $S(n,d)$, so it is the mass-bearing decomposition.

**Net.** All seven T0 items resolved for the physical finite-active internal operator (items 1–4, 6, 7 with the stated caveats; item 5 obstruction located). The one substantive correction: item 7's spectral dimension is $1/2$ (the $d=2$-dominated mass-count summability), not the geometric dimension. **Written into Part 9 T0 (2026-06-13, Fedge-authorized):** all seven items updated with the labels above and the item-7 correction (items 1–4, 6, 7 ✅ for the physical triple with stated caveats; item 5 obstruction located).

**Addendum — the smooth subalgebra named precisely; items 4 and 6 made unconditional (2026-06-14).** The residual flagged for items 4 and 6 was "fix the smooth subalgebra precisely." The correct choice is
$$\mathcal{A}=C^\infty_b\!\bigl(M_\infty^{\rm phys}\bigr)\otimes\bigoplus_{d\in D}\mathcal{M}_{n_d}(\mathbb{C}),\qquad C^\infty_b=\{f\in C^\infty:\ \partial^\alpha f\in L^\infty\ \forall\alpha\},$$
the smooth functions all of whose derivatives are bounded, tensored with the constant matrix factor, on the finite-dimensional physical manifold $M_\infty^{\rm phys}=\mathbb{R}^{3,1}\times\prod_{d\in D}\Xi_d$ (the genuinely infinite-dimensional $M_\infty$ stays item 1's residual). Three facts make this the right algebra and close the residual.

1. **$\mathcal{A}$ is a Fréchet pre-$C^*$-algebra.** With the seminorms $p_\alpha(f)=\|\partial^\alpha f\|_\infty$, $C^\infty_b$ is a Fréchet $*$-algebra, and it is spectrally invariant in its $C^*$-closure $C_b(M_\infty^{\rm phys})$: if $f\in C^\infty_b$ with $\inf|f|>0$ then by Faà di Bruno every derivative of $1/f$ is a polynomial in the $\partial^\alpha f$ divided by powers of $f$, hence bounded, so $1/f\in C^\infty_b$ (checked symbolically). Spectral invariance is exactly what makes $\mathcal{A}$ carry the same $K$-theory/$K$-homology as its closure, so the Fredholm-module class of item 4 is well-defined on $\mathcal{A}$.

2. **The confining potential is invisible to every commutator.** $D=D_{\rm free}+V$ with $V=\bigoplus_d\lambda_d r_d^2$ a multiplication operator. For $a\in\mathcal{A}$, $V$ and $a$ are both multiplications and commute, so $[D,a]=[D_{\rm free},a]=\gamma^A(\partial_A a)$ — bounded because $\nabla a$ is bounded, and independent of $\lambda_d$. The potential shapes the spectrum (it is what supplies the compact resolvent of item 2) but never enters $[D,a]$ or the iterated $\delta^k(a)$. So items 4 and 6 reduce to the standard flat-space Dirac result, with confinement contributing only the compactness item 4 needs.

3. **Items 4 and 6 then hold unconditionally on $\mathcal{A}$.** Item 4: internal compact resolvent (item 2) $+$ bounded $[D,a]$ $\Rightarrow$ $[F,a]$ compact ($F=D|D|^{-1}$), so $(\mathcal{A},\mathcal{H}_{\rm int},F)$ is a Fredholm module. Item 6: since $V$ is order $0$ it leaves the principal symbol of $|D|$ equal to $|\xi|$, so $\delta(a)=[|D|,a]$ is an order-$0$ pseudodifferential operator (bounded) and every $\delta^k(a)$ is order $0$; hence $a,[D,a]\in\bigcap_k\operatorname{Dom}(\delta^k)$ — regular. Honest caveat: the coordinate functions $x^A$ are *not* in $C^\infty_b$ (they are unbounded), but $[D,x^A]=\gamma^A$ is bounded, so the metric/Connes-distance content lives in the usual larger operator system with $x^A$ affiliated; $\mathcal{A}=C^\infty_b\otimes(\oplus\mathcal{M}_{n_d})$ is the smooth pre-$C^*$-algebra on which the $K$-homology (item 4) and regularity (item 6) statements are unconditional. This closes the smooth-subalgebra residual; T0 overall remains 🔶 (item 1 infinite $M_\infty$ and item 5 KO-obstruction stand). Proposed one-clause refinement of the Part 9 T0 items-4/6 note (name $\mathcal{A}=C^\infty_b\otimes\bigoplus\mathcal{M}_{n_d}$, spectrally invariant) — for Fedge to place, since T0 wording is flagged sensitive.

### §35. The d=6 mode dimension $S(13,6)=18564$ is a cumulative count, not a single $\mathbb{CP}^3$ harmonic eigenspace (2026-06-13)

A concrete step on the open STEP 66 problem (the $\ell$-multiplicities of the $d=6$ modes), via a Weyl-dimension sweep. Two findings. (1) The SU(4) irreps of dimension $S(13,6)=18564$ are exactly $(0,12,3)$ and its conjugate $(3,12,0)$ in Dynkin labels — a complex-conjugate (chiral) pair, not self-conjugate. (2) The $\mathbb{CP}^3$ scalar-harmonic eigenspaces are the $(m,0,m)$ class, with dimensions $15, 84, 300, 825, 1911, 3920, 7344, 12825, 21175, \ldots$ — and **18564 is not among them** (it falls in the gap between $m=8$: $12825$ and $m=9$: $21175$). So $S(13,6)$ is not a single $\mathbb{CP}^3$ Laplacian eigenspace.

This confirms concretely STEP 66's caveat that $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}$ is not a standard harmonic-space dimension, and aligns it with Theorem S1: $S(n,d)$ is the **cumulative** Dirac count to level $n-1$, a sum over harmonic levels $0,\ldots,n-1$, not a single irrep. Consequence for the electron $\ell$-content (this session's §6.4 correction): the correct object is the cumulative harmonic tower up to level $12$, which includes the level-$0$ ($\ell=0$) component — reinforcing $\ell=0$ **present** for the electron; the single-irrep $(0,12,3)$ dimension match is a coincidence, not the physical content. The STEP 66 framing "identify the SU(4) irrep of dimension 18564 and branch it" therefore targets the wrong object: the $\ell$-content should be assembled level-by-level from the harmonic tower, then branched under the physical SO(3).

**Embedding resolved (2026-06-13; `files/idwt.py` STEP 81).** The physical SO(3) is the **observable-coordinate rotation** SO(3)$\subset$SO(6)$\cong$SU(4)$\cong$Spin(6) — the rotation of the 3 observable spatial coordinates (the $d=3$ marginal, Part 11 §6.1), which is what defines angular momentum $\ell$ for a $d=3$ observer. Split $\mathbb{R}^6=\mathbb{R}^3_{\rm obs}\oplus\mathbb{R}^3_{\rm hid}$; the isotropic oscillator factorizes ($N=N_{\rm obs}+N_{\rm hid}$), the 3D oscillator at level $N_{\rm obs}$ carries each $\ell\in\{N_{\rm obs},N_{\rm obs}-2,\ldots\}$ once, and the hidden $\mathbb{R}^3$ at level $N_{\rm hid}$ contributes $\binom{N_{\rm hid}+2}{2}$ SO(3)$_{\rm obs}$-scalar states, giving
$$ m(\ell,N)=\sum_{N_{\rm obs}=\ell,\,\ell+2,\ldots\le N}\binom{N-N_{\rm obs}+2}{2}, \qquad M_n(\ell)=\sum_{N=\ell}^{n-1}m(\ell,N). $$
This is the embedding that works: per level $\sum_\ell(2\ell+1)m(\ell,N)=\binom{N+5}{5}$ exactly, and the cumulative mode reproduces $S(n,6)$ exactly — electron $n=13\to\sum_\ell(2\ell+1)M(\ell)=18564$, muon $n=35\to 3{,}838{,}380$ (verified). It is selected uniquely by reproducing $S(n,d)$, needs no SU(4) character formula (bypassing the $t(\theta)$ non-regular 0/0), and dissolves the "$\mathrm{Sym}^n\ne S(n,d)$" mismatch ($S$ is the cumulative count, not $\mathrm{Sym}^n$). The electron multiplicities: $M(0..12)=1036,784,581,420,295,200,130,80,46,24,11,4,1$; $M(0)=1036>0$, so $\ell=0$ is **present** (reconfirming the §6.4 contact correction). This $m(\ell,N)$ is the bound-problem SO(3)$_{\rm obs}$ branch (next paragraph).

**Correction — no intrinsic SO(3); the free-mode classifier is SO(6)$\cong$SU(4) (2026-06-13; `files/idwt.py` STEP 82).** Reading "physical SO(3) = observable rotation" as the free mode's intrinsic content imports a 3D frame the free mode does not have. The $d=6$ sector space is flat $\mathbb{R}^6$ (the $\mathbb{CP}^3$ label is the local symmetry of the potential minimum, not the global topology), so its geometric symmetry is the rotation group SO(6)$\cong$Spin(6)$\cong$SU(4) — the SU(4) already named as the $\mathbb{CP}^3$ isometry in Part 8 §14.2. A free electron marks out no three of its six dimensions (§14.2), so it carries SU(4) labels, not an $\ell$. The frame-free content is the SO(6) harmonic tower
$$ \mathrm{Sym}^N(\mathbb{R}^6)=\bigoplus_k H_{N-2k},\quad H_m=(0,m,0)_{SU(4)}=\text{degree-}m\ S^5\text{ harmonic},\quad \dim H_m=\binom{m+5}{5}-\binom{m+3}{5}, $$
with multiplicity in mode $n$ equal to $\#\{N\in[0,n-1]:N\ge m,\ N\equiv m\ (\mathrm{mod}\ 2)\}$ and $\sum_m \mathrm{mult}(m,n)\dim H_m=S(n,6)$ exactly for all $n$ (electron $n=13$: $m=0..12$ with multiplicities $7,6,6,5,5,4,4,3,3,2,2,1,1$, dims $1,6,20,50,105,196,336,540,825,1210,1716,2366,3185$, summing to $18564$). So $18564$ is the $(0,m,0)$ $S^5$-tower sum: the flat sector uses the $\mathbb{R}^6/S^5$ harmonics, not the compact $\mathbb{CP}^3$ Laplacian $(a,0,a)$ eigenspaces $15,84,300,825,1911,\ldots$.

An SO(3) $\ell$ exists only when an external $d=3$ object — the nucleus — breaks SO(6)$\to$SO(3)$_{\rm obs}\times$SO(3)$_{\rm hid}$ in the **bound** hydrogen problem (§14.2: "the split is anchored by the nucleus, not the electron"); STEP 81's $m(\ell,N)$ is that nucleus-anchored branch. The earlier follow-up flag resolves as a no: STEP 81's SO(3)$_{\rm obs}$ (real; mixed-parity $\ell$; $\ell=0$ for every $n$) and the Part 8 §14.3 holomorphic SU(4)$\supset$SU(3)$\supset$SO(3) (STEP 66; parity-$N$) are **different subgroups** giving different $\ell$-spectra — the vector $\mathbf{6}$ branches as $\ell{=}1\oplus\ell{=}1$ under the former and $\ell{=}1\oplus 3{\cdot}\ell{=}0$ under the latter (`explore_so3_embedding_check.py`). Their disagreement is the proof that no SO(3) is intrinsic. The load-bearing "$\ell=0$ contact present iff $n$ odd" (Part 7 §1.2; Part 11 §6.4) is frame-free as **the SO(6) singlet $H_0$, present iff $N=n-1$ is even iff $n$ is odd** — "$\ell=0$" there names the rotation-invariant contact harmonic, not an SO(3) label. ⭐ identity (pure representation theory / dimension counting).

### §36. Six-dimensional probe: $e$–$e$ scattering and the hidden-coordinate momentum channel (2026-06-14, Fedge directive; `files/idwt.py` STEP 83)

A falsifiable consequence of taking the electron seriously as a $d=6$ object — six equal macroscopic spatial dimensions, none privileged (Part 1 ontology). The pieces are all established; this assembles them.

**Setup.** Two electrons scatter as $6$-dimensional objects, conserving the full $6$-momentum; a detector built from $d=3$ matter resolves only $3$ of the $6$ spatial momentum components. A beam prepared by a $d=3$ source carries momentum in the observable coordinates alone ($P_4=P_5=P_6=0$ incoming), with the centroid propagating freely, $E^2=|\mathbf P|^2+m^2$, $\mathbf P$ a $6$-vector (Part 1 §3h–§3i, "bound within / free without"; STEP 58 centroid covariance).

**Why ordinary Møller shows nothing — and why this is different (the scope point).** Long-range $e$–$e$ electromagnetism is the $d=2$ zero mode, supported on the shared *observable* coordinates $1,2$. It is uniform in the hidden coordinates, so the projection theorem (Part 3 §0.8a; Marginal Exactness, Part 11 §6.1) collapses it to the ordinary $3$D Møller amplitude with no deviation — the theorem's scope condition is precisely "potential from a $3$D source, uniform in the hidden coordinates." A second electron violates that condition: it is a *localized* $6$D probe, not a uniform $3$D source, so the theorem does not apply to it. The short-range kernel contact $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$, of $6$D range $L_6=1.414$ fm (STEP 59–60, gate $\Omega=e^{-R^2/4}$), acts on all six shared coordinates and can deflect the relative momentum into the hidden directions $4,5,6$.

**Kinematic factor (⭐, exact).** In the $6$D centre-of-mass frame the incoming relative momentum $\mathbf k$ lies along an observable direction $\hat{\mathbf k}$; elastic scattering gives $\mathbf k'=k\cos\theta\,\hat{\mathbf k}+k\sin\theta\,\hat{\mathbf n}$ with $\hat{\mathbf n}$ uniform on the $4$-sphere of directions perpendicular to $\hat{\mathbf k}$ — the perpendicular space is $5$-dimensional ($2$ observable $+\,3$ hidden) and the kernel is SO(6)-invariant. Hence $\langle|\hat{\mathbf n}_{\rm hidden}|^2\rangle=3/5$: three-fifths of the transverse momentum transfer goes into invisible coordinates. The two outgoing electrons carry equal and opposite hidden momenta, so the *total observable* momentum is still conserved, but each separately reconstructs an inflated invariant mass $m_{\rm app}^2=m^2+|\mathbf p_{\rm hidden}|^2$ — missing momentum/energy per particle.

**Threshold (✅).** Bringing two electrons within $R=L_6$ against their Coulomb repulsion requires centre-of-mass relative kinetic energy $E\ge\alpha\hbar c/L_6\approx1.06$ MeV (IDWT $\alpha$). Below this the contact channel is Coulomb-blocked; above it, it opens.

**Rate and the open factor (🔶 channel; ❓ rate).** The contact is a point coupling, so its cross-section is flat in energy, $\sigma_{\rm contact}\lesssim\pi L_6^2\approx63$ mb, while the Møller cross-section falls as $1/E^2$ (the two cross near the $\sim1$ MeV threshold). The actual rate carries a hidden-coordinate overlap factor $f_{\rm hid}=\exp(-\Delta X_{456}^2/4L_6^2)\in[0,1]$ — set by where ordinary $3$D matter sits in coordinates $4,5,6$, the open structural piece. $f_{\rm hid}\sim1$ is excluded (it would dominate all high-energy $e$–$e$ scattering); pinning $f_{\rm hid}$ is what would convert the bound into a sharp number.

**The observable, and why existing limits miss it.** The signature is *missing* momentum, not *excess* observable wide-angle scattering. $e$–$e$ compositeness limits ($\Lambda\gtrsim10$ TeV) bound an additional observable hard-scattering amplitude; they do not bound momentum quietly leaving into invisible coordinates. That instead registers as anomalous beam diffusion — transverse emittance growth beyond standard intra-beam (Coulomb) scattering — switching on above $\sim1$ MeV relative CM energy and carrying the $3/5$ kinematic fingerprint, and as missing-momentum events in precision fixed-target Møller. Because IDWT fixes the kinematics in advance, an excess of the predicted form (or its absence, once $f_{\rm hid}$ is derived) is falsifiable. Written into Part 6 (Falsifiability) and Part 5 §9.

**Addendum — $f_{\rm hid}$ resolved structurally: a hidden-volume overlap that vanishes at rest; the open piece reduces to one cosmological number (2026-06-14, opus, Fedge "get the math completely done").** Three results.



*1. The overlap form is exact (⭐).* The electron's $d=6$ profile has Gaussian width $L_6=\lambda_6^{-1/4}=4^{1/4}=\sqrt2$ in sector units ($\lambda_6=(g_{66}/2)^{2/3}=1/4$; $=1.414$ fm via STEP 59/60). Two electrons whose hidden centroids are separated by $\Delta X$ in coordinates $4,5,6$ have amplitude overlap $\langle\psi_1|\psi_2\rangle=\exp(-\Delta X^2/4L_6^2)$ — verified to machine precision against the direct Gaussian integral. (The density–density contact, the actual two-body kernel form, gives $\exp(-\Delta X^2/2L_6^2)$; the factor-of-2 in the exponent is the one O(1) ambiguity and does not affect the structural result below.)

*2. The hidden centroid is a free translational zero mode; at rest it is uniform (✅).* The question "where does $3$D matter sit in coordinates $4,5,6$" has a structural answer. Nothing in ordinary laboratory physics localizes an electron's centroid in $4,5,6$: electron–nucleus and electron–electron electromagnetism is the $d=2$ zero mode, supported on the shared observable coordinates $1,2$ and uniform in $4,5,6$ (Part 1 §3i), so it exerts no force there; by Marginal Exactness (Part 11 §6.1) every $3$D-source field is uniform in the hidden coordinates and contributes zero to motion along them. The only operator that acts in $4,5,6$ is the short-range kernel contact itself — the rare channel under discussion. So the hidden centroid is a free translational coordinate under all non-contact interactions, and by "bound within, free without" (STEP 33, ✅) a free direction's rest state is the uniform (constant) state. A $3$D-prepared beam, which cannot localize $4,5,6$ (Marginal Exactness forbids it), therefore sits at the uniform/rest limit in the hidden coordinates.

*3. $f_{\rm hid}$ is a hidden-volume overlap $\sim(L_6/L_{\rm hid})^3$, $\to 0$ at rest.* With both centroids uniform over the hidden extent $L_{\rm hid}$ that bulk matter occupies in $4,5,6$, the effective factor is the average of $\exp(-\Delta X^2/4L_6^2)$ over the uniform separation distribution: $\langle f_{\rm hid}\rangle=(4\pi L_6^2)^{3/2}/L_{\rm hid}^3$ for $L_{\rm hid}\gg L_6$ (confirmed analytically and by Monte Carlo). So $f_{\rm hid}$ is not an $O(1)$ Gaussian at a fixed $\Delta X$ but a **volume-ratio suppression**, and it $\to 0$ as $L_{\rm hid}\to\infty$ (genuinely delocalized rest centroids). This is why ordinary high-energy $e$–$e$ scattering shows nothing — not a tuned cancellation but a structural consequence of the hidden centroid being an unlocalizable free coordinate: $f_{\rm hid}\sim 1$ is impossible for $3$D-prepared matter. **Net:** the open structural piece is reduced from a function to a single number, $L_{\rm hid}$ = the hidden-coordinate clustering extent of bulk matter, with a clean dichotomy — if the hidden centroids are truly delocalized ($L_{\rm hid}\to\infty$) the channel is *exactly closed* and IDWT predicts **no** anomalous beam diffusion from it (a sharp falsifiable null); if some interaction clusters matter in $4,5,6$ over a finite $L_{\rm hid}$, the rate carries the computable $(L_6/L_{\rm hid})^3$ factor. The only force that acts in all coordinates and could set a finite $L_{\rm hid}$ is gravity (M$_\infty$ curvature); whether it clusters matter in the hidden coordinates is the remaining open question, now a single well-posed one. Status: overlap form ⭐; zero-mode/uniform-rest reduction ✅; $L_{\rm hid}$ (hence the absolute rate) ❓, but the channel is structurally suppressed and plausibly null. The verified pieces ($L_6$, the overlap coefficient, the volume law) are recorded in `files/idwt.py` STEP 84; the resolution is written into Part 6 (Falsifiability, "A six-dimensional probe") and Part 5 §9 C9, replacing the "open factor $f_{\rm hid}$" wording with the hidden-volume suppression and the single open number $L_{\rm hid}$ (notebook index regenerated).

### §38. Meta's minuscule representation claims — verification (2026-06-14)

Meta proposed three mathematical routes connecting the IDWT tower to minuscule representation theory. All three were verified and found incorrect in their specific claims; the broad direction (minuscule posets may be relevant) is plausible but unestablished.

**(A) Coxeter number claim.** Meta: "$d$-values $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ = Coxeter numbers of $A_1,A_2,A_3,D_4,D_5,E_6$ minus 1." Checked: the Coxeter numbers are $A_1=2, A_2=3, A_3=4, D_4=6, D_5=8, E_6=12$; subtracting 1 gives $\{1,2,3,5,7,11\}$, not $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$. **WRONG.** No variant of this mapping (ranks, half-Coxeter, dual Coxeter) produces $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ from these six algebras.

**(B) Hockey-stick sum.** Meta: "$2926 = 1+3+6+\cdots+76$" (triangular numbers). Checked: $\sum_{k=1}^{76} T_k = \binom{78}{3} = 76{,}076$, not 2926. What 2926 actually is: $S(76,2) = \binom{77}{2} = 2926$, a single evaluation of the mass formula, not a cumulative sum. **WRONG.**

**(C) 15 irreducible $d$-complete poset shapes.** Meta: "15 irreducible $d$-complete poset shapes correspond exactly to the 15 IDWT modes." First reading checked minuscule poset *shapes*: the $A_n$ series alone gives infinitely many (one $k \times m$ rectangle per pair $k \le m$), so a literal shape count is infinite, and the only finite exceptional shape count is 3 ($E_6\,\omega_1$, $E_6\,\omega_6$, $E_7\,\omega_7$). That reading checked the wrong object — the "15" refers to *classes*, not shapes, and the count is genuine. The proper probe is part (G) below.

**(D) Exceptional minuscule dimensions.** Checked whether any IDWT $S(n,d)$ value equals an exceptional (non-$A_n$) minuscule representation dimension ($E_6$: 27; $E_7$: 56; $D_n$ vector: $2n$; $D_n$ spinor: $2^{n-1}$). Only one match found: $S(4,3)=20 = 2\cdot10$ (the $D_{10}$ vector representation). This is a small-number coincidence; 20 is not structurally motivated for $D_{10}$ from IDWT. Every other IDWT $S(n,d)$ misses all exceptional minuscule dimensions.

**(E) Tautological $A_n$ connection.** Every $S(n,d) = \binom{n+d-1}{d}$ equals the dimension of $\omega_d$ of $A_{n+d-2}$, which is a minuscule representation. This is true for ALL $(n,d)$ pairs, not just the tower — a tautology, not a selection.

**(F) APS $\eta$-invariant $n$-parity claim (Meta's route #1, 2026-06-14).** Meta: the Atiyah–Patodi–Singer $\eta$-invariant on $S^{2d-1}$ selects "the odd-$n$ series for $d$ odd and the even-$n$ series for $d$ even, which is why you see $(1,3)$ and $(4,3)$ but not $(2,3)$ or $(3,3)$." Checked against the tower $n$-values within each sector: $d=2$ carries $n\in\{0,76,81,95\}$ (parities even, even, odd, odd); $d=3$ carries $n\in\{1,4\}$ (odd, even); $d=4$ carries $\{3,20,72\}$ (odd, even, even); $d=5$ carries $\{10,15,22\}$ (even, odd, even). Every sector holds mixed $n$-parity, and Meta's own cited example $(4,3)$ has even $n$ in an odd sector. **WRONG**, and self-contradictory. The genuine IDWT parity result is on the harmonic level $N=n-1$, not $n$, and is per-sector: $\ell=0$ present iff $n$ odd (l-parity, the established $\bigstar$ result for odd levels, §15/STEP 64–66). Meta conflated $n$ with the level and asserted a uniform odd/even-$d$ split that the tower does not have.

**(G) $d$-complete poset classification — proper probe (2026-06-14).** Proctor's Dynkin-diagram classification (R. A. Proctor, *Dynkin diagram classification of $\lambda$-minuscule Bruhat lattices and of $d$-complete posets*, J. Algebraic Combin. 9 (1999) 61–94) sorts every irreducible $d$-complete poset into exactly 15 classes: (1) Shapes, (2) Shifted shapes, (3) Birds, (4) Insets, (5) Tailed insets, (6) Banners, (7) Nooks, (8) Swivels, (9) Tailed swivels, (10) Tagged swivels, (11) Swivel shifteds, (12) Pumps, (13) Tailed pumps, (14) Near bats, (15) Bat. So Meta's *count* is real; the cardinality coincidence $15 = 15$ is the only substance to the claim, and it does not survive contact with the structure.

Each class is an infinite family (Class 1 alone is every Young-diagram shape). The decisive test is which class each IDWT mode occupies. The mass $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}$ is the number of order ideals of the $d \times (n-1)$ rectangle poset (equivalently, the weights of $\omega_d$ of $A_{n+d-2}$ realized on the Grassmannian $\mathrm{Gr}(d,n+d-1)$). A rectangle is a **Class 1 "Shape"**. Verified for all 15 modes: each is the $d\times(n-1)$ rectangle and $\#\text{ideals} = \binom{(n-1)+d}{d} = S(n,d)$ exactly (e.g. $e$: $6\times12$, 18564; $\tau$: $10\times22$, 64512240; $\mathrm{up}$: $4\times2$, 15). All 15 modes collapse into the single class Shapes — they do not spread across the 15 classes, so there is no bijection and no structural content behind $15 = 15$. The classification describes the hook-length / $P$-partition generating function of *any* shape and selects no subset, so like (E) it is universal and non-selective. The route is now probed and closed.

**Genuine (previously known) connection.** $n_{\rm top} = \chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)\cdot\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)\cdot\chi(\mathbb{CP}^5) = 3\cdot4\cdot6 = 72$ (already STEP 1). The Kähler sector Euler characteristics $\{2,3,4,6\}$ equal Coxeter numbers of $\{A_1,A_2,A_3,A_5\}$, which is just $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^k)=k+1 = h(A_k)$ — not new. The Kähler half-dimensions $d/2=\{1,2,3,5\}$ for the active even sectors $d\in\{2,4,6,10\}$ are consecutive Fibonacci numbers with a gap at $4$; that gap is $d=8$, the excluded even sector ($\chi$-gap, T15b), so the observation restates the known $d=8$ exclusion rather than adding to it.

**Verdict.** Meta's specific mathematical claims (Coxeter, hockey-stick, APS $n$-parity) are false. No new selective connection to exceptional Lie algebras was found. The $d$-complete poset / minuscule route is now probed and closed (G): the IDWT mass is the order-ideal count of a rectangular Class-1 Shape, every mode sits in the same one of Proctor's 15 classes, and the formula is universal over all $(n,d)$, so the framework carries zero selective power for the tower. The $15 = 15$ cardinality match is coincidence. Recorded to prevent re-running these checks.

---

### §39. Cross-concept literature scan (2026-06-14; web sources, no IDWT computation)

Method: looked up the genuine mathematical structures that have surfaced in IDWT — minuscule representations / fundamental weights, $d$-complete posets (Proctor), the Hopf-fibration chain, Clifford algebras / Bott periodicity, and the dimension set $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ — across several independent sources, recording which adjacent concepts recur. One concept recurs strongly and lands directly on IDWT structure; two others recur but attach only weakly.

**Strong recurrence — compact Hermitian symmetric spaces (CHSS) / cominuscule varieties.** Independent literatures converge here: minuscule and cominuscule flag manifolds *are* the compact Hermitian symmetric spaces; their Schubert calculus is governed by exactly the Proctor $d$-complete posets and Schützenberger jeu de taquin that §38 examined; for simply-laced $G$ a minuscule node is cominuscule, so $G/P$ is a CHSS (Borel–de Siebenthal). The classification (Cartan): four classical families — Grassmannians $\mathrm{Gr}(k,n)$ (type A III, including $\mathbb{CP}^{n}=\mathrm{Gr}(1,n+1)$), quadrics, $SO(2n)/U(n)$, $Sp(n)/U(n)$ — plus two exceptional, $E\,\mathrm{III}$ ($E_6$, complex dim 16) and $E\,\mathrm{VII}$ ($E_7$, complex dim 27). Relevance to IDWT: the Kähler sectors $\mathbb{CP}^{d/2}$ for $d\in\{2,4,6,10\}$ are exactly the rank-one CHSS (type A III), while the real sectors $S^3,S^5$ ($d=3,5$) are odd-dimensional spheres and are *not* Hermitian symmetric. So the standard CHSS framework reproduces the IDWT Kähler-vs-real sector split for free, and it is the established home for everything the framework has been recovering combinatorially (minuscule dimensions §38E, rectangular order-ideal posets §38G). Caveat consistent with §38: the apparatus applies to every $\mathbb{CP}^{k}$ uniformly, so it organizes the sector geometry without by itself selecting which modes are physical. The untested, genuinely new handle is the *product* structure — cominuscule Littlewood–Richardson / jeu-de-taquin Schubert calculus on $\mathbb{CP}^{d/2}$ — as a candidate model for the kernel's mode-combination (four-wave / additive-index) rule. Logged to todo as a lead.

**Weak recurrence — Bott periodicity / Clifford period 8.** This is the literature home of the IDWT $d \bmod 8$ neutrino result (Part 5: $d=5$ gives a Dirac-type spinor, no $C$ on $S^5$). Real spinor representations repeat with period 8, complex with period 2. The recurring "10" attached to this — the tenfold way / Altland–Zirnbauer classes ($2$ complex $+\,8$ real Morita classes $=10$) — is a Bott-derived 10 that coincides with the IDWT terminal sector $d=10$. IDWT's $d=10$ has an independent derivation (Rule B Gegenbauer criticality, $b=\tfrac12$ at $d=10$; T15b $\chi$-gap), so the match is numerological unless a $2+8$ decomposition of the terminal sector actually appears. Flagged $\textbf{❓}$, not pursued.

**Weak recurrence — Freudenthal–Tits magic square / division algebras.** The exceptional CHSS dimensions (16, 27) and the exceptional minuscule dimensions (27 for $E_6$, 56 for $E_7$) are the octonionic / exceptional-Jordan-algebra numbers tied to $E_6,E_7$ via the magic square and the four Hopf-invariant-one division algebras ($\dim 1,2,4,8$). §38D already found no tower $S(n,d)$ hits 27 or 56, and the IDWT sector dimensions $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ are not the division-algebra dimensions $\{1,2,4,8\}$, so the connection is weak. Recorded to prevent re-chasing.

**Verdict.** The one concept that recurs across multiple independent literatures *and* lands on IDWT structure is the compact Hermitian symmetric space (cominuscule) framework: the even/Kähler sectors are precisely the rank-one CHSS, and minuscule-dimension and $d$-complete-poset facts are its standard combinatorics. It is a reframing, not (yet) a selector. The concrete lead worth testing is cominuscule Schubert calculus as a model for kernel mode-combination.

**Test of the lead — the cominuscule product does not model the four-wave rule (2026-06-14, opus). NULL.** The untested handle was whether the cominuscule LR / jeu-de-taquin product reproduces the kernel's additive-index (four-wave) rule. It does not, for a scale reason and a structural reason. (i) *Scale.* The rank-one CHSS are $\mathbb{CP}^k$ with $k=d/2\in\{1,2,3,5\}$; their Schubert degrees run $0..k$ (the product $h^a h^b=h^{a+b}$, truncated at $k$), so a single sector caps at degree $5$ and the product variety $\mathbb{CP}^1\times\mathbb{CP}^2\times\mathbb{CP}^3\times\mathbb{CP}^5$ at total degree $11$. The tower's additive relations run over indices up to $95$ ($e=\nu_1+\mathrm{up}$, $\nu_3=\nu_1+\nu_2-\mathrm{up}$, $\tau=\nu_3+\mathrm{down}$, the boson cascade), orders of magnitude above any available Schubert degree. (ii) *Structure.* Each mode is its own Grassmannian $\mathrm{Gr}(d,n{+}d{-}1)$ (§38); LR multiplies Schubert classes *within one* variety, whereas the four-wave rule relates indices *across* different modes and sectors — there is no single cominuscule variety whose product is the cross-mode rule. So the cominuscule product is non-selective for the same reasons §38's poset apparatus was: degree-bounded and within-variety, while the tower combination is large-index and cross-variety. The §39 product handle is closed.

---

### §40. Cross-concept literature scan, round 2 (2026-06-14; web sources, no IDWT computation)

Method as in §39, on structures not yet scanned: the sector dimension set, the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel, and Gegenbauer criticality. Two concepts recur strongly and land on IDWT.

**Strong recurrence — normed division algebras and the dimension set $\{3,4,6,10\}$.** An independent literature (Baez–Huerta, *Division Algebras and Supersymmetry* I–III; Anastasiou–Borsten–Duff et al., *Super Yang–Mills, division algebras and triality*) establishes that classical super-Yang–Mills — and the Green–Schwarz superstring — exist precisely in dimensions $D\in\{3,4,6,10\}$, because a normed division algebra exists in dimension $D-2\in\{1,2,4,8\}$ ($\mathbb{R},\mathbb{C},\mathbb{H},\mathbb{O}$). The enabling object is a $\Gamma$-matrix/Fierz identity (the "$3$-$\psi$ rule") equivalent to the existence of the division algebra and to triality. IDWT independently reaches the active set $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ (Part 1 §3a: Hopf-chain / Kähler closure $+$ Gegenbauer threshold $+\ \chi$; Rule A/B), which contains $\{3,4,6,10\}$ exactly and shares the distinctive jump $6\to10$ skipping $d=7,8,9$ — the same gap the division-algebra ladder leaves. The shared origin is spinor representation theory, the machinery IDWT already uses for the neutrino (Clifford $d\bmod 8$, no $C$ on $S^5$, Part 5). **Caveat (load-bearing):** IDWT is a classical field theory with no supersymmetry; this is a coincidence of the dimension set plus a shared spinor-identity origin, not a claim that IDWT is super-Yang–Mills, and SUSY structure must not be imported (CLAUDE.md framework-import rule). Recorded as a candidate bearing on sector selection: the open question is whether the division-algebra/triality Fierz condition is the *same* condition as Rule A/Rule B — if so, the sector-set derivation upgrades. Logged to todo.

Sub-observation ($\textbf{❓}$): triality is sharpest at $\mathrm{Spin}(8)/D_4$ (the three $8$-dimensional irreps $8_v,8_s,8_c$ permuted by the $S_3$ outer automorphism of the most symmetric Dynkin diagram), i.e. $d=8$ — the sector IDWT excludes ($\chi$-gap, T15b). Both IDWT and the super-Yang–Mills ladder skip $d=8$. Whether the two exclusion mechanisms coincide is unprobed.

**Strong recurrence — Gegenbauer / zonal positive-definite kernels (Schoenberg, Funk–Hecke).** Schoenberg's theorem: an $O(d)$-invariant positive-definite kernel on $S^{d-1}$ is exactly a non-negative combination of Gegenbauer (ultraspherical) polynomials; the Funk–Hecke theorem gives the eigenvalue of a dot-product kernel on each spherical-harmonic level. The IDWT kernel $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ is a degree-2 zonal dot-product kernel, so it decomposes into exactly the $\ell=0$ and $\ell=2$ harmonic components already used in the kernel angular-support analysis (§22), with Funk–Hecke fixing the per-level eigenvalues; Rule B (Gegenbauer criticality, $b=\tfrac12$ at $d=10$) sits natively in this ultraspherical framework. This is the rigorous home of the kernel's angular structure and a computational tool — kernel matrix elements via Funk–Hecke rather than ad hoc. Already partly used; recorded as the formal framework, not a new selector.

**Verdict.** Round 2's strongest finding is the division-algebra dimension match $\{3,4,6,10\}\subset$ active sectors, sharing the $6\to10$ gap, with a shared spinor-identity (triality/Fierz) origin — a candidate that Rule A/B sector selection might coincide with the $D-2$ division-algebra condition (to be tested, not imported). The Gegenbauer/Schoenberg framework is the rigorous home and computational tool for the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel. Both verified against primary literature; neither imports SUSY nor runs IDWT computation.

**Test of the lead — does the division-algebra condition coincide with Rule A/B? (2026-06-14).** Result: the two are **different conditions that agree on a meaningful subset**, not the same rule. Details:

*Not Rule A or Rule B.* IDWT selects $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$, with $(d-2)\in\{0,1,2,3,4,8\}$; the division-algebra condition is $(d-2)\in\{1,2,4,8\}$, i.e. $\{3,4,6,10\}$. IDWT includes $d=2$ ($d-2=0$) and $d=5$ ($d-2=3$), which the division-algebra condition excludes, so IDWT's selection is strictly broader. Rule B alone selects only the terminal $d=10$; Rule A selects $d=6$ and excludes $7,8,9$. Neither rule, nor their union, is the four-element set $\{3,4,6,10\}$. And the relation $4k_0=(d-2)^2$ that Rule B does use gives $(d_{\rm terminal}-2)=2n_s=8$ as a downstream consequence of the seed $n_s=4$ (equivalently $N_c=3$ via $d_{\rm terminal}=2(N_c+2)$), not from a division-algebra input — the octonion dimension at $d=10$ is equivalent to "three colours," reached independently.

*Not the IDWT charge mechanism.* IDWT derives electric charge from the $\mathbb{CP}^2$ spin$^c$ / $SU(3)=\mathrm{Isom}(\mathbb{CP}^2)$ structure and anomaly cancellation ($Q=T_3+Y$, $N_c=3$; Part 3 §8, §13) — unrelated to a division-algebra count.

*What does hold, exactly.* The set $\{d : d-2\in\{1,2,4,8\}\}=\{3,4,6,10\}$ equals the IDWT **charged-fermion sectors** exactly (down $d{=}3$, up $d{=}4$, $e/\mu$ $d{=}6$, $\tau$ $d{=}10$), with the two exceptions being the neutral-fermion sector ($\nu$, $d{=}5$, $d-2=3$) and the boson sector ($d{=}2$, $d-2=0$). Here $d-2$ is IDWT-meaningful in two independent ways: the number of sector coordinates beyond the universal $d=2$ electromagnetic plane (nesting $\Xi_2\subset\Xi_d$), and the transverse quantity in Rule B's $4k_0=(d-2)^2$. The same set is what the SUSY-*independent* $3$-$\psi$/triality $\Gamma$-matrix Fierz identity selects (it holds at $D\in\{3,4,6,10\}$ by Hurwitz on the $D-2$ transverse dimensions — a pure Clifford-algebra fact, not a supersymmetry assumption). So a normed division algebra lives in the beyond-EM transverse dimensions of precisely the charged-fermion sectors.

*Strongest point and honest status.* $d=5$ is the odd one out in **both** frameworks independently: IDWT flags it as the unique sector with $\chi(S^5)=0$, no Kähler form, and no self-coupling fixed point (Part 1 §3a), while the division-algebra side has $d-2=3\notin\{1,2,4,8\}$. Two unrelated criteria agree on which sector is exceptional. But this is a coincidence of the selected *set* plus a shared spinor-algebra fact, not a shared *mechanism*: IDWT's sector selection is geometric (couplings, $\chi$, Gegenbauer criticality, $N_c=3$) and its charges come from $\mathbb{CP}^2$ anomaly cancellation. The open conjecture (status $\textbf{❓}$, not for any Part) is whether the transverse division-algebra / triality structure is what *makes* those sectors host charged fermions — which IDWT does not currently derive. The $d=8$ (Spin(8) triality) exclusion coincides in both ($d-2=6\notin\{1,2,4,8\}$; IDWT $\chi$-gap T15b) but again by different mechanisms. No SUSY is imported; no Part edit follows from this.

---

### §41. The convergent exceptionality of the $d=5$ sector (consolidating cross-reference, 2026-06-14)

The $d=5$ sector — the neutrinos — is singled out as the exceptional sector along several axes that were established independently and live in different Parts. Collected here so the convergence is recorded in one place rather than scattered. Each axis is an established IDWT result; the proposed single root is the only $\textbf{❓}$.

1. **Geometry — no self-coupling fixed point.** $d=5$ is a real (non-Kähler) active sector with no self-coupling fixed point of its own (Part 1 §3a). It shares $\chi(S^5)=0$ with $d=3$ ($\chi(S^3)=0$ — every odd sphere has $\chi=0$), so vanishing Euler characteristic is not the discriminator. What separates them is parallelizability: $S^3=SU(2)$ is a parallelizable division-algebra sphere ($\mathbb{H}$ on $\mathbb{R}^4$) and closes on its own group structure, while $S^5$ is non-parallelizable ($S^n$ is parallelizable only for $n=1,3,7$) and has no fixed point of its own. Every other active sector closes on itself; $d=5$ does not.
2. **Mass — not self-generated.** Because there is no own fixed point, $m_{{\rm scale},5}$ is fixed parasitically by a cross-sector relation $m_{{\rm scale},5}\,m_{{\rm scale},4}^2=(n_u/n_s)\,m_{{\rm scale},6}^3$ (Part 1 §3a; Part 2 §9c), and the resulting masses are tiny ($\sum m_\nu\approx 60$ meV; idwt.py STEP 12) — the lightest matter sector by orders of magnitude.
3. **Charge — the one gap in $\{1,2,4,8\}$.** $d-2=3$ is the unique non-division-algebra value among the active sectors' $(d-2)\in\{0,1,2,3,4,8\}$; $d=5$ is the lone *neutral*-fermion sector while $\{3,4,6,10\}$ host the charged fermions (§40 test of the lead; charge mechanism Part 3 §8/§13).
4. **Spinor type — no Majorana.** $d\bmod 8=5$ gives a Dirac-type spinor and admits no charge-conjugation matrix $C$ on the $S^5$ bundle, so no Majorana operator exists at any order ($0\nu\beta\beta=0$ at all orders; Part 5).
5. **Mixing — largest angles.** $d=5$ sits adjacent to the Gegenbauer-critical $d=10$; the near-degeneracy $|n_\tau-n_{\nu_3}|=1$ at the critical endpoint maximizes the Gegenbauer propagator and makes $\theta_{23}$ the largest mixing angle (Part 9 T6).

**Observation ($\textbf{❓}$, not for any Part).** These are not obviously five separate facts. A candidate single root is axis 1 — the absence of a self-coupling fixed point — but the root of that absence is not $\chi(S^5)=0$ (which $d=3$ shares); it is the non-parallelizability of $S^5$, the failure of a division-algebra structure at $d=5$. A sector with no division-algebra grip of its own would host a particle that barely couples (neutrality), has no mass of its own (tiny, cross-sector-fixed scale), and exists only relative to its neighbours (mixing dominated by the adjacent critical sector). The testable form of the conjecture: the full neutrino phenomenology should be derivable from the parallelizability/division-algebra failure at $d=5$ alone. This is an interpretation, not a theorem — axes 1–5 are each established, but the claim that they share one root is unproved. Convergence with §40: the division-algebra criterion flags the same sector by $d-2=3\notin\{1,2,4,8\}$. These are two distinct division-algebra facts — non-parallelizability of the sector sphere $S^5$, and the absence of a normed algebra in the transverse dimension $d-2=3$ — but both fail at $d=5$, so axis 1 and §40 plausibly share one obstruction rather than agreeing by coincidence.

---

### §42. Do the 15 mode indices equal representation dimensions of their sector's isometry group? (2026-06-15)

**Conjecture tested.** GPT's "highest-weight framing" of the n-selection (raised after analysing the 15 n-values): S(n,d) = dim(Sym^d(ℂ^n)), so n is the dimension of the base space for a symmetric-power representation. Does n itself equal the dimension of an irreducible representation of the sector's isometry group G_d?

**Setup.** The isometry groups by sector are: d=2 → SU(2); d=3 → SO(4) = SU(2)×SU(2); d=4 → SU(3); d=5 → SO(6) ≅ SU(4); d=6 → SU(4) (same, since both S⁵ and CP³ carry SU(4) isometry); d=10 → SU(6). SU(2) and SO(4) achieve all positive integers as representation dimensions (SU(2) via spin-j and SO(4) via (a+1)(b+1)), so the test is trivially passed for d=2,3. The non-trivial sectors are d=4 (SU(3)), d=5 (SU(4)), d=6 (SU(4)), d=10 (SU(6)).

Irrep dimensions were enumerated up to 200 using the Weyl dimension formula
(l-vector method: l_i = λ_i + N - i for SU(N), dim = ∏_{i<j}(l_i-l_j)/(j-i)).
Enumeration verified: [1,0,0]→4, [0,1,0]→6, [1,0,1]→15, [2,0,0]→10, [4,0,0]→35 for SU(4);
[1,0]→3, [1,1]→8 for SU(3).

SU(3) dims ≤ 200: {1,3,6,8,10,15,21,24,27,28,35,36,42,45,...}.
SU(4) dims ≤ 200: {1,4,6,10,15,20,35,36,45,50,56,60,64,70,84,...}.
SU(6) dims ≤ 200: {1,6,15,20,21,35,56,70,84,105,120,126,175,189}.

**Results.**

| Particle | n  | d  | G_d  | n ∈ dims(G_d)? | G_d labels (if yes) |
|----------|----|----|------|----------------|---------------------|
| photon   | 0  | 2  | SU(2)| n/a (massless) | —                   |
| W,Z,H   | 76,81,95 | 2 | SU(2) | trivially YES | (all pos ints) |
| down     | 1  | 3  | SO(4)| trivially YES  | (all pos ints)       |
| strange  | 4  | 3  | SO(4)| trivially YES  | (all pos ints)       |
| up       | 3  | 4  | SU(3)| **YES**        | [0,1] and [1,0] (fundamental 3) |
| charm    | 20 | 4  | SU(3)| **NO**         | 20 ∉ SU(3) dims     |
| top      | 72 | 4  | SU(3)| **NO**         | 72 ∉ SU(3) dims     |
| ν₁       | 10 | 5  | SU(4)| **YES**        | [2,0,0] and [0,0,2] (Sym²(4)) |
| ν₂       | 15 | 5  | SU(4)| **YES**        | [1,0,1] (adjoint)   |
| ν₃       | 22 | 5  | SU(4)| **NO**         | 22 ∉ SU(4) dims     |
| e        | 13 | 6  | SU(4)| **NO**         | 13 ∉ SU(4) dims     |
| μ        | 35 | 6  | SU(4)| **YES**        | [4,0,0] and [0,0,4] (Sym⁴(4)) |
| τ        | 23 | 10 | SU(6)| **NO**         | 23 ∉ SU(6) dims     |

**Misses (non-trivial sectors): charm(20), top(72), ν₃(22), e(13), τ(23).**
Note: n_e=13 and n_τ=23 are primes not achievable as SU(4)/SU(6) rep dims at low rank; no classical group of rank ≤ 5 has a representation of dimension 13 or 22 or 23 (checked).

Cross-sector check: n_charm=20 IS an SU(4) dim ([0,2,0],[1,1,0],[0,0,3]) and an SU(6) dim ([0,0,1,0,0]), i.e. it passes the PARENT sector (d=5, G=SU(4)) and grandparent sector (d=10, G=SU(6)) groups — but not its own d=4 sector's SU(3). n_top=72 fails SU(3) and SU(4). The remaining misses fail all groups checked.

**Pattern in the SU(4) hits.** The three SU(4) hits are:
- n_ν₁ = 10 = S(n_up, n_up) = C(5,3): equals dim([2,0,0]) = C(n_up+N-1, N-1) for N=4, n=2.
- n_ν₂ = 15 = S(n_up, n_up+1) = C(6,4): equals dim([1,0,1]) = (N)²-1 = 15 for N=4.
- n_μ  = 35 = S(n_s, n_s) = C(7,4): equals dim([4,0,0]) = C(n_s+N-1,N-1) for N=4, n=n_s.

All three are "diagonal" evaluations of the S-table (n=d or n=d+1 with the two seeds n_up, n_s). The misses — n_ν₃=22, n_e=13 — are additive combinations (22 = n_ν₁+n_ν₂−n_up; 13 = n_ν₁+n_up), not diagonal evaluations. So the hit/miss split within SU(4) modes tracks the diagonal-vs-off-diagonal structure of the IDWT construction, not an independent representation-theoretic selection.

**Verdict.** The "n = dim(G_d irrep)" criterion is **NULL** as a universal selection rule: 5 of 15 modes fail (charm, top, ν₃, e, τ). The partial hits (up quark, ν₁, ν₂, μ) reflect the fact that S(k,k) and S(k,k±1) for k ∈ {n_up, n_s} happen to equal SU(4) rep dims — a consequence of the IDWT combinatorial structure (seeds propagating through symmetric-power evaluations), not an independent representation-theory gate. The strongest form of the §42 conjecture is refuted. No new search warranted.

**Status:** ❓ → NULL (2026-06-15). Recorded in §15 dead-ends below with a pointer here.

---

### §37. d=6 charged leptons share a common residue mod 11 (numerical observation only, 2026-06-14)

From the full-15 battery (see §15 null entry). Both charged lepton modes satisfy $n\equiv 2\pmod{11}$: $n_e=13=1\cdot11+2$ and $n_\mu=35=3\cdot11+2$. No other sector shows a shared residue under the same test mod $(2d-1)$: $d=3$ mod 5 gives $\{1,4\}$; $d=4$ mod 7 gives $\{3,6,2\}$; $d=5$ mod 9 gives $\{1,6,4\}$; $d=10$ mod 19 gives $\{4\}$ (single point, uninformative).

**Absence of geometric motivation (corrected 2026-06-14).** The modulus 11 = $2\cdot6-1$ was initially accompanied by a claim that $S^{11}$ is the sphere on which $d=6$ spinor harmonics are defined — this is wrong. The $d=6$ sector geometry is $\mathbb{CP}^3$ (real dimension 6); its Hopf fibration is $S^1\to S^7\to\mathbb{CP}^3$, so the associated Hopf sphere is $S^7$ (dimension 7), not $S^{11}$. The sphere $S^{11}=S^{2\cdot5+1}$ is the Hopf total space for $\mathbb{CP}^5$, which belongs to the $d=10$ sector ($\tau$). There is currently no geometric reason for the modulus 11 to be special for the $d=6$ sector.

**Prior probability:** two uniformly random integers in $[1,95]$ agreeing mod 11 occurs with probability $\approx 9/94 \approx 9.6\%$, so the coincidence is not decisive on its own.

**Status:** pure numerical observation (❓). No geometric motivation in hand. Recorded so this specific check is not re-run; do not pursue without a concrete reason why $11$ — rather than $7$ (the Hopf sphere dimension for $\mathbb{CP}^3$) — should appear.

---

### §43. Bott-closure conjecture: $n \equiv 0 \pmod{8}$ as a standing-wave condition for 3rd-generation quarks (2026-06-15)

**Observation.** Among the 15 physical mode indices $\{0,1,3,4,10,13,15,20,22,23,35,72,76,81,95\}$, exactly two non-trivial members satisfy $n \equiv 0 \pmod{8}$:

- $n_{\rm top} = 72 = 9 \times 8$ (up-type quark, $d=4$)
- $k_{\rm bottom} = 16 = 2 \times 8$ (down-type quark resonant site, $d=3$)

Both are 3rd-generation quarks — the heaviest quark of each type. All other physical mode indices have $n \bmod 8 \in \{1,2,3,4,5,6,7\}$ (checked: $n=0$ is the photon ground state and trivially satisfies the condition but is massless and separate). The boson indices $\{76,81,95\}$ have $76 \bmod 8 = 4$, $81 \bmod 8 = 1$, $95 \bmod 8 = 7$.

**Proposed mechanism.** The real Clifford algebra $\mathrm{Cl}(n,0)$ over $\mathbb{R}$ has period 8 in $n$ (Bott periodicity). At $n = 8k$, $\mathrm{Cl}(n) \cong M_{2^{4k}}(\mathbb{R})$ — purely real matrix algebra, the "Majorana point" of the spinor clock where the algebra returns to its simplest (real) type. The conjecture is that a mode at $n = 8k$ constitutes a **closed spinor orbit** in mode-index space: after $k$ complete Clifford clock cycles, the mode's spinor structure returns to its starting type, satisfying a self-consistency / standing-wave condition in the combined sector-$\times$-mode space.

Under this picture, 1st- and 2nd-generation quark modes ($n=1,3,4,20$ for quarks) are open-orbit modes — the Bott clock does not complete — and they are lighter. The 3rd-generation quark resonant sites ($n_{\rm top}=72$, $k_{\rm bottom}=16$) close the clock and are the heaviest. This would give a structural explanation for **generation-3 mass exceptionalism** and a derivation of both $n_{\rm top}=72$ and $k_{\rm bottom}=16$ from the Bott period alone (times respective multipliers 9 and 2, whose ratio $9/2 = N_c^2/2$ awaits explanation).

Note: the Bott clock relevant to the sector spinor type is $d \bmod 8$ (sector dimension). The clock proposed here acts on $n$ (mode index), which would need to be interpreted as the dimension of an effective "mode-occupation space" — the physical motivation for $n$ playing that role is not yet derived.

**Consistency check.** $d=10$ sector: $d \bmod 8 = 2 = $ same as $d=2$ (photon sector). This is the established Bott equivalence of the $\tau$ and $\gamma$ sectors, which gives the same spinor type. The $n$-axis clock ($n_\tau = 23$, $23 \bmod 8 = 7$) is not at a closure point, consistent with the $\tau$ not being a Bott-resonant site under this conjecture.

**Status:** ❓ conjecture (2026-06-15). Positive observation only; no mechanism derived. The key open question is whether IDWT's kernel or spinor EoM gives a physical reason for Bott-period multiples in $n$ to be preferred resonant sites. Pursue before integrating into any Part.

**Addendum (2026-06-15, kernel-mechanism investigation).** Attack on open questions (a)/(c). Results, with honest labels:

1. **Selector is exact (🔵).** Tested $n \equiv 0 \pmod 8$ against the full 16-mode spectrum (not just quarks). It isolates exactly $\{$top$=72$, bottom$=16\}$ with **zero false positives** — no lepton ($n_e=13$, $n_\mu=35$, $n_\tau=23$), neutrino ($10,15,22$), or boson ($76,81,95$) is a non-zero multiple of 8. Among the six quarks the split is clean: down$=1$, up$=3$, strange$=4$, charm$=20$ all have $n\bmod 8 \neq 0$; only the two 3rd-generation quarks close.

2. **Among the quarks, $16$ and $72$ are the only non-$S$-value indices (⭐).** $S(n,d)=16$ and $S(n,d)=72$ have **no solutions** for any $(n,d)$ (checked $d\le 11$, $n\le 200$); the other four quark indices are single hockey-stick values ($1,3,4,20$). **Correction:** being off the single-$S$-image is *not* unique to $16,72$ — the leptons/neutrinos $13,22,23$ and the bosons $76,81,95$ are also not single $S$-values. The distinction is in *how* each is built: those are additive simplex sums and Vandermonde $g$-steps, whereas $16$ and $72$ are products (point 3). That product character — among the quarks — is what is special, and is the structural reason the binomial "T-anchor" restatement (`idwt.py` STEP 1) reaches the top via $T-r+1$ with a $\mathbf{+1}$ offset (🔶): the offset is the residue of forcing a product value out of the additive stick.

3. **Clean closed forms, automatically Bott-closed (⭐).** $16 = n_s^2 = 4^2$ (the bottom beat-site index) and $72 = N_c\,n_s\,N_f = 3\cdot 4\cdot 6$ (already recorded in `idwt.py` STEP 1 as a cross-check). Both are $\equiv 0 \pmod 8$ automatically because $n_s=4$ supplies the even factors ($n_s^2 = 16$; $n_s N_f = 24$). So Bott closure of the two heavy quark indices is a **consequence** of the established product formulas, not an independent input. The multiplier puzzle ($72=9\cdot 8$, $16=2\cdot 8$; ratio $9/2$) dissolves: the products $N_c n_s N_f$ and $n_s^2$ are the primary objects; $9$ and $2$ are just $N_c N_f/(?)$ artifacts of factoring out $8$, not fundamental.

4. **Spinor "Bott clock" mechanism — REFUTED in its stated form (verified 2026-06-15).** The proposed reason for (a) was that a real-spinor Clifford grade advances $\equiv n \pmod 8$ and the real (KO) module returns to type $\mathbb R$ at $n\equiv 0$, admitting a self-conjugate standing wave. This was tested directly. The real division-algebra type of the irreducible Clifford module (Atiyah–Bott–Shapiro; anchors verified computationally — $\mathrm{Cl}_{0,1}\cong\mathbb C$ commutant dim 2, $\mathrm{Cl}_{0,2}\cong\mathbb H$ commutant dim 4) is **real at three residues mod 8, never at one**: $\mathrm{Cl}_{n,0}$ real at $n\bmod 8\in\{0,1,2\}$; $\mathrm{Cl}_{0,n}$ real at $\{0,6,7\}$; Lorentzian Majorana exists at $d\bmod 8\in\{0,1,2,3,4\}$ (the IDWT-accepted convention: $d=5$ no-$C$, $d=10$ MW). Tested against the spectrum, **no spinor reality invariant fires on exactly $\{$top, bottom$\}$**: Cl$_{n,0}$-real also flags down, $\nu_1$, Z; Cl$_{0,n}$-real also flags $\nu_2,\nu_3,\tau$, Higgs; Majorana flags 10 of 15. Only **plain divisibility $8\mid n$** fires on exactly $\{16,72\}$. No period-8 spinor/KO invariant is residue-$0$-unique (KO$^{-n}=\mathbb Z$ at $n\equiv 0,4$; simple-real-matrix type at $n\equiv 0,2$), so the "spinor Bott clock" cannot be the mechanism.

5. **Selector, not generator.** Within the admissible index pool $<100$, **every** multiple of 8 appears: $\{8,16,24,\dots,96\}$. So $8\mid n$ classifies the *actual* physical modes cleanly but is not generative — it cannot pick $16,72$ from the 8-ladder. The specific values are fixed by the product formulas (point 3).

6. **Spectrum partition and additivity diagnostic (2026-06-15, with Fedge).** The spectrum is presented in three tiers by *how* each index is generated. (1) **Lattice** — eleven additively generated modes (photon ground $+$ hockey-stick fermions $\{1,3,4,10,13,15,20,22,23,35\}$), which T0.5 selects; closes with no reference to $16$ or $72$. (2) **Product-form quarks** $\{16,72\}$ — external sites, origin open (the going-forward primary). (3) **Boson $g$-chain** $\{76,81,95\}$ — the same additive $g$-rule seeded by the external top: $76=g(5,72)$, $81=g(6,76)$, $95=g(15,81)$. One additive operation, two starting points (seeds $\to$ lattice, top $\to$ bosons). **Diagnostic:** isolating $72$ as an explicit node lets the chain direction be read off it — the dependents build strictly *upward* ($72\to76\to81\to95$; steps $+4,+5,+14$), so the tower operation is additive, not subtractive. The old T-anchor boson forms were directionally mixed ($T-q,\,T-p,\,T-r+1,\,T+a+1$: three minus, one plus); that sign-incoherence is the signature of bookkeeping, not a mechanism. The top's structural role is thus the entry point of the electroweak chain. Implemented in `idwt.py` STEP 1 (sets `lattice`, `product_form_quarks`, `boson_chain`, with the partition and direction asserts) and Part 9 T0.5.

**Net (revised).** The "Bott closure / spinor clock" framing is **not defensible** and must not be written into any Part — no Clifford/KO reality invariant selects $n\equiv 0\pmod 8$ uniquely; reality type occupies three residues, and the framework's own $d$-clock convention (Majorana at $d\bmod 8\in\{0,1,2,3,4\}$) applied to $n$ would flag most of the spectrum. What survives is arithmetic, and it survives cleanly: (i) among the six quarks, $16$ and $72$ are the **only two that are not single $S(n,d)$ values** (point 2, ⭐); (ii) they have **product closed forms** $16=n_s^2$, $72=N_c n_s N_f$ (point 3, ⭐) — distinct from the additive sums and $g$-steps that build every other index — both divisible by 8 as a *consequence* of $n_s=4$ carrying even factors, so the shared $8\mid n$ is an observation about those factorizations, not a spinor mechanism. The reclassification of $\{16,72\}$ as the two product-form quark sites (and dropping the T-anchor + the top/Higgs $+1$ offsets in favour of the product forms) is therefore justified on arithmetic grounds **without** any Bott claim. Recommend: write up the arithmetic reframe; drop "Bott" as a mechanism, demote to at most a footnote observation that both indices are $\equiv 0\pmod 8$. Decision left to Fedge.

**Addendum 2 (2026-06-15): parametric/product read of the sites — tested; the teardown was mostly WRONG and is reversed (Fedge pushback, same day).** An initial pass attacked a strawman (on-shell *additive* three-wave mixing of carriers $=\chi(\mathbb{CP}^k)$, $\{d2,d4,d6,d10\}\to\{2,3,4,6\}$) and claimed five "breaks." The computations stand; four of the five interpretations do not. (1) **Non-uniqueness, not refutation:** products of $\{2,3,4,6\}$ (2–4 factors) give 13 values in $[10,100]$ incl. $16,72$ — so "is a product" is an *incomplete* selector, not a wrong mechanism (most real rules are "product AND …"). (2) **Layer error [retracted]:** the claim "the bottom ($d=3$) can't contain its own sector since $\chi(S^3)=0$" imports the **post-prism sector assignment** into the pre-prism integer game. Sectors are assigned late (the prism is late in the chain); when working the index arithmetic, sectors must be ignored. Objection void. (3) **"Additive only" is too strong:** the framework already carries a *multiplicative* ladder $S(n,d{+}1)=S(n,d)\,(n+d)/(d+1)$ (§18) and the prism is itself multiplicative, so a multiplicative index-combination is not foreign pre-prism. The genuine open question (not a break): does a pre-prism multiplicative operation land on $16,72$? (4) **Two laws is fine [retracted]:** top and bottom are *already* two different misfits — top is a tower index carrying the GTC correction $(1-\varepsilon)^{10}$, bottom is a beat resonance $\sqrt{S(16,3)S(17,3)}$ carrying **no** GTC — so demanding one unified law fit both is unmotivated; their already-different treatment makes two distinct operations the natural expectation. (Optics aside: SHG $\omega+\omega$ and SFG $\omega_1+\omega_2$ are one $\chi^{(2)}$ nonlinearity, degenerate vs not.) (5) **Not a falsification:** the set also hits $81$ (Z) and $4$ (strange), but those are real modes with their own derivations, so reaching them adds no false positive. **Net:** only the strawman (additive $\chi$-carrier mixing) is excluded. The product/joint-count idea for $\{16,72\}$ is **OPEN**. Correct framing for the tier-2 origin: **sector-free, pre-prism** — is there a multiplicative combination in the integer game (possibly two different ones, matching the two different corrections) producing $16$ and $72$? Reading that survives: $72=N_c\,n_s\,N_f$ and $16=n_s^2$ as joint internal counts (colour $\times$ flavour $\times$ seed) — the same *kind* of object as $S(n,d)$ (a count) but over internal quantum numbers rather than spatial directions. (Computations verified inline 2026-06-15; verdict corrected after Fedge pushback.)

**Addendum 3 (2026-06-15): multiplicative test, sector-free / pre-prism (Fedge framing; landing on real modes counts as free).** Findings. (a) $16 = n_s^2 = 4\cdot 4$, and since $4$ is the strange index, $16 = (\text{strange})^2$ — a **within-down-type self-square** (strange and bottom are both $d=3$ down quarks). Cleanest single relation found. (b) $72 = N_c\,n_s\,N_f = 3\cdot4\cdot6$, reachable only with $N_f=6$, which is a flavour **count**, not a particle mode; $72$ has no factoring into particle modes at all. So the two heavy quarks differ in kind even multiplicatively — a mode self-square vs a count-triple — consistent with the two distinct corrections they already carry. (c) **Obstruction (unchanged shape):** free multiplication of $\{3,4,6\}$ sprays non-particles — products $\le100$ include $9,12,18,24,27,36,48,54,64,96$, none of which are modes. So "is a product" overgenerates $\sim10$ spurious states even granting all real-mode hits as free; a constraint on **which** products is still missing — the same selection gap as before, now in multiplicative form. (d) Tentative (fit-to-answer, not derived) distinguisher: $72$ uses each of the three counts once, $16$ is the **composite** seed squared; the spurious products are partial/pairwise or the **primitive**-seed square ($9=n_u^2$). Both physical products share the factor $n_s$. Lead worth a dedicated look: the $16=(\text{strange})^2$ within-family square; no analogous clean within-up-type relation found for $72$ from $\{n_u=3,\ \text{charm}=20\}$.

**Category objection (Fedge, 06-15) — demotes the counts reading.** A product of internal-label cardinalities (colours $\times$ flavours $\times$ seed) is the *size of a label set*, not a *frequency*. A mode index is an overtone / which-harmonic; nothing turns a static count of properties into a resonant overtone. So $72=N_c n_s N_f$ is an arithmetic identity (⭐ at most), **not** a physical origin — it fails the framework's physical-motivation bar (a manipulation that only reproduces a number is not a result). **Redirect:** seek a *dynamical / frequency-domain* origin. The bottom already has one — it is a quartic bifurcation / beat at $d=3$ occupation $16$ ($m_b=\sqrt{S(16,3)\,S(17,3)}$, Part 7 §1.3b), so $16=n_s^2$ is merely the **address** of a dynamical event, not its cause. The top has no analogous story; the real tier-2 problem is to find the $d=4$ dynamical event (bifurcation / beat / instability) that lands at $72$. If the counts reappear, they must describe that event's structure (e.g. a bifurcation order/multiplicity), not stand as a static count promoted to a frequency.

**Resolution — the additive/multiplicative split IS the linear/nonlinear split of the wave (Fedge, 06-15).** "How does addition become a frequency?" — because pre-prism the world is a common-$\omega$ harmonic ladder, so the overtone index counts units of $\omega$ and index-addition $n_i+n_j=n_k+n_l$ **is** frequency addition: sum-frequency / four-wave mixing (STEP 85). You *do* add frequencies — SFG ($\omega_1+\omega_2\to\omega_3$) and SHG ($\omega+\omega\to2\omega$) are the most ordinary nonlinear-optics processes. So the additive tower is the **linear resonance ladder**. What is *not* physical is multiplying frequencies (dimensionally $\omega^2$). So the multiplication in $\{16,72\}$ cannot be frequency$\times$frequency — but it need not be: it is **amplitude$\times$amplitude**, the nonlinear coupling. The kernel $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ is itself a product, and the bottom's geometric-mean beat $m_b=\sqrt{S(16,3)\,S(17,3)}$ is literally an amplitude product from the quartic density–density coupling. So the clean reading: the **additive tower = linear (frequency-sum) resonances**; the two product quarks = **nonlinear (amplitude-product) coupling sites** — beats/bifurcations, which the bottom already exemplifies. $\{16,72\}$ are not count-products; they are the wave's quartic-coupling addresses. Tier-2 problem, sharpened: find the $d=4$ quartic/beat event that lands the top at $72$ (the bottom's $d=3$ analogue is solved). Distinguish three multiplications: count$\times$scale (the prism, units), amplitude$\times$amplitude (nonlinear coupling — this is the right one for $16,72$), count$\times$count (tensor/joint space — the demoted "counts" reading).

### §44. Gegenbauer criticality at IDWT sectors recovers down-quark generation indices (2026-06-15, Opus)

**Setup.** The existing T5 analysis (`idwt.py` STEP 26; Part 9 §T5) uses the Gegenbauer coupling coefficient

$$b_{k_0}(d) = \frac{\sqrt{k_0(k_0 + d - 1)}}{2k_0 + d - 2}$$

with the resonance site fixed at $k_0 = n_s^2 = 16$ and asks: at which sector $d$ does $b = \tfrac{1}{2}$ (the extended/localised boundary)? The unique answer is $d = 10$, via the integer condition $4k_0 = (d-2)^2$, which terminates the sector chain.

**Observation.** Reversing the question — holding $d$ fixed and solving $4k_0 = (d-2)^2$ for $k_0$ — gives one critical $k_0$ per even sector:

| IDWT sector $d$ | critical $k_0 = \bigl(\tfrac{d-2}{2}\bigr)^2$ | IDWT identity |
|---|---|---|
| $d = 4$ (CP², up-type quarks) | $k_0 = 1$ | $= n_{\text{down}}$ |
| $d = 6$ (CP³, electron) | $k_0 = 4$ | $= n_s = n_{\text{strange}}$ |
| $d = 10$ (CP⁵, tau/terminal) | $k_0 = 16$ | $= n_s^2 = $ bottom beat index |

The critical $k_0$ values at the three active even IDWT sectors are exactly the down-quark generation indices: $1, 4, 16 = n_s^0, n_s^1, n_s^2$. The same geometric sequence with ratio $n_s$ that appears as the down-quark mode indices in $d=3$ also emerges as the Gegenbauer critical endpoints of $d = 4, 6, 10$ respectively. Note that $d = 8$ (critical $k_0 = 9$) is not an active IDWT sector, so the correspondence is exact on the active set.

The connection to the bottom quark: the bottom uses $k_0 = 16$ as the beat index in $d = 3$ precisely because $16$ is the $d = 10$ Gegenbauer critical endpoint (the terminal sector's resonance site). The bottom sits at the top of the $d = 3$ generation tower and "inherits" the global Gegenbauer boundary.

**Status:** ⭐ structural identity. The coincidence $\bigl(\tfrac{d-2}{2}\bigr)^2 = n_{\text{down-gen}}$ at IDWT sectors is exact and arithmetically forced once $n_s = 4$ is given (since the down-quark indices are $n_s^0, n_s^1, n_s^2$ and the critical $k_0$ sequence is $1^2, 2^2, 4^2 = (n_s/2)^{2\cdot0}, (n_s/2)^{2\cdot 1}, (n_s/2)^{2\cdot 2}$ evaluated at $d = 4, 6, 10$). No dynamical claim.

**Implication for the top (null result).** The observation does not deliver a beat index for the top quark in $d = 4$. The $d = 4$-specific Gegenbauer critical $k_0 = 1$ gives a beat mass $\sqrt{S(1,4)\,S(2,4)}\times m_{\text{scale},4} \approx 0.32$ MeV — trivially small. Applying the global resonance $k_0 = 16$ to the $d = 4$ sector gives $\sqrt{S(16,4)\,S(17,4)}\times m_{\text{scale},4} \approx 629$ MeV — not the top. The index $k_0 = 72$ satisfies $4\times72 = 288 = (d-2)^2$ only at $d = 2 + \sqrt{288} \approx 18.97$, not an integer, so $72$ has no Gegenbauer criticality at any active sector. The $d = 4$ sector is supercritical ($b > \tfrac{1}{2}$) for all $k_0 > 1$ and approaches $\tfrac{1}{2}$ only asymptotically as $k_0 \to \infty$ — there is no large interior Gegenbauer endpoint in $d = 4$ analogous to $k_0 = 16$ at $d = 10$. The Gegenbauer route is therefore closed for the top; the beat/bifurcation mechanism for the top in $d = 4$, if it exists, must come from a different condition.

### §45. The up-quark sites as a second criticality branch $(d-1)(d-2)$ on the Kähler hosts, and the GTC exponent revision (2026-06-15, Opus)

**Setup.** §44 fixed the down-quark generation sites as the Gegenbauer (sphere) critical endpoints $(d-2)^2/4$ evaluated at the Kähler matter sectors $d\in\{4,6,10\}$: this gives $\{1,4,16\}$ exactly, the down-type indices, with the third-generation site $16$ inherited from the terminal sector $d=10$. The open question it left was the origin of the up-type sites $\{n_{\rm up}=3,\ n_{\rm charm}=20,\ n_{\rm top}=72\}$, and in particular a *dynamical* (criticality / bifurcation) address for the top's $72$ to replace the static count $72=N_c\,n_s\,N_f$ (demoted by the category objection in §43: a product of label cardinalities is not a frequency).

**Observation (site parallel).** Writing $\lambda=(d-2)/2$ (the Gegenbauer index of the down branch, with down site $=\lambda^2$), the up-type heavy-quark sites are the parallel quantity $2\lambda(2\lambda+1)=(d-1)(d-2)$ at the *same* host sectors:

| host $d$ | down site $(d-2)^2/4$ | up site $(d-1)(d-2)$ | IDWT |
|---|---|---|---|
| $d=4$ (CP², gen 1) | $1$ | $6$ | down $1$ / up $3=6/2$ (seed) |
| $d=6$ (CP³, gen 2) | $4$ | $20$ | strange $4$ / **charm $20$** |
| $d=10$ (CP⁵, gen 3) | $16$ | $72$ | bottom $16$ / **top $72$** |

Generations 2 and 3 match exactly: $20=(6{-}1)(6{-}2)$ and $72=(10{-}1)(10{-}2)$. The ratio up/down $=4(d-1)/(d-2)$ gives $5$ at $d=6$ and $4.5$ at $d=10$, reproducing $n_{\rm charm}/n_{\rm strange}=20/4=5$ and $n_{\rm top}/n_{\rm bottom\,site}=72/16=4.5$. Under this reading the heaviest quark of *each* type would inherit its site from the terminal sector $d=10$, with the generation index mapping to the host Kähler sector $\{4,6,10\}$.

**Correction — this does NOT source $72$; it re-spells it (Fedge's challenge, 06-15).** The "Observation" above is circular as a derivation of the site. $20$ and $72$ are the *accepted tier-2 inputs* ($n_{\rm charm}=20$, $n_{\rm top}=72=N_c\,n_s\,N_f$, STEP 1); the formula $(d-1)(d-2)$ was reverse-engineered to pass through $\{(6,20),(10,72)\}$. Evaluating it at $d=10$ therefore cannot *predict* $72$ — $72$ was used to *find* the formula. The reframe gives $72$ no origin it did not already have; it remains an input, exactly as §43 tier-2 had settled. The asymmetry with the down branch is the whole point: there the site $16$ is the critical endpoint of an *independently defined, derived* object — the Gegenbauer coupling coefficient $b_{k_0}(d)$ (STEP 26) genuinely equals $\tfrac12$ at $d=10$ when $k_0=16$, so $16$ falls out of a spectral condition. The up branch has **no such coefficient**: $(d-1)(d-2)$ is asserted by the fit, not obtained from a Kähler/Jacobi coupling coefficient. Until such a coefficient is written down and shown to cross its threshold at $(d-1)(d-2)$, the "parallel" is cosmetic and $(d-1)(d-2)|_{d=10}=72$ is an identity, not a derivation. Status of the site reframe: **❓** (downgraded from 🔶) — a pointer toward where a Kähler criticality might live, not a result. What survives is *conditional on the input $72$*: the GTC $k$-value result below constrains the top's correction *given* its site and excludes the stale $\{0,3,10\}$; it makes no claim about where $72$ comes from.

**Mass test — the GTC exponents are physical $k$-values (phase load per up-type quark), determined by the derived scale, not fitted.** The correction is $m=S(n,4)\,m_{\text{scale},4}\,(1-\varepsilon)^{k}$, $\varepsilon=1/(280\sqrt7)$, with $k$ the accumulated $l=2$ phase load (up $k=0$). The current assignment $k\in\{0,3,10\}=\{0,n_{\rm up},n_{\nu_1}\}$ carries the "generation depth" reading whose top justification is stale. The corrected $k$-values are **$\{0,7,16\}$**, and these are *fixed by the derived $m_{\text{scale},4}$ and $\varepsilon$*, not chosen to match PDG:

For each candidate integer $k$, charm and top each imply the $m_{\text{scale},4}$ they would require to land on PDG 2024. Only at $(k_{\rm charm},k_{\rm top})=(7,16)$ does the implied scale equal the *independently derived* $m_{\text{scale},4}=0.145102$ MeV for both simultaneously — charm$\to0.145126$, top$\to0.145082$ (agreeing with the derived value to $0.02\%$). The current $(3,10)$ implies $0.144344$ (charm) and $0.143911$ (top): $\sim1\%$ below the derived scale and mutually inconsistent by $0.3\%$. So $(7,16)$ is selected by self-consistency with the derived scale; no other integer pair (e.g. $(6,15)$, $(8,17)$) reproduces the derived scale from both quarks.

- top, $k=16$: $S(72,4)\,m_4(1-\varepsilon)^{16}=172{,}594$ MeV vs PDG $172{,}570\pm290$ → $+0.08\sigma$. (Current $k=10$: $173{,}999$ MeV, $+4.9\sigma$.)
- charm, $k=7$: $S(20,4)\,m_4(1-\varepsilon)^{7}=1272.8$ MeV vs PDG $1273.0\pm4.6$ → $-0.05\sigma$. (Current $k=3$: $1279.7$ MeV, $+1.45\sigma$.)
- up, $k=0$: unchanged, $S(3,4)\,m_4=2.18$ MeV.

**$k$-value identities.** $k_{\rm charm}=7=n_s+n_{\rm up}$ (the argument of the universal $\sqrt7$); $k_{\rm top}=16=n_s^2=k_0$, the resonance site $=$ the down-gen-3 (bottom) site $=$ the $d=10$ Gegenbauer endpoint. Unified phase-load rule $k=g(g+2n_{\rm up})=(g+n_{\rm up})^2-n_{\rm up}^2$ in the generation index $g\in\{0,1,2\}$: a monic zero-constant quadratic $k=g^2+bg$ returns the same $b=6=2n_{\rm up}$ from charm ($g{=}1$) and top ($g{=}2$) independently. (At $n_s=4$ the rule's $g{=}2$ value $g(g+2n_{\rm up})=16$ coincides with $k_0=n_s^2$, since $4n_s=n_s^2$ at $n_s=4$ — the two readings of $k_{\rm top}$ agree.)

**Top as a resummed correction at the critical endpoint.** Because $\varepsilon=g_{\rm coeff}/(k_0\,n_\mu)$ with $g_{\rm coeff}=2/\sqrt7$, $k_0=16$, $n_\mu=S(n_s,4)=35$, the top's $k=k_0$ correction is $(1-\varepsilon)^{k_0}=(1-g_{\rm coeff}/(k_0 n_\mu))^{k_0}\approx\exp(-g_{\rm coeff}/n_\mu)$. The resummed form $\exp(-g_{\rm coeff}/n_\mu)=\exp(-2/(35\sqrt7))=0.978634$ has **no free exponent** (both $g_{\rm coeff}$ and $n_\mu$ are derived) and gives $172{,}597$ MeV ($+0.09\sigma$) — agreeing with $(1-\varepsilon)^{16}$ to $0.1$ MeV. This mirrors the $\tau$ at the same $d=10$ critical endpoint, where the divergent series resums to $1+1/1680$; the top, inheriting the $d=10$ endpoint as its site, takes the analogous all-orders form rather than a truncated power.

**Top is not a $d=4$ beat (control).** The bottom's mechanism (a beat $\sqrt{S(k_0,3)S(k_0{+}1,3)}$ at its site) does not transfer: $\sqrt{S(71,4)S(72,4)}\,m_4=171{,}597$ MeV ($-3.35\sigma$) and $\sqrt{S(72,4)S(73,4)}\,m_4=181{,}198$ MeV ($+30\sigma$). The $d=4$ rungs grow too fast for an adjacent-site geometric mean to land the top; the up-type mechanism is the rung with the multiplicative $(1-\varepsilon)^k$ shift, not a beat. (The bottom beat control reproduces $4181$ MeV, $-0.29\sigma$, as expected.)

**Status and what is open.**
- The site parallel is **🔶**, weaker than the down branch (§44 is ⭐, three-point exact). The up branch matches generations 2–3 ($20,72$) but gen 1 needs the seed exception ($(d-1)(d-2)=6$ at $d=4$, vs $n_{\rm up}=3=6/2$; $n_{\rm up}=3$ has its own anchor $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)=N_c$). As a bare two-point fit $(d-1)(d-2)$ is not unique (a one-parameter family of quarter-integer quadratics passes through $(6,20),(10,72)$); its weight comes entirely from the parallel to the verified down branch on the same hosts and the shared terminal-sector inheritance.
- The $k$-value revision $\{0,7,16\}$ is **🔵**: the integers are determined by self-consistency with the derived $m_{\text{scale},4}$ and $\varepsilon$ (not fitted to PDG), each has a closed identity ($n_s+n_{\rm up}$; $n_s^2=k_0$), and the unified rule $k=g(g+2n_{\rm up})$ is consistent across both heavy up quarks. What remains **🔶** is the *derivation* of the phase-load rule from the kernel's $l=2$ accumulation — why generation $g$ loads $g(g+2n_{\rm up})$ steps, and (cleaner) why the top resums to $\exp(-g_{\rm coeff}/n_\mu)$ at the $d=10$ endpoint. The current $\{0,3,10\}$ is excluded: it cannot reproduce the derived scale from charm and top simultaneously.
- **Candidate mechanism for the factor $\sim4$** (up site $/$ down site $=4(d-1)/(d-2)\to4$): the Kähler hosts $\mathbb{CP}^m$ carry only the class-1 $(k,k)$ harmonics — the holomorphic quotient suppresses odd degrees, so the effective angular step is doubled relative to the sphere $S^d$. A doubled angular index enters the centrifugal/criticality quantity squared, $\sim4\times$. This is a plausibility argument, not a derivation; the Jacobi/$\mathbb{CP}^m$ analogue of the Gegenbauer coupling coefficient $b_{k_0}(d)$ and its endpoint condition have not been written down.

**Not yet propagated.** This is a structural fork (it changes the top's origin story and the up-type GTC exponents, touching the standing CLAUDE.md rule $k\in\{0,3,10\}$, `idwt.py` STEP 4, and the charm input to the $D$-meson masses in STEP 7a). Recorded here only; `idwt.py`/Part edits await Fedge.
