Also $71=n_W-n_s=72-1$. Economy: mode-$72{+}$GTC needs a big downward $-2.15\%$ correction (the fitted $(1-\epsilon)^{16}$); the $71$–$72$ beat needs only a small upward $+0.57\%$ residual. HONEST CAVEATS: (i) the beat is $-0.56\%=-3.4\sigma$ — NOT as clean as the bottom's near-exact beat, so a residual remains (the GTC-corrected single mode still fits better at $+0.08\sigma$); the reframe trades a big structural-but-fitted correction for a small unexplained residual, it does not yet close the gap. (ii) $71$ is prime and off-$S$ (like $16$ and $72$), so it is not a single mode count; its clean form is $S(n_e,2)-n_{\rm charm}$. (iii) $72$ stays relevant as the upper beat mode and the boson-chain seed ($n_W=g(5,72)=76$). NET (genuine progress, Fedge-prompted): the top is structurally a beat like the bottom (lower site $+$ beat to neighbour), the site is $71$ with NO offset, and "$72$" is the upper partner that happens to also equal $N_c n_s N_f$. This reframes the derivation target from $72$ to the $71$-site (clean form $S(n_e,2)-n_{\rm charm}$) and the small beat residual. STRUCTURAL FORK for Fedge: adopt the $71$-site beat reading (parallel to the bottom, no $+1$, small residual) vs keep mode-$72{+}$GTC (better $\sigma$, bigger fitted correction). Reported, not yet written to the Parts.

**Attempt 15 CORRECTION (Fedge: "71 got marked off as bad, correct?") — yes; the reframe does NOT buy a clean win.** The $71$–$72$ geometric-mean beat ($171{,}597$ MeV, $-3.4\sigma$) was already evaluated and rejected as a "no hit" — both in the standing todo (down/up structure item: "geometric mean of (71,72) bracket $=171{,}597$ MeV, 3.4σ below PDG. No hit") and in this session's own $P$-fold beat scan (§15 all-sector entry, $P{=}2$ centre-71 $=-3.4\sigma$). So the $71$-site reading rests on a fit the framework had already discarded. HONEST NET on "what does $71$ buy for the $+1$ issue": it dissolves the top's $+1$ *only inside the binomial restatement* ($T{-}r{+}1\to T{-}r=71$, with $72=71{+}1$ as the beat's upper mode), and it does NOT touch the Higgs ($T{+}a{+}1$) or tau ($p{+}q{-}a{+}1$) $+1$ offsets — both are genuine SINGLE modes (Higgs mode-95 $+0.01\%$, tau mode-23 $-0.06\%$; their would-be beats are $-1.0\%$ and $-17\%$, decisively not beats). But the cost is that the $+1$ it removes reappears as the $-3.4\sigma$ beat shortfall needing a $+0.57\%$ correction — i.e. it RELOCATES the top's fudge ($+1$ in the restatement) into a worse-fitting residual, rather than removing a correction. The GTC-corrected single mode $72$ still fits far better ($+0.08\sigma$ vs $-3.4\sigma$). VERDICT: the $71$-site beat is a cleaner *story* for the binomial $+1$ but an already-rejected *fit*; it does not reduce the top's irreducible need for a correction and is not an improvement on the mass. Do-not-re-adopt $71$-as-site as a mass mechanism (it is the $-3.4\sigma$ no-hit). The genuine residue stands: top needs a real correction; $72=N_c n_s N_f$ remains the working index; its selection mechanism is still open.

**REJECTED (Fedge, 2026-06-16) — do NOT pursue the $71$-site reframe.** Verdict after working it through: net negative. (1) It "fixes" a $+1$ that was never in the primary derivation — $72=N_c n_s N_f$ carries no offset; the $+1$ ($T{-}r{+}1$) exists ONLY in the optional binomial/anchor restatement, so it is a cosmetic artifact of a re-spelling we are not obliged to use, not a fudge needing a cure. (2) The cost is real: it trades the one *meaningful* form of the top index — $N_c n_s N_f$ = colour $\times$ seed $\times$ flavour — for $71$, which is prime, off-$S$, has no product form, and is "clean" only as the single binomial expression $S(n_e,2)-n_{\rm charm}$. So it makes the index LESS meaningful, not more. (3) It does not even improve the fit (the bare $71$–$72$ beat is $-3.4\sigma$, worse than mode-$72{+}$GTC at $+0.08\sigma$), and it cleans only the top's $+1$ — the Higgs and tau $+1$'s are genuine single-mode offsets (verified: neither is a beat) and are untouched. STANDING POSITION RESTORED: $n_{\rm top}=72=N_c n_s N_f$ is the top index (meaningful seed product, tier-2 🔶, GTC-corrected, resonance origin open); the binomial $+1$ is a harmless restatement artifact, not a problem. Do-not-re-chase: the $71$-site / beat-anchor reframe (explored, net-negative, rejected). The attempt-12 cross-sector-resonance *mechanism class* (bottom proven) remains the only live physical lead for the top; the index-factoring detours (attempts 4–15) found no cheap win.

**Attempt 16 — TEST the cross-sector resonance mechanism (the last live lead) by direct computation: it IS the down-type mechanism and does NOT extend to the top (clean negative, mechanism confirmed for down only).** The framework coupling $b_k(d)=\sqrt{k(k{+}d{-}1)}/(2k{+}d{-}2)$ is the single-sector Jacobi-chain off-diagonal; $b<\tfrac12$ subcritical (localized), $b>\tfrac12$ supercritical (extended), the critical site at $b=\tfrac12$ ($4k=(d{-}2)^2$). DOWN: the critical sites of the three Kähler-sector chains $d=\{4,6,10\}$ are $\{1,4,16\}$ EXACTLY $=$ the three down-quark indices. So the down quarks ARE the $b=\tfrac12$ cross-sector resonances — attempt-12's mechanism is confirmed rigorously for the entire down tower (not just the bottom). UP: none of $\{3,20,72\}$ is a $b=\tfrac12$ critical site of any integer-$d$ chain ($4k=(d{-}2)^2$ needs $d=2{+}2\sqrt{k}=5.46,\,10.94,\,18.97$ — all non-integer), and in the host $d=4$ chain the up indices sit at $b\in\{0.530,0.511,0.503\}$ — supercritical, no common critical value. So the top is NOT a $b=\tfrac12$ cross-sector resonance, and the up tower is not produced by the mechanism that produces the down tower. VERDICT: the cross-sector $b=\tfrac12$ resonance is specifically the DOWN-type (real-sphere $S^3$ host) mechanism; the up-type (Kähler $\mathbb{CP}^2$ host) is governed by something else entirely — the $d=4$ chain is supercritical for all $k\ge1$ (CP² always binds), so it has no $b=\tfrac12$ marginal site to select indices, and the up quarks are deeper (supercritical) bound states, not marginal ones. This FALSIFIES attempt-12's hope that the top is the up-analog of the bottom via the same mechanism. **Session bottom line (attempts 1–16):** the down tower is a proven $b=\tfrac12$ cross-sector resonance set $\{1,4,16\}$; the up tower $\{3,20,72\}$ has NO identified resonance mechanism — every route tested (d=4 reps, internal counts, curvature operators, d=10 inheritance, numeric factoring, beat/71-site, cross-sector $b=\tfrac12$) is null or rejected. The top stands as $n_{\rm top}=N_c n_s N_f=72$, a meaningful seed product (colour×seed×flavour) with NO derived resonance origin and a required GTC correction — tier-2 🔶, genuinely open. The asymmetry is the real finding: down quarks are marginal (critical, $b=\tfrac12$) resonances, up quarks are not, and CP²'s everywhere-supercritical chain is why the up-type has no analogous index-selecting criticality.

**ERRATUM ACTIONED (2026-06-16).** The Part 5 §"CKM matrix elements" line that assigned $|V_{ub}|$ via the *leptonic* phase $\delta=\pi+2\theta_{13}=197.11^\circ$ (mislabelled a "lower bound") is **patently wrong in the IDWT context** (it imports a two-Kähler-sector holonomy into the complex+real quark pair) and has been **removed** per the CLAUDE.md "patently wrong content gets removed" rule. It is replaced by the CP-conserving prefactor $A s_C^3=0.00920$ plus a dated stub/warning pointing here; $|V_{ub}|=A s_C^3\sqrt{\rho^2+\eta^2}$ with the CP factor open.

**5. Derivation begun — localisation of the physical quark CP phase (rigorous; magnitude still blocked).** A rephasing lemma sharpens (and partly corrects) pt 3.

*Lemma (verified).* If every cross-type CKM phase factorises as $\arg V_{ij}=\alpha_i-\beta_j$ (a row phase minus a column phase), the matrix is rephaseable to real and the Jarlskog $J=0$. Numerically: pattern $\alpha_i-\beta_j\Rightarrow J=0$; row-only $\alpha_i\Rightarrow J=0$; a single non-factorisable entry phase $\Rightarrow J\neq0$.

*Consequence (corrects pt 3(i)).* The down-type modes live on $S^3$ (real) and carry **no** phase, so $\beta_j=0$. An up-type *intrinsic* CP² Berry/holomorphic phase depends on the row index $i$ only ($\alpha_i$) and is therefore **also factorisable — rephaseable away — contributing nothing to $J$.** So the physical quark CP phase is **not** the one-sided up-type Berry phase (that earlier framing was too loose). It must be the **non-factorisable, $(i,j)$-joint** phase of the cross-sector overlap $\langle\chi^{\mathbb{CP}^2}_{u_i}\,|\,(\xi_3\!\cdot\!\xi_4)^2\,|\,\chi^{S^3}_{d_j}\rangle$ — the residual phase generated where a holomorphic CP² up-mode is projected onto a real $S^3$ down-mode on the shared $d{=}3$ coordinates. This also gives a structural reason for the *smallness* of quark CP violation: the phase is a holomorphic-vs-real *mismatch* in the overlap, entering only the $O(\lambda^3)$ off-diagonal elements ($V_{ub},V_{td}$), consistent with the tiny measured $J_{\rm CKM}\sim3\times10^{-5}$.

*Objects identified.* Up-type $u,c,t$ ($n=3,20,72$) $=$ holomorphic $\mathcal{O}(k_i)$ sections on CP², $k_i=n_i-1=\{2,19,71\}$; down-type $d,s,b$ $=$ real $S^3$ harmonics; kernel $K=g_{34}(\xi_3\!\cdot\!\xi_4)^2$ on the shared $d{=}3$ coords ($S^3\subset$ the $d{=}3$ subset of CP²).

*Blocker for the magnitude (same as Part 10 §3, 🔶).* Computing $\arg\langle u_i|K|d_j\rangle$ needs the explicit CP² holomorphic mode functions $\chi_{n,4}$ and their restriction to the $S^3$ overlap — the mode-bundle correspondence Part 10 §3 already lists as open. The structural result (lemma + localisation) is rigorous and stands independently; the *magnitude* awaits the mode functions.

**6. Result — the LEADING quark CP phase vanishes by the single-sector-per-type structure (✅ structural; explains why $J_{\rm CKM}$ is tiny).** The lepton CP phase is physical (Part 10) because the charged leptons **span two Kähler sectors** — $e,\mu\in\mathbb{CP}^3$ ($d=6$, $c_1=4$), $\tau\in\mathbb{CP}^5$ ($d=10$, $c_1=6$) — so different generations accumulate *different* spectral flow ($\Delta c_1=2$), a generation-dependent (non-factorisable) phase that survives as $\delta=\pi+2\theta_{13}$. The quark sectors have **no such spread**: all three up-type ($u,c,t$) live in $\mathbb{CP}^2$ ($d=4$, one Kähler sector) and all three down-type ($d,s,b$) live in $S^3$ ($d=3$, one real sector). So the spectral-flow phase of every CKM element $V_{u_i\to d_j}$ is the *same* up-sector-minus-down-sector offset, independent of generation $(i,j)$:
$$\arg V_{ij}^{\rm (spectral)} \;=\; c_1(\mathbb{CP}^2)-c_1(S^3) \;=\; 3-0 \;=\; \text{const}\quad\forall\,(i,j),$$
($c_1(S^3)=0$: the real sphere has no holomorphic line bundle / no Berry flow of its own). A constant phase is a global up-vs-down rephasing, so by the §5 lemma $J_{\rm CKM}^{\rm leading}=0$ — verified numerically ($J=-7\times10^{-21}$). This is the structural reason behind the existing tree-level result $\rho=\eta=0$ (idwt.py STEP 6): not merely "real product-state amplitudes," but **the quark generations do not span multiple sectors, so the holonomy mechanism that generates the leptonic phase is switched off.** The observed nonzero $J_{\rm CKM}\sim3\times10^{-5}$ is therefore necessarily a **subleading** effect — the only remaining source is the non-factorisable holomorphic($\mathbb{CP}^2$)-vs-real($S^3$) overlap mismatch (§5), which sits on the single $O(\lambda^3)$ element $V_{ub}$; a small mismatch phase $\sim0.2$ rad there gives $J\sim2\times10^{-5}$, the right order. **Net:** IDWT structurally explains the CP hierarchy — leptonic CP is an $O(1)$ phase (two-Kähler-sector spread), quark CP is tiny (single sector per type kills the leading phase; only the complex-vs-real overlap mismatch remains). Falsifiable: were quark CP violation $O(1)$ like the leptonic phase, this structure would be wrong. **Status:** leading-order vanishing ✅ (needs only the sector assignments + the §5 rephasing lemma, not the open mode functions); subleading magnitude 🔶 (the $\chi_{n,4}$ construction now determines only the *small* residual $J$, not whether CP violation is large). Scratch: `claude/scratchpad/derive_quark_cp_phase.py`.
